Ijarah — Hire and Lease
intermediate
8 min
Definition of Ijarah: Sale of a Known Benefit for a Known Wage
Defines ijarah and explains its components and conditions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi definition of ijarah and identify the essential elements (benefit, wage) and the condition that both must be known (ma'lum).

Core Idea
Ijarah is not selling a physical object but selling its benefit for a known wage.

In this passage, the commentator opens the Book of Ijarah by explaining its placement after charity and then provides a precise definition: ijarah is the sale of a known benefit for a known wage. This definition establishes the essential nature of the contract as a transfer of usufruct in exchange for compensation, and it introduces the critical condition that both the benefit and the wage must be specified to avoid uncertainty (gharar). Understanding this definition will help you distinguish ijarah from other contracts like gift loans (ariyah) and marriage (nikah).

Guided Path
1
Identify the act being defined
The passage defines ijarah (lease/hire) as a specific type of contract. Recognize that the definition is given in a single phrase: 'sale of a known benefit for a known wage.'
2
Parse the definition into its components
The definition has three key parts: 'sale' (bay'), 'benefit' (manfa'ah), and 'wage' (ujrah). Note that 'sale' is a genus that includes both sale of physical objects and sale of benefits. 'Benefit' excludes sale of physical objects. 'Wage' is the compensation.
3
Understand why 'sale' is used as a genus
By saying 'sale', the author includes ijarah under the broad category of sales, but also excludes contracts that involve transfer of benefit without compensation (like ariyah) or transfer of a right that is not a benefit (like nikah).
In logic, a genus both includes its species and excludes others.
4
Recognize the condition 'known'
The word 'known' (ma'lum) qualifies both the benefit and the wage. This condition is essential for validity. If either is unknown, the contract is invalid due to gharar (uncertainty). The commentator gives an example: hiring a slave with a known wage and unknown food and clothing is not permissible.
5
Distinguish ijarah from similar contracts
Use the components to differentiate: ijarah is a sale of a known benefit for a known wage; ariyah is a gift of benefit without wage; nikah is the transfer of the right to intimacy (bud'), which is not considered a benefit in Hanafi fiqh; and the sale of a physical object is excluded because it involves the corpus, not benefit.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الإجارة
لما فرغ من بيان تمليك الأعيان بغير عوض وهو الهبة شرع في بيان تمليك المنافع بعوض وهو الإجارة، وقدم الأول على الثاني لأن الأعيان مقدمة على المنافع، ولأن الأولى فيها عدم العوض والثانية فيها العوض والعدم مقدم على الوجود ثم لعقد الإجارة مناسبة خاصة بفعل الصدقة من حيث إنهما يقعان لازمين فلذلك أورد كتاب الإجارة متصلاً بفعل الصدقة. وقال صاحب العناية وإنما جمعها إشارة إلى أنها حقيقة وذات أفراد فإن لها نوعين : نوع يرد على الأعيان كاستئجار الدور والأراضي، ونوع يرد على العمل كاستئجار المحترفين للأعمال نحو الخياطة والقصارة .اهـ. وسيبين المؤلف أن المنفعة تارة تصير معلومة ببيان المدة، وتارة تصير معلومة بالتسمية وتارة تصير معلومة بالتعيين والإشارة. ولو قال مصدر المؤلف كتاب الإيجار لكان أولى لأن الذي يعرف هو الإيجار الذي . هو بيع المنافع لا الإجارة التي هي الأجرة. قال رحمه الله تعالى: (هي) بيع منفعة معلومة بإجرة معلومة) فقوله «بيع» جنس يشمل بيع العين والمنفعة وهو وإن كان جنساً كما يكون مدخلاً يكون مخرجاً كما تقرر في المعقولات، فخرج به العارية لأنها تمليك المنافع، والنكاح لأنه تمليك البضع ليس بمنفعة . وخرج بقوله «منفعة» بيع العين وقوله بإجرة معلومة تمام التعريف. ولا يخفى أن بيع باع والمصدر هو المعنى القائم بالذات، وجاز أن يراد به اسم المفعول وهو المبيع، وسواء أريد المصدر أو اسم المفعول لا يصلح ما ذكر تعريفاً للإيجاب لأن الإيجاب والقبول والارتباط غير المعنى المصدري واسم المفعول فهذا تعريف ببعض الخواص، ولو أراد التعريف بالحقيقة لقال : عقد يرد على بيع إلى آخره. واحترز بذكر المعلوم عما إذا اشتمل العقد على بيع معلوم وأجرة معلومة وشيء مجهول بأن استأجر عبداً مائة معلومة بأجرة معلومة وطعامه وكسوته، وهذا لا يجوز للجهالة ؛ كذا في الخلاصة. وإنما لا يصح البيع من غير أن يملك الرقبة ولو ملك المنفعة. قال في الذخيرة وقف على قوم معينين فأجرهم القيم الوقف جاز لأنهم لا حق لهم في الرقبة وإنما حقهم في الغلة فصاروا في حق الرقبة كالأجانب إلا أنه يسقط
Book of Ijarah. When the author finished explaining the ownership of physical objects without compensation, which is gift (hibah), he began explaining the ownership of benefits with compensation, which is ijarah. He placed the first before the second because physical objects take precedence over benefits, and because the first involves no compensation while the second involves compensation, and absence precedes existence. Then the contract of ijarah has a special connection with the act of charity (sadaqah) in that both are binding (lazim), so he placed the Book of Ijarah immediately after the chapter on charity. The author of al-'Inayah said: He only combined them (the types) to indicate that it (ijarah) is a reality with individuals; it has two types: one that applies to physical objects, like renting houses and lands, and one that applies to work, like hiring professionals for tasks such as sewing and laundry – end quote. And the author will explain that the benefit is sometimes made known by specifying the duration, sometimes by naming (the specific benefit), and sometimes by identification and indication. If the author had said 'Book of Ijar' (instead of Ijarah), it would have been more appropriate because what is known is ijar (the contract) which is the sale of benefits, not ijarah which is the wage. The author (may Allah have mercy on him) said: (It is) the sale of a known benefit for a known wage. His saying 'sale' is a genus that includes the sale of a physical object and the sale of a benefit, and although it is a genus, just as it includes, it also excludes, as established in logic. By this, 'ariyah (loan for use) is excluded because it is a transfer of benefit without compensation, and marriage (nikah) because it is the transfer of the right to intimacy (bud') which is not a benefit. And by his saying 'benefit', the sale of a physical object is excluded, and his saying 'for a known wage' completes the definition. It is not hidden that 'sale' (bay') is a verbal noun (masdar) indicating the meaning inherent in the action, and it is permissible to intend the passive participle (mabi') meaning the sold item; whether the verbal noun or the passive participle is intended, what has been mentioned does not serve as a definition of the offer (ijab) because the offer, acceptance, and connection are other than the verbal noun meaning and the passive participle; so this is a definition by some of the properties. If he intended the definition by the essence, he would have said 'a contract that applies to the sale of... etc.' And he guarded by mentioning 'known' against the case where the contract includes a known sale, a known wage, and an unknown thing, such as hiring a slave for a known period with a known wage and his food and clothing – this is not permissible due to ignorance; as in al-Khulasah. And the sale is not valid without owning the corpus (raqabah), even if one owns the benefit. Al-Dhakhirah said: If a waqf is for specific people, and the administrator of the waqf rents it to them, it is permissible because they have no right to the corpus, only to the yield (ghallah), so they are like strangers regarding the corpus, except that it drops...
Source pages p. 3

Commentary
This passage is the opening of the Book of Ijarah (Lease/Hire) in the commentary. The author explains the logical placement of this chapter after the chapter on charity (sadaqah), noting that ijarah involves compensation while charity does not, and that both contracts are binding. He cites al-'Inayah to highlight that ijarah covers two types: renting physical assets (like houses and land) and hiring human labor (like tailors and launderers). The author then gives the definition of ijarah as 'the sale of a known benefit for a known wage'. The commentator expands on each part of this definition. 'Sale' (bay') is a broad genus that encompasses both the sale of physical objects and the sale of benefits, thus excluding 'ariyah (gratuitous loan of a benefit) and nikah (marriage, which involves the right to intimacy, not a benefit). The word 'benefit' (manfa'ah) excludes the sale of physical objects themselves. 'Known wage' (ujrah ma'lumah) is a condition for validity. The commentator notes that the definition is not a definition of the offer (ijab) but of the contract as a whole, and that it is a definition by properties rather than essence. The condition of 'known' prevents contracts that include unknown elements, e.g., hiring a slave with additional indeterminate food and clothing. The passage concludes with a reference from al-Dhakhirah about waqf property: when the beneficiaries are specific persons, the administrator can rent it to them because they only have a right to the yield, not the corpus, but this does not give them ownership rights in the corpus.

Key Terms
الإجارة (al-ijarah): Contract of hiring or leasing; sale of a known benefit for a known wage.
منفعة (manfa'ah): Benefit or usufruct; what is derived from using an asset or service.
أجرة (ujrah): Wage or rent; the compensation paid in exchange for the benefit.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the definition in this passage, what is ijarah?
A) A gift of benefits without compensation.
B) A sale of a known benefit for a known wage.
C) A transfer of ownership of a physical object.
D) A marriage contract for intimacy.

Key Takeaway
Ijarah in Hanafi fiqh is defined as the sale of a known benefit for a known wage, making it a subcategory of sale contracts with the condition that both the benefit and wage are specified to avoid uncertainty.

Ijarah — Hire and Lease
beginner
8 min
Ijarah: Definition, Evidence and Conditions
Introduction to Ijarah with definition, proofs, and conditions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define Ijarah according to the Hanafi school, identify its proofs, and state its essential conditions and pillars.

Core Idea
Ijarah is a sale of known benefits for a known wage, permissible by Quran, Sunnah, and Ijma.

The Book of Ijarah follows the chapter on Hibah because both involve transfer of ownership, but Ijarah adds compensation. In this introduction, the author defines Ijarah, discusses its linguistic nuances, and establishes its proofs and conditions. Understanding this foundation is essential for applying the detailed rules of leasing.

Guided Path
1
Understand the definition
Break down the definition 'sale of a known benefit for a known wage' and identify what each term includes and excludes.
The genus 'sale' excludes lending and marriage; 'benefit' excludes sale of corporeal things.
2
Examine the linguistic debate
Note the dispute about the term 'ijarah' versus 'ijar' – the proper term for the contract is 'ijar' but 'ijarah' is used metonymically.
3
Identify the evidence
List the Quranic verse (Shu’ayb), the hadith about paying wages promptly, and the consensus of the ummah.
The shari'ah of previous prophets is binding when related without criticism.
4
Learn the conditions and pillars
State the three conditions (known wage, known object, known equivalent) and three pillars (offer, acceptance, connection).
Ignorance in any condition invalidates the contract.
5
Apply to examples
Use examples from the text to see how the definition excludes invalid contracts, e.g., hiring for non-intended benefits like tying a horse for show.
Benefits must be customarily intended.

Source Text

بسم الله الرحمن الرحيم
كتاب الإجارة
لما فرغ من بيان تمليك الأعيان بغير عوض وهو الهبة شرع في بيان تمليك المنافع بعوض وهو الإجارة، وقدم الأول على الثاني لأن الأعيان مقدمة على المنافع، ولأن الأولى فيها عدم العوض والثانية فيها العوض والعدم مقدم على الوجود ثم لعقد الإجارة مناسبة خاصة بفعل الصدقة من حيث إنهما يقعان لازمين فلذلك أورد كتاب الإجارة متصلاً بفعل الصدقة. وقال صاحب العناية وإنما جمعها إشارة إلى أنها حقيقة وذات أفراد فإن لها نوعين : نوع يرد على الأعيان كاستئجار الدور والأراضي، ونوع يرد على العمل كاستئجار المحترفين للأعمال نحو الخياطة والقصارة .اهـ. وسيبين المؤلف أن المنفعة تارة تصير معلومة ببيان المدة، وتارة تصير معلومة بالتسمية وتارة تصير معلومة بالتعيين والإشارة. ولو قال مصدر المؤلف كتاب الإيجار لكان أولى لأن الذي يعرف هو الإيجار الذي هو بيع المنافع لا الإجارة التي هي الأجرة. قال رحمه الله تعالى: (هي بيع منفعة معلومة بأجرة معلومة) فقوله «بيع» جنس يشمل بيع العين والمنفعة وهو وإن كان جنساً كما يكون مدخلاً يكون مخرجاً كما تقرر في المعقولات، فخرج به العارية لأنها تمليك المنافع، والنكاح لأنه تمليك البضع ليس بمنفعة . وخرج بقوله «منفعة» بيع العين وقوله بأجرة معلومة تمام التعريف. ولا يخفى أن بيع باع والمصدر هو المعنى القائم بالذات، وجاز أن يراد به اسم المفعول وهو المبيع، وسواء أريد المصدر أو اسم المفعول لا يصلح ما ذكر تعريفاً للإيجاب لأن الإيجاب والقبول والارتباط غير المعنى المصدري واسم المفعول فهذا تعريف ببعض الخواص، ولو أراد التعريف بالحقيقة لقال : عقد يرد على بيع إلى آخره. واحترز بذكر المعلوم عما إذا اشتمل العقد على بيع معلوم وأجرة معلومة وشيء مجهول بأن استأجر عبداً مائة معلومة بأجرة معلومة وطعامه وكسوته، وهذا لا يجوز للجهالة ؛ كذا في الخلاصة. وإنما لا يصح البيع من غير أن يملك الرقبة ولو ملك المنفعة. قال في الذخيرة وقف على قوم معينين فأجرهم القيم الوقف جاز لأنهم لا حق لهم في الرقبة وإنما حقهم في الغلة فصاروا في حق الرقبة كالأجانب إلا أنه يسقط حصة المستأجر لأنه لو أخذ منه يسترد له. وفي القنية : لو أجر القيم نفسه للعمل في الوقف فعمل يستحق الأجرة وبه يفتى ولو عمل من غير عقد يستحق الأجرة وعليه العمل. والكلام في الإجارة في مواضع : الأول في معناها لغة قيل هي بيع المنافع قال العيني وفيه نظر قال قاضي زاده: قولهم الإجارة في اللغة بيع المنافع قال الشارح العيني فيه نظر لأن الإجارة اسم للأجرة وهي ما أعطيت من كراء الأجير كما صرحوا به. قال قاضي زاده : والنظر المذكور وارد لأن المذكور في كتب اللغة إنما هو الإجارة التي هي اسم الأجرة، والذي هو بيع المنافع الإيجار لا الأجرة. قال العيني وتجوز أن تكون الإجارة مصدراً. قال قاضي زاده : ولم يسمع في اللغة أن الإجارة مصدر وفي المضمرات : يقال أجره إذا أعطاه أجرته والأجرة ما يستحق على عمل الخير ولهذا يدعى به يقال آجرك الله وعظم الله أجرك . وفي كتاب العيني: أجره مملوكي وأجره إيجاراً فهو مؤجر وفي الأساس: أجرني داره فاستأجرتها وهو مؤجر ولا يقال مؤاجر فإنه خطأ وقبيح . قال : وليس آجر هذا فاعل بل هو أفعل .اهـ. وأما دليلها من الكتاب فهو قوله تعالى حكاية عن شعيب على أن تاجرني ثماني حجج) [القصص: ٢٧] وشريعة من قبلنا شريعة لنا إذا قصها الله علينا من غير إنكار. ومن السنة قوله عليه الصلاة والسلام أعطوا الأجير أجرته قبل أن يجف عرقه». ومن الإجماع فإن الأمة أجمعت على جوازها. وسبب المشروعية الحاجة لأن كل إنسان لا يجد ما يشتري به العين فجوزت للضرورة. وأما ركنها فهو الإيجاب والقبول والارتباط بينهما. وأما شرط جوازها فثلاثة أشياء : أجر معلوم وعين معلوم وبدل معلوم ومحاسنها دفع الحاجة بقليل المنفعة. وأما الملك حكمها فوقوع في البدلين ساعة فساعة . وأما ألفاظها فتنعقد بلفظين ماضيين أو يعبر بأحدهما عن الماضي والآخر عن المستقبل كقوله أجرتك وأعرتك منفعة داري سنة بكذا. وتنعقد بالتعاطي كما في البيع. وفي التتارخانية : وتنعقد الإجارة بغير لفظ كما لو استأجر داراً سنة فلما انقضت المدة قال ربها للمستأجر فرغها لي اليوم وإلا فعليك كل شهر بألف درهم فتجعل في قدر ما ينقل متاعه بأجرة المثل، فإن سكن شهراً فهي بما قال المالك إلى آخر ما ذكر. وصفتها أنها عقد لازم وفي العناية ويثبت في الإجارة خيار الشرط والرؤية والعيب كما في البيع .اهـ. وأفاد المؤلف أن عقد الأجارة ينعقد بإقامة العين مقام المنفعة ولهذا لو أضاف العقد إلى المنافع فلا تجوز بأن قال أجرتك منافع داري بكذا شهراً وإنما يصح إضافته إلى العين والمراد من المنفعة أن تكون مقصودة من العين فلو استأجر ثياباً ليبسطها ولا يجلس عليها ولا ينام أو دابة ليربطها في داره ويظن الناس أنها له أو ليجعلها أجنبية بين يديه أو آنية يضعها في بيته يتجمل بها ولا يستعملها فالإجارة في جميع ذلك فاسدة، ولا أجرة له لأن هذه المنفعة غير مقصودة ؛ كذا في الخلاصة في الجنس الثالث من الدواب كما في البيع اه.
In the name of Allah, the Most Gracious, the Most Merciful. Book of Ijarah. When [the author] finished explaining the transfer of ownership of corporeal things without compensation, which is Hibah, he began explaining the transfer of ownership of benefits with compensation, which is Ijarah. He placed the first before the second because corporeal things are prior to benefits, and because in the first there is no compensation while in the second there is compensation, and non-existence is prior to existence. Then the contract of Ijarah has a special connection to the act of Sadaqah in that both are binding, therefore he mentioned the Book of Ijarah connected to the act of Sadaqah. The author of al-‘Inayah said: He only combined them to indicate that it (Ijarah) is a reality with individuals, for it has two types: a type that pertains to corporeal things like renting houses and lands, and a type that pertains to work like hiring professionals for tasks such as tailoring and laundering. End quote. And the author will explain that the benefit sometimes becomes known by specifying the duration, sometimes by naming, and sometimes by designation and pointing. If he said the source of the author “Book of Ijar” it would be more appropriate because what is known is Ijar which is the sale of benefits, not Ijarah which is the wage. He, may Allah have mercy on him, said: “It is a sale of a known benefit for a known wage.” So his saying “sale” is a genus that includes the sale of a corporeal thing and a benefit, and although it is a genus, just as it includes, it also excludes, as established in rational sciences. Thus, by it are excluded ‘Ariyah (lending) because it is a transfer of ownership of benefits, and Nikah (marriage) because it is a transfer of ownership of the vulva, which is not a benefit. And by his saying “benefit” is excluded the sale of a corporeal thing. And his saying “for a known wage” completes the definition. It is not hidden that “sale” is a verb, and the infinitive is the meaning subsisting in the essence, and it is permissible to intend by it the passive participle which is the sold object. Whether the infinitive or the passive participle is intended, what has been mentioned is not a definition of Ijab (offer) because Ijab, Qabul (acceptance), and connection are other than the infinitive meaning and the passive participle. So this is a definition by some properties. If he intended the definition by essence, he would have said: “A contract pertaining to a sale…” etc. By mentioning “known”, he guarded against when the contract includes a known sale and a known wage but something unknown, such as hiring a slave for a known one hundred [dirhams] with a known wage and his food and clothing; this is not permissible due to ignorance. This is in al-Khulasa. And the sale is not valid without ownership of the corpus, even if one owns the benefit. It is said in al-Dhakhirah: If a waqf is made for specific people, and the custodian leases it to them, it is permissible because they have no right in the corpus; their right is only in the produce, so they become like outsiders regarding the corpus, except that the lessee’s share is dropped because if taken from him it is returned to him. In al-Qunyah: If the custodian leases himself to work for the waqf and works, he deserves the wage, and this is the fatwa. If he works without a contract, he deserves the wage and must do the work. The discussion about Ijarah is in several places: First, its linguistic meaning. It is said it is the sale of benefits. Al-‘Ayni said: This is debatable. Qadi Zadah said: Their statement “Ijarah in language is the sale of benefits” – the commentator al-‘Ayni said it is debatable because Ijarah is a noun for the wage (ujrah), which is what is given as the hire of the hired worker, as they have stated. Qadi Zadah said: The aforementioned doubt is valid because what is mentioned in language books is only Ijarah which is the noun for the wage, while what is the sale of benefits is Ijar (lease), not Ijarah. Al-‘Ayni said: It is possible that Ijarah is an infinitive. Qadi Zadah said: It has not been heard in language that Ijarah is an infinitive. In al-Mudmarat: It is said “ajarahu” when he gave him his wage, and “ujrah” is what is deserved for a good deed; hence supplication is made with it: “May Allah reward you (Ajrak Allah) and magnify your reward.” In the book of al-‘Ayni: “Ajarahu mamlooki” (He hired my slave) and “Ajarahu ijaaran” (he leased it) so he is “mu’jir”. And in al-Asas: “Ajarani darahu fasta’jartuha” (He leased me his house so I rented it) and he is “mu’jir” (lessor), and it is not said “mu’ajir” for it is erroneous and ugly. He said: This “Ajar” is not “fa’ala” but “af’ala”. End quote. As for its proof from the Book, it is His statement, exalted, narrating from Shu’ayb: “on condition that you hire me for eight years” [al-Qasas:27]. And the shari’ah of those before us is a shari’ah for us if Allah relates it to us without rejection. From the Sunnah is his saying, peace be upon him: “Give the hired worker his wage before his sweat dries.” And from Ijma: the ummah is unanimous on its permissibility. The reason for legislation is need because every person does not find what to buy the corpus with, so it was permitted out of necessity. As for its pillar, it is offer, acceptance, and the connection between them. As for its condition of validity, three things: a known wage, a known object, and a known equivalent. Its virtues are fulfilling need with little benefit. As for the ruling of ownership, it is occurrence in the two compensations moment by moment. As for its expressions, it is concluded with two past-tense verbs or one expressing past and the other expressing future, like saying “I leased to you and lent you the benefit of my house for a year for such-and-such.” And it is concluded by mutual deal (ta’ati) as in sale. In al-Tatarakhaniyyah: Ijarah is concluded without words, such as if someone rents a house for a year, and when the period ends the owner says to the lessee: “Vacate it for me today, otherwise you owe me every month a thousand dirhams,” then it is set in the amount of what he moves his belongings at the like wage; if he resides for a month, it is as the owner said… etc. Its description is that it is a binding contract. In al-‘Inayah: Option of condition, inspection, and defect are established in Ijarah as in sale. End quote. And the author conveyed that the contract of Ijarah is concluded by substituting the corpus for the benefit; therefore if he adds the contract to the benefits, it is not permissible, such as saying “I leased you the benefits of my house for such-and-such a month.” It is only valid to add it to the corpus, with the intention that the benefit is intended from the corpus. So if someone hires clothes to spread them but not to sit on or sleep on, or an animal to tie in his house and people think it is his, or to make it a decoration before him, or vessels to place in his house for adornment without using them, then Ijarah in all that is invalid, and there is no wage for it because this benefit is not intended. This is in al-Khulasa in the third type of animals, as in sale. End.
Source pages p. 3

Commentary
This passage is the introduction to the Book of Ijarah from al-Bahr al-Ra’iq, a commentary on Kanz al-Daqa’iq. It begins by explaining the arrangement of chapters: after Hibah (gift without compensation), Ijarah (lease with compensation) follows because the book moves from simple to complex, from uncompensated to compensated transfers. The author then provides the definition of Ijarah as 'sale of a known benefit for a known wage.' This definition is a genus-species definition: 'sale' is the genus, which excludes loans and marriage (since they involve transfer of ownership but not sale or benefit); 'benefit' excludes sale of corporeal things; 'known wage' ensures that the consideration is specified, avoiding ambiguity. The author discusses linguistic issues: the term 'Ijarah' properly refers to the wage (ujrah), not the contract itself, but it is used metonymically. Proofs for Ijarah are drawn from the Quran (story of Shu’ayb), the Sunnah (hadith about paying the worker before his sweat dries), and Ijma’ (consensus of the ummah). The underlying reason (sabab al-mashru’iyyah) is need: not everyone can buy property, so leasing allows access to benefits. Pillars (arkan) are offer, acceptance, and connection; conditions (shurut) are a known wage, known object, and known equivalent. The contract is concluded by specific verbal expressions or by mutual deal (ta’ati). Options of condition, inspection, and defect are established as in sale. The passage also clarifies that the contract must be attached to the corpus (object), not the benefit directly, and that any benefit not customarily intended (e.g., tying a horse for show) invalidates the contract. This foundational discussion sets the stage for detailed rules in subsequent sections.

Key Terms
إجارة (Ijarah): A contract for the sale of known benefits in exchange for a known wage.
منفعة (Manfa'ah): The benefit or usufruct derived from an object or service, which is the subject matter of Ijarah.
أجرة (Ujrah): The wage or rent paid in exchange for the benefit, which must be known (ma'lumah) at the time of contract.
بيع (Bay'): Used as a genus in the definition of Ijarah, meaning a transfer of ownership (tamlik) for compensation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the definition in this passage, what is excluded by the word 'benefit' (منفعة) in the definition of Ijarah?
A) Sale of a corporeal thing (بيع العين)
B) Marriage (النكاح)
C) Loan (العارية)
D) All of the above

Key Takeaway
Ijarah is a sale of known benefit for known wage, requiring three conditions and three pillars, and is proven by Quran, Sunnah, and Ijma.

Definition and Evidence of Ijarah
Defines ijarah and cites primary evidence

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi legal definition of ijarah, identify its rukn, list its three conditions of validity, and cite its primary evidence from Quran, Sunnah, and Ijma.

Core Idea
Ijarah is a contract on a known benefit for a known wage.

The contract of ijarah (hiring/leasing) is a fundamental transaction in daily life. This passage opens the Book of Ijarah by clarifying its precise linguistic and legal meaning, establishing its permissibility through primary sources, and laying out its essential components and validity conditions. Understanding this foundational material is critical before delving into the detailed rulings of hire contracts.

Guided Path
1
Distinguish linguistic from legal definition
First, identify the linguistic dispute: some say ijarah is the sale of benefits, but the author clarifies that linguistically ijarah is the name for the wage (ujrah), not the sale. The correct legal definition is a contract on a known benefit for a known wage.
2
Identify the rukn (pillar) of ijarah
Locate the statement 'its rukn is offer and acceptance and their connection'. Note that for Hanafis, the rukn is the verbal expression of offer and acceptance linked together.
3
List the three conditions of validity (shurut al-jawaz)
The passage explicitly states three conditions: a known wage (ajr), a known object (ayn), and a known substitute (badal). Understand that these ensure the contract is free from gharar (uncertainty).
4
Examine the evidence (Quran, Sunnah, Ijma)
The author cites the Quranic verse from Shu'ayb (al-Qasas:27), the hadith 'Give the worker his wage before his sweat dries', and the consensus of the ummah. Note the Hanafi principle that earlier shari'as are binding when narrated without disapproval.
5
Understand the hukm (ruling) of ownership
The passage concludes that ownership in ijarah occurs gradually (moment by moment) in both the wage and the benefit. This means during the tenancy period, the hirer owns the benefit incrementally.

Commentary
This passage opens the Book of Ijarah with a linguistic and shar'i definition. The author first addresses a preliminary case: the share of the lessee (hissat al-musta'jir) and a ruling from al-Qunyah about a trustee hiring himself out for waqf work. Then he systematically presents the linguistic meaning of ijarah, noting the disagreement whether it is the sale of benefits or the name for the wage itself, citing al-Ayni and Qadizadah. The correct madhhab position is that ijarah in legal terminology is a contract on a known benefit for a known wage. The passage then provides the three proofs of its permissibility: Quranic verse about Shu'ayb (considered an earlier shari'a that is binding when narrated without censure), the hadith commanding payment of the worker before his sweat dries, and the consensus of the ummah. The reason for legislation is necessity (hajah) as a concession. The rukn of ijarah is offer and acceptance linked together. The conditions of validity (shurut al-jawaz) are three: known wage (ajr), known object (ayn), and known substitute (badal). The merits include fulfilling need with minimal benefit. Finally, the hukm of ownership is that ownership of the wage and benefit occurs gradually over the tenancy period. This is a foundational overview of the contract.

Key Terms
إجارة (ijārah): In this text, ijarah is the name for the contract of hiring, or sometimes the wage itself; the author distinguishes it from 'ijaar (the sale of benefits).
الركن (al-rukn): The integral part (pillar) of the contract: offer (ijab) and acceptance (qabul) with connection.
الأجر (al-ajr): The wage or rent given in exchange for the benefit in ijarah.

Wording and Binding Nature of Ijarah
Explains how ijarah is concluded with words or conduct, and its binding nature.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two methods of concluding ijarah (verbal expression and mutual conduct) and explain its binding nature along with the options that qualify it.

Core Idea
Ijarah is a binding contract formed by words or conduct, with options like sale.

This lesson unpacks the Hanafi ruling on how an ijarah (lease) contract is formed and its legal effect. The passage clarifies that ijarah can be concluded either by explicit verbal expressions or by mutual conduct (ta'ati) without speech, and it is a binding contract (lazim) unless options intervene.

Guided Path
1
Identify methods of conclusion
Read the first part: ijarah is concluded by two past-tense verbs, or one past and one future. Recognize the example given ('ajartuka wa a'tartuka...').
Verbal form is explicit, but note the flexibility in tense.
2
Understand ta'ati
Notice that ijarah can be concluded by mutual dealing (ta'ati) just like sale. This is a key Hanafi position.
Ta'ati means conduct alone suffices without verbal offer/acceptance.
3
Analyze the example from al-Tatarkhaniyyah
Consider the scenario: after a lease ends, the landlord demands vacation or payment. If the tenant stays, ijarah is created by action. This illustrates ta'ati in practice.
The example shows how ijarah can arise from context and conduct.
4
Grasp the binding nature
The passage states ijarah is a binding contract (laazim). However, it immediately mentions three options that provide flexibility.
Binding means no unilateral cancellation, but options can make it revocable.
5
Enumerate the options
From al-Inayah: khiyar al-shart (option of stipulation), khiyar al-ru'yah (option of inspection), and khiyar al-'ayb (option of defect) are established in ijarah as in sale.
These options limit the immediate binding effect.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما ألفاظها فتنعقد بلفظين ماضيين أو يعبر بأحدهما عن الماضي والآخر عن المستقبل كقوله أجرتك وأعرتك منفعة داري سنة بكذا. وتنعقد بالتعاطي كما في البيع. وفي التتارخانية : وتنعقد الإجارة بغير لفظ كما لو استأجر داراً سنة فلما انقضت المدة قال ربها للمستأجر فرغها لي اليوم وإلا فعليك كل شهر بألف درهم فتجعل في قدر ما ينقل متاعه بأجرة المثل، فإن سكن شهراً فهي بما قال المالك إلى آخر ما ذكر. وصفتها أنها عقد لازم وفي العناية ويثبت في الإجارة خيار الشرط والرؤية والعيب كما في البيع .اهـ.
As for its expressions, it is concluded with two past-tense verbs, or by expressing one of them as past and the other as future, such as saying: 'I leased to you and gave you as a gift the benefit of my house for a year for such and such.' It is also concluded by mutual dealings (ta'ati) as in sale. In al-Tatarkhaniyyah: Ijarah is concluded without speech, as if someone leases a house for a year, then when the period ends, the owner says to the lessee: 'Vacate it for me today, otherwise you owe me one thousand dirhams each month'; then it is set according to the amount he transfers his belongings for the equivalent rent. If he stays for a month, it is as the owner said, etc. Its description is that it is a binding contract. In al-Inayah: Option of stipulation, option of inspection, and option of defect are established in ijarah as in sale. End.
Source pages p. 4

Commentary
This passage details the method of concluding ijarah. It can be done with two past-tense verbs like 'ajartuka' (I leased to you) and 'a'tartuka' (I gave you the benefit), or one past and one future. Also, ijarah can be concluded by ta'ati (mutual dealing) without verbal expression, similar to sale. The author cites al-Tatarkhaniyyah for an example: after a lease ends, the landlord demands vacating or payment of a monthly rent; if the tenant stays, it becomes a rental at the stated amount. This shows ijarah can arise from action and context. Ijarah is a binding contract (laazim), meaning neither party can unilaterally rescind without cause. However, the option of stipulation (khiyar al-shart), option of inspection (khiyar al-ru'yah), and option of defect (khiyar al-'ayb) are established in ijarah, as in sale, meaning the contract is not immediately binding if those options are present. This is from al-Inayah.

Key Terms
التعاطي (al-ta'āṭī): Mutual dealing without verbal expression; conduct indicating consent.
عقد لازم (ʿaqd lāzim): A binding contract that cannot be rescinded unilaterally without legal cause.
خيار الشرط (khiyār al-sharṭ): Option of stipulation: right to rescind within a period if agreed in the contract.
خيار الرؤية (khiyār al-ru’yah): Option of inspection: right to rescind if the object does not match description.
خيار العيب (khiyār al-‘ayb): Option of defect: right to rescind if a defect is discovered.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
Ijarah is valid by verbal expression or mutual conduct, and is binding unless an option applies.

Invalid Ijarah for Non-Intended Benefits
States the rule that ijarah must be on the 'ayn and benefit must be intended, with examples of invalid contracts.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify when an ijarah contract is fasid due to the benefit not being the intended purpose, and apply the rule to new scenarios.

Core Idea
Ijarah is fasid if the contracted benefit is not the primary intended use of the object.

The contract of ijarah must be attached to the 'ayn (object), not directly to the manafi' (benefits). More importantly, the benefit must be the intended purpose (manfa'ah maqsudah) of the object. In this lesson, we examine examples where hiring an object for a non-intended benefit renders the contract void (fasid) and no wage is due.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its category
Recognize that we are dealing with ijarah (hire/lease) contracts. The passage gives examples of hiring cloth, an animal, or vessels.
Ijarah is a contract of exchange for a benefit.
2
Identify the hukm level
The passage states that the ijarah in these examples is fasid (void). Understand that fasid means the contract is defective and does not produce its intended effects.
Fasid is distinguished from batil; here the contract is invalid from the start.
3
List the conditions for validity
The passage gives two conditions: (1) the contract must be concluded on the 'ayn, not directly on the manafi'; (2) the benefit must be intended (maqsudah) from that 'ayn.
The benefit must be the primary purpose for which the object is typically used.
4
Note what invalidates the contract
Examples: hiring clothes to spread without sitting/sleeping, hiring an animal to tie as decoration, hiring vessels for adornment. In each case, the benefit is not intended, so the contract fails.
The 'illa (legal cause) is that the benefit is ghayr maqsudah.
5
Derive the 'illa and apply the rule
The underlying reason (talil) is that the consideration (wage) is for a benefit that is not the intended one; hence the contract lacks a valid subject matter.
Apply: for any ijarah, ask if the benefit is the natural intended use of the object.

وأفاد المؤلف أن عقد الأجارة ينعقد بإقامة العين مقام المنفعة ولهذا لو أضاف العقد إلى المنافع فلا تجوز بأن قال أجرتك منافع داري بكذا شهراً وإنما يصح إضافته إلى العين والمراد من المنفعة أن تكون مقصودة من العين فلو استأجر ثياباً ليبسطها ولا يجلس عليها ولا ينام أو دابة ليربطها في داره ويظن الناس أنها له أو ليجعلها أجنبية بين يديه أو آنية يضعها في بيته يتجمل بها ولا يستعملها فالإجارة في جميع ذلك فاسدة، ولا أجرة له لأن هذه المنفعة غير مقصودة ؛ كذا في الخلاصة في الجنس الثالث من الدواب كما في البيع
اه.
And the author informed that the contract of ijarah is concluded by placing the 'ayn in the position of the benefit; hence if he attaches the contract to the benefits, it is not permissible, such as saying: 'I leased to you the benefits of my house for such and such for a month.' Rather, it is valid to attach it to the 'ayn, and the intended meaning of the benefit is that it is intended from the 'ayn. So if he hires clothes to spread them out but does not sit on them or sleep, or an animal to tie it in his house so that people think it is his, or to put it in front of him as a decoration, or vessels to place in his house for adornment without using them, then the ijarah in all that is void (fasid), and he is not entitled to any wage because this benefit is not intended. Such is in al-Khulasah in the third category of animals, as in sale. End.
Source pages p. 4

Commentary
This passage clarifies a key principle: the contract of ijarah must be attached to the 'ayn (the object), not directly to the manfa'ah (benefit). Saying 'I rent you the benefits of my house' is invalid. The benefit must be the intended purpose of the object. The author provides examples of invalid ijarah when the intended benefit is not the natural or customary use: hiring clothes to spread them without sitting or sleeping on them, hiring an animal to tie in the house as a display (people think it's his), hiring a vessel for decoration without use. In all these, the contract is fasid (void), and no wage is due because the benefit is not the intended one (ghayr maqsudah). This is taken from al-Khulasah in the third category of animals, analogous to sale. The underlying 'illa is that the contract is conditional upon the benefit being maqsudah from that 'ayn; if the benefit is merely incidental or not typical, the consideration fails.

Key Terms
منفعة مقصودة (manfaʿah maqṣūdah): A benefit that is the intended purpose of the object; e.g., sitting on a cloth, riding an animal.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
Ijarah is void if the contracted benefit is not the intended purpose of the object; the contract must be on the 'ayn and the benefit must be maqsudah.

Conditions of Ujrah in Ijarah: What Can Be a Valid Wage
Ruling statement with commentary on ujrah specification.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions for valid ujrah in Ijarah and classify different types of ujrah with their specification requirements.

Core Idea
Only what is valid as thaman or a specified 'ayn can be ujrah; specification requirements depend on the type.

This lesson from Bahr al-Raiq explains that ujrah is the price of the benefit, so it follows the rules of thaman. However, there is an asymmetry: some things can be ujrah but not thaman. The passage details the specification requirements for different categories of ujrah and concludes with Abu Yusuf's ruling on how to handle changes in the value of ujrah before possession.

Guided Path
1
Identify the general principle
The passage states: 'what is valid as a price (thaman) is valid as a wage (ujrah)'. Understand that ujrah is considered the price of the benefit, so the same rules apply.
2
Recognize the asymmetry
Note that some things valid as ujrah are not valid as thaman, e.g., benefits themselves, specific unique items like animals. This is because thaman in a sale must be established in the dhimmah, while ujrah can be a specified 'ayn.
3
Classify the types of ujrah
The passage divides ujrah into three categories based on the nature of the item: dirhams/dinars, measured/weighed items, and clothes/goods. Each has specific requirements.
4
List specification requirements for each type
For dirhams/dinars: amount and quality must be specified. For measured/weighed: amount, quality, and place of delivery (if transport cost is involved). For clothes/goods: amount, term, and quality, unless physically pointed to.
5
Handle special cases: fluctuation and obsolescence
The passage cites Abu Yusuf: if the ujrah is a fals (copper coin) and its value changes before possession, the agreed fals remains the ujrah; if it becomes obsolete, the value of the benefit must be paid.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الإجارة
هي بيع
قال
منفعة معلومة بإجرة معلومة وما صح ثمناً صح أجرة والمنفعة تعلم ببيان
رحمه الله : (وما صح ثمناً صح أجرة لأن الأجرة ثمن المنفعة فتعتبر بثمن المبيع، ثم إن كانت الأجرة عيناً جاز أن يكون كل عين بدلاً عن المبيع ولا ينعكس حتى صح أجرة ما لا ثمناً كالمنفعة فإنها لا تصح ثمناً وتصح أجرة إذا كانا مختلفي الجنس كما سيأتي . وفي الجوهرة : لو كان عبد بين اثنين فأجر أحدهما نصيبه من شريكه على أن يخيط معه شهراً على أن يخدم الآخر في الشهر الثاني لم يجز من جهة أن النصيبين في العبد الواحد متفقان في الصفقة، ولو كان في العبدين جاز اهـ. وإن كانت الأجرة دراهم أو دنانير لا بد من بيان القدر والصفة وأنه جيد أو رديء وإن كانت النقود مختلفة انصرفت إلى غالب نقد البلد، وإن كانت الأجرة مكيلاً أو موزوناً يحتاج إلى بيان القدر والصفة ومكان الإيفاء. هذا إذا كان له حمل ومؤنة عند الإمام وإلا فلا يحتاج إلى بيان مكان الإيفاء. وإن كانت ثياباً أو عروضاً فالشرط بيان القدر والأجل الصفة لأنه لا يثبت في الذمة إلا بهذا. هذا إذا لم يكن مشاراً إليه. وفي الهداية وما لا يصلح ثمناً يصلح أجرة أيضاً كالأعيان التي ليست من ذوات الأمثال كالحيوان والثياب مثلاً فإنها إذا كانت معينة تصلح أجرة ولا تصلح ثمناً كما إذا استأجر داراً بثوب معين فإنه لا يصلح ثمناً لما تقرر في كتاب البيوع إذا الأموال ثلاثة : ثمن محض كالدراهم والدنانير ومبيع محض كالأعيان التي ليست من ذوات الأمثال، وما كان بينهما كالمكيل والموزون . قال في العناية وفيه نظر لأن المقايضة بيع وليس فيها إلا العين من الجانبين فإذا لم تصلح العين ثمناً كان بيعاً بلا ثمن وهو باطل وأجيب بأن المراد بالثمن ما ثبت في الذمة وإذا كانت الأجرة فلساً فغلا أو رخص قبل القبض فالأجرة الفلس لا غير، وإن كسدت فعليه قيمة المنفعة؛ كذا عن أبي يوسف وكذا إذا كان الثمن كيلاً أو موزوناً فانقطع عن أيدي الناس .اهـ.
Book of Ijarah. It is the sale of a known benefit for a known wage. And what is valid as a price (thaman) is valid as a wage (ujrah). The benefit is known by specifying (the duration). He (the author) said: 'And what is valid as a price is valid as a wage because the wage is the price of the benefit, so it is considered like the price of the sold item. Then if the wage is an 'ayn (non-fungible), it is permissible for every 'ayn to be a substitute for the sold item, but not vice versa, so that what is not valid as a price is valid as a wage, such as a benefit: it is not valid as a price but is valid as a wage if they are of different types, as will come.' In al-Jawharah: If a slave is owned by two, and one of them leases his share to his partner on condition that he sews with him for a month, and the other serves in the second month, it is not permissible because the two shares in one slave are similar in the transaction; if they were in two slaves, it would be permissible. End. If the wage is dirhams or dinars, it is necessary to specify the amount and quality, and whether it is good or bad. If the currencies are different, it refers to the prevalent currency of the country. If the wage is a measured or weighed item, it requires specification of amount, quality, and place of delivery. This is if it has transportation and cost according to Imam (Abu Hanifa); otherwise, specification of place of delivery is not needed. If it is clothes or goods, the condition is to specify the amount, term, and quality because it is not established in the dhimmah except by that. This is if it is not referred to. In al-Hidayah: And what is not valid as a price is valid as a wage, such as items that are not of the same type like animals and clothes, for if they are specific, they are valid as wage but not as price. For example, if one leases a house for a specific garment, it is not valid as a price as established in the Book of Sales: wealth is of three types: pure price like dirhams and dinars, pure sold item like items that are not of the same type, and what is between them like measured and weighed items. He said in al-Inayah: There is consideration because barter is a sale and involves only 'ayn from both sides; so if the 'ayn is not valid as a price, it would be a sale without a price, which is void. The answer is that what is meant by price is what is established in the dhimmah. And if the wage is a fals (small coin) and it increases or decreases in value before possession, the wage is that fals and nothing else. If it becomes obsolete, he must pay the value of the benefit. This is from Abu Yusuf. Similarly, if the price is measured or weighed and it disappears from the hands of the people. End.
Source pages p. 5

Commentary
This lesson begins with the matn of Kanz al-Daqaiq: 'Ijarah is the sale of a known benefit for a known wage. And what is valid as a price is valid as a wage.' The sharh expands: the wage is the price of the benefit, so it follows the rules of thaman. However, there is an asymmetry: some things valid as wage are not valid as price (e.g., benefits themselves, specific animals). The passage then details requirements for different types of ujrah: for dirhams/dinars: specify quantity and quality; for measured/weighed items: specify quantity, quality, and place of delivery (with a nuance from Abu Hanifa regarding transportation cost); for clothes/goods: specify quantity, term, and quality unless they are physically pointed to. The author also cites al-Hidayah on the three categories of wealth (amwal): pure price (gold and silver), pure sold item (unique items like animals), and intermediate (fungibles). A unique item can be ujrah if specified but cannot be thaman in a conventional sale. A comment from al-Inayah questions this, but answers that 'thaman' here means what is established in the dhimmah. The passage concludes with a ruling from Abu Yusuf: if the ujrah is a fals (copper coin) that changes value before possession, the contracted ujrah stands; if the coin becomes obsolete, the musta'jir must pay the value of the benefit. Same for a commodity that disappears.

Key Terms
ثمن محض (thaman maḥḍ): Pure price: dirhams and dinars (gold and silver currency).
ذوات الأمثال (dhawāt al-amthāl): Fungible items that can be replaced by similars (e.g., measured/weighed).
أجرة (ujrah): Wage or rental payment for a benefit.
فلس (fals): Copper coin, a type of currency with intrinsic value.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is required for ujrah in the form of coins (dirhams/dinars)?
A) Only the amount
B) Amount and quality
C) Amount, quality, and place of delivery
D) Nothing; it is determined by custom

Key Takeaway
The validity of ujrah depends on its type: for each type, specific conditions must be met to avoid gharar, and if the ujrah is a specified item its value fluctuation before possession is irrelevant, but obsolescence requires paying the benefit's value.

Duration of Lease and the Lifespan Dispute
Ruling with proof and intra-Hanafi dispute on lease duration beyond lifespan.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on lease duration and explain the dispute regarding leases extending beyond normal lifespan.

Core Idea
Any known duration makes a lease valid; the lifespan limit is contested but the permissive view is relied upon.

This lesson addresses a key question: can a lease be valid for a period longer than a person's expected life? The Hanafi school holds that as long as the duration is specified, the lease is valid regardless of length. However, a minority disputed this, arguing that a duration beyond normal lifespan introduces uncertainty. We will examine both views and the evidence.

Guided Path
1
State the general rule
The author states that the benefit (manfa'ah) is known by specifying the duration, making the lease valid for any known period.
This applies whether the lease is immediate or delayed (mudafah).
2
Identify the dispute
Some scholars, like al-Qadi Abu 'Ismah, argue that a duration beyond normal life expectancy is invalid because the prevalent (ghalib) is treated as certain.
3
Analyze the opposing proof
The opposing view relies on the principle that al-ghalib ka al-muhaqqaq (the prevalent is like the certain). Hence, exceeding normal lifespan is like impossibility.
4
Examine the Hanafi response
Al-Khassaf and others permit such durations, considering the possibility that the lessor might survive, and the benefit remains known through the specified duration.
The permissibility view is based on istihsan and practicality.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
The relied-upon fatwa is on permissibility, as indicated by the text's presentation and the authority of al-Khassaf.
This allows long-term leases like 99-year agreements.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما إذا كانت حيواناً لا يجوز إلا إذا كان معيناً. قال رحمه الله : والمنفعة تعلم ببيان المدة كالسكنى والزراعة فتصح على مدة معلومة) أي مدة كانت لأن المدة إذا كانت معلومة كانت المنفعة معلومة فيجوز ، طالت المدة أو قصرت أو تأخرت بأن كانت مضافة أو تقدمت بأن كانت متصلة بوقت العقد، ولأن المنافع لا تصير معلومة إلا بضرب المدة. وقال بعضهم : لا يجوز أن يضرب إلى مدة لا يعيش إليها عادة لأن الغالب كالمتحقق في حق الأحكام فصار كالثابت بعد فلا تجوز وبه كان يفتي القاضي أبو عصمة. وبعض العلماء، فيجوز ضرب المدة التي لا يعيش إلى مثلها، ومنهم الخصاف . قال في الخانية : رجل قال لآخر أجرتك دابتي غداً بدرهم ثم أجرها اليوم وغداً وبعد غد من غيره ثلاثة أيام فجاء الغد وأراد المستأجر الأول أن يفسخ الإجارة الثانية اختلف أصحابنا في رواية يفسخ الإجارة أخذ نصير وفي رواية ليس له أن يفسخ وبه أخذ الفقيه أو جعفر والفقيه أو الليث وشمس الأئمة الحلواني وعليه الفتوى، فيستوفي الأول مدته والثاني ما بقي له. وفي الثانية وبه
And as for animal (as ujrah), it is not permissible unless it is specified. He (the author) said: 'And the benefit is known by specifying the duration, like tenancy (sukna) and farming (zira'ah), so it is valid for a known duration' — any duration, because if the duration is known, the benefit is known, so it is permissible, whether the duration is long or short, delayed (mudafah) or immediate (connected to the time of contract). Because benefits are only known by setting a duration. Some said: It is not permissible to set a duration beyond which a person would not normally live, because the prevalent is considered certain in legal rulings, so it becomes as if established, so it is not permissible. This was the fatwa of al-Qadi Abu 'Ismah. And some scholars permit setting a duration that one would not live to see, among them al-Khassaf. In al-Khaniyyah: A man said to another: 'I leased you my animal tomorrow for one dirham,' then he leased it today, tomorrow, and the day after to someone else for three days. When tomorrow came, the first lessee wanted to cancel the second lease. Our companions differed in a narration: he cancels the lease (taken by Nasir), and in another narration: he does not have the right to cancel. This (second) was adopted by al-Faqih Abu Ja'far, al-Faqih Abu al-Layth, and Shams al-A'immah al-Halwani, and the fatwa is upon it. So the first lessee takes his period, and the second takes what remains. In the second narration, and by it.
Source pages p. 5

Commentary
This final lesson covers two topics: duration of ijarah and overlapping leases. First, the author reiterates that the benefit is known through specifying the duration (muddah). Whether the lease is for a long or short term, immediate or starting in the future (mudafah), it is valid as long as the duration is clear. However, there is an ikhtilaf: some scholars, like al-Qadi Abu 'Ismah, hold that a duration beyond a normal human lifespan is invalid because the benefit is uncertain (gharar). Others, like al-Khassaf, permit it, considering that the majority view is that the contract is valid. The relied-upon position is that it is permissible, as the passage implies by presenting both views. Second, the passage presents a case from al-Khaniyyah: a man leases his animal to one person for tomorrow, then leases it to another for today, tomorrow, and the day after. When the first lessee wants to exercise his right for tomorrow, he seeks cancellation of the second lease. There is a textual dispute: according to one narration (from Nasir), he can cancel; according to another, he cannot. The latter is adopted by later authorities (Abu Ja'far, Abu al-Layth, al-Halwani) and is the fatwa. The practical solution: the first lessee takes his agreed day (tomorrow), and the second takes the remaining days (today and the day after tomorrow). This shows the Hanafi method of reconciling overlapping contracts without voiding either completely.

Key Terms
مضافة (muḍāfah): A lease that begins in the future (e.g., 'I lease you from next month').
الغالب كالمتحقق (al-ghālib ka al-muḥaqqaq): A legal maxim meaning the prevalent (what normally happens) is treated as certain in legal rulings.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the text, which Hanafi scholar opposed leases beyond normal lifespan?
A) Al-Khassaf
B) Al-Qadi Abu 'Ismah
C) Al-Faqih Abu Ja'far
D) Shams al-A'immah al-Halwani

Key Takeaway
A lease is valid for any specified duration; the dispute over lifespan is resolved by the permissibility view adopted for fatwa.

Overlapping Leases (Tazahum al-Ijaratayn)
Case from al-Khaniyyah on overlapping leases with intra-Hanafi dispute on cancellation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to resolve a conflict between two overlapping leases on the same object, applying the Hanafi rule that the first lessee takes his period and the second takes the remainder.

Core Idea
When two leases overlap, the first lessee's right is confined to his agreed period, and the second lessee takes the remaining days.

When a lessor leases the same object to two parties for overlapping periods, a conflict arises. This lesson presents a classic case from al-Khaniyyah: a man leases his animal to one person for tomorrow, then leases it to another for three days including tomorrow. The Hanafi scholars debated whether the first lessee can cancel the second lease. The relied-upon solution is that neither lease is void; rather, the first lessee takes his day, and the second takes the remaining days. We will explore the reasoning behind this.

Guided Path
1
Identify the conflicting leases
First lease: animal for tomorrow (one day). Second lease: same animal for today, tomorrow, and the day after (three days). Overlap occurs on tomorrow.
2
State the dispute
When the first lessee wants to exercise his right for tomorrow, he seeks cancellation of the second lease. There are two narrations: one allows cancellation (taken by Nasir), the other does not.
3
Analyze the authorities who adopt non-cancellation
Al-Faqih Abu Ja'far, al-Faqih Abu al-Layth, and Shams al-A'immah al-Halwani adopt the view that the first lessee cannot cancel the second lease.
This view is the basis for the fatwa.
4
Derive the practical resolution
The first lessee takes his period (tomorrow) and the second lessee takes the remaining days (today and the day after tomorrow). Neither lease is void; they coexist.
This is consistent with the principle that each contract is valid for its specified period.
5
Note the fatwa
The fatwa is upon the non-cancellation view, as stated 'وعليه الفتوى'.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما إذا كانت حيواناً لا يجوز إلا إذا كان معيناً. قال رحمه الله : والمنفعة تعلم ببيان المدة كالسكنى والزراعة فتصح على مدة معلومة) أي مدة كانت لأن المدة إذا كانت معلومة كانت المنفعة معلومة فيجوز ، طالت المدة أو قصرت أو تأخرت بأن كانت مضافة أو تقدمت بأن كانت متصلة بوقت العقد، ولأن المنافع لا تصير معلومة إلا بضرب المدة. وقال بعضهم : لا يجوز أن يضرب إلى مدة لا يعيش إليها عادة لأن الغالب كالمتحقق في حق الأحكام فصار كالثابت بعد فلا تجوز وبه كان يفتي القاضي أبو عصمة. وبعض العلماء، فيجوز ضرب المدة التي لا يعيش إلى مثلها، ومنهم الخصاف . قال في الخانية : رجل قال لآخر أجرتك دابتي غداً بدرهم ثم أجرها اليوم وغداً وبعد غد من غيره ثلاثة أيام فجاء الغد وأراد المستأجر الأول أن يفسخ الإجارة الثانية اختلف أصحابنا في رواية يفسخ الإجارة أخذ نصير وفي رواية ليس له أن يفسخ وبه أخذ الفقيه أو جعفر والفقيه أو الليث وشمس الأئمة الحلواني وعليه الفتوى، فيستوفي الأول مدته والثاني ما بقي له. وفي الثانية وبه
And as for animal (as ujrah), it is not permissible unless it is specified. He (the author) said: 'And the benefit is known by specifying the duration, like tenancy (sukna) and farming (zira'ah), so it is valid for a known duration' — any duration, because if the duration is known, the benefit is known, so it is permissible, whether the duration is long or short, delayed (mudafah) or immediate (connected to the time of contract). This was the fatwa of al-Qadi Abu 'Ismah. And some scholars permit setting a duration that one would not live to see, among them al-Khassaf. Key Terms
تزاحم الإجارتين (tazāhum al-ījāratayn): Conflict between two leases on the same object for overlapping periods.
يفسخ (yafsukh): He cancels (the lease).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the text, what is the fatwa regarding the cancellation of the second lease in the overlapping case?
A) The first lessee may cancel the second lease.
B) The second lessee takes priority.

Key Takeaway
When two leases overlap, the first lessee takes his agreed period, and the second takes the remaining days; this is the mufta bihi.

Ijarah — Hire and Lease

Definition of Ijarah and the General Principle of Rent
Opening of Kitab al-Ijarah with definition and principle on rent

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi definition of ijarah and apply the principle that what is valid as price is valid as rent, identifying exceptions for specified non-fungibles.

Core Idea
Ijarah is a sale of benefits; anything valid as a price is valid as rent, except specified non-fungibles which can be rent but not price.

This lesson opens the chapter on ijarah. The author defines ijarah as a contract for the sale of a known benefit for a known rent, then establishes a key principle: whatever can serve as a price in a sale can also serve as rent. The passage explores the scope of this principle, explaining how it applies to different types of assets and discussing important exceptions, including the case where the rent is a specific non-fungible item like an animal or garment.

Guided Path
1
Understand the definition of ijarah
Ijarah is a sale (bay') of a benefit (manfa'ah), not of a physical object. Both the benefit and the rent must be known (ma'lum).
This classification as a sale of benefits is unique to the Hanafi school.
2
Grasp the core analogy between price and rent
The author states 'wa ma saha thamanan saha ujrah' because 'al-ujrah thaman al-manfa'ah'. Rent is the price of the benefit, so by qiyas, any item that can be a valid price (thaman) in a sale can also be a valid rent.
This analogy is a qiyas jaliy, based on the common element of being a substitute in exchange.
3
Examine the exceptions for non-price items
Items that are not valid as price (e.g., specific animals, garments) can still be valid as rent if they are specified ('ayn). The text says 'ma la yasluhu thamanan yasluhu ujratan aydan'.
This is because rent is a substitute for a benefit, and specified items can serve as such.
4
Analyze the conditions for different types of rent
For dirhams/dinars: specify quantity, quality, type. For measured/weighed items: specify quantity, quality, and place of delivery (if transport costs). For garments/wares: specify quantity, quality, and term (ajal).
These conditions ensure the rent is known and avoid gharar.
5
Apply the ruling on change in value and obsolescence
If rent is a fals (copper coin) and its value changes before possession, the rent is that fals. If it becomes obsolete, the value of the benefit must be paid (from Abu Yusuf).
This shows that the rent is established at contract, but if the specified object becomes unusable, liability shifts to market value.

كتاب الإجارة هي بيع منفعة معلومة بإجرة معلومة وما صح ثمناً صح أجرة والمنفعة تعلم ببيان رحمه الله : (وما صح ثمناً صح أجرة لأن الأجرة ثمن المنفعة فتعتبر بثمن المبيع، ثم إن كانت الأجرة عيناً جاز أن يكون كل عين بدلاً عن المبيع ولا ينعكس حتى صح أجرة ما لا ثمناً كالمنفعة فإنها لا تصح ثمناً وتصح أجرة إذا كانا مختلفي الجنس كما سيأتي . يصح وفي الجوهرة : لو كان عبد بين اثنين فأجر أحدهما نصيبه من شريكه على أن يخيط معه شهراً على أن يخدم الآخر في الشهر الثاني لم يجز من جهة أن النصيبين في العبد الواحد متفقان في الصفقة، ولو كان في العبدين جاز اهـ. وإن كانت الأجرة دراهم أو دنانير لا بد من بيان القدر والصفة وأنه جيد أو رديء وإن كانت النقود مختلفة انصرفت إلى غالب نقد البلد، وإن كانت الأجرة مكيلاً أو موزوناً يحتاج إلى بيان القدر والصفة ومكان الإيفاء. هذا إذا كان له حمل ومؤنة عند الإمام وإلا فلا يحتاج إلى بيان مكان الإيفاء. وإن كانت ثياباً أو عروضاً فالشرط بيان القدر والأجل الصفة لأنه لا يثبت في الذمة إلا بهذا. هذا إذا لم يكن مشاراً إليه. وفي الهداية وما لا يصلح ثمناً يصلح أجرة أيضاً كالأعيان التي ليست من ذوات الأمثال كالحيوان والثياب مثلاً فإنها إذا كانت معينة تصلح أجرة ولا تصلح ثمناً كما إذا استأجر داراً بثوب معين فإنه لا يصلح ثمناً لما تقرر في كتاب البيوع إذا الأموال ثلاثة : ثمن محض كالدراهم والدنانير ومبيع محض كالأعيان التي ليست من ذوات الأمثال، وما كان بينهما كالمكيل والموزون . قال في العناية وفيه نظر لأن المقايضة بيع وليس فيها إلا العين من الجانبين فإذا لم تصلح العين ثمناً كان بيعاً بلا ثمن وهو باطل وأجيب بأن المراد بالثمن ما ثبت في الذمة وإذا كانت الأجرة فلساً فغلا أو رخص قبل القبض فالأجرة الفلس لا غير، وإن كسدت فعليه قيمة المنفعة؛ كذا عن أبي يوسف وكذا إذا كان الثمن كيلاً أو موزوناً فانقطع عن أيدي الناس .اهـ. وأما إذا كانت حيواناً لا يجوز إلا إذا كان معيناً.
The Book of Ijarah. It is a sale of a known benefit for a known rent. And whatever is valid as a price is valid as rent. May Allah have mercy on him: (And whatever is valid as a price is valid as rent because the rent is the price of the benefit, so it is considered by the price of the sold item. Then if the rent is an 'ayn (specific item), it is permissible for every 'ayn to be a substitute for the sold item, but not the reverse, so that what is not valid as a price, like a benefit, is valid as rent if they are of different types, as will come. It is valid. And in al-Jawharah: If a slave was between two people, and one of them leased his share from his partner on condition that he sews with him for a month, and that the other serves in the second month, it is not permissible because the two shares in one slave are identical in the transaction, but if it were two slaves, it would be permissible, end. And if the rent is dirhams or dinars, specification of quantity and quality is necessary, and whether it is good or bad. And if the currencies differ, it refers to the prevalent currency of the country. And if the rent is something measured or weighed, it requires specification of quantity, quality, and place of delivery. This is if it has transport and expense according to Imam, otherwise no need to specify place of delivery. And if it is garments or wares, the condition is specification of quantity, quality, and term because it is not established in the dhimmah except by this. This is if it is not pointed to. And in al-Hidayah: What is not valid as price can also be valid as rent, like goods that are not fungibles, such as animals and garments, for if they are specified, they are valid as rent but not as price, like if one rents a house with a specific garment, it is not valid as price according to what is established in the Book of Sales, for properties are three: pure price like dirhams and dinars, pure sold item like goods that are not fungibles, and what is between them like measured and weighed items. He said in al-'Inayah: And there is a problem because muqayadah is a sale and involves only 'ayn from both sides, so if the 'ayn is not valid as price, it is a sale without price, which is void. And it was answered that by price is meant what is established in the dhimmah. And if the rent is a fals and it increases or decreases in value before taking possession, the rent is that fals, nothing else. And if it becomes obsolete, then the value of the benefit is due; thus from Abu Yusuf. And similarly if the price is something measured or weighed and it disappears from people's hands. End. And as for if it is an animal, it is not permissible unless it is specified.
Source pages p. 5

Commentary
This passage opens the chapter on ijarah. The author first defines ijarah as a contract for the sale of a known benefit for a known rent. He then establishes the principle that anything valid as a price (thaman) in a sale is also valid as rent (ujrah) in ijarah, because rent is the price of the benefit. The commentary elaborates: if the rent is a specific item ('ayn), it is permissible, but the reverse is not true—what cannot be a price can still be rent if the contract is of a different type. Various forms of rent are discussed: for dirhams and dinnars, quantity, quality, and type must be specified; for measured or weighed items, the place of delivery must also be stated if there is transport cost. For garments and wares, the term (ajal) must be specified because otherwise it is not established in the dhimmah. The commentary then cites al-Hidayah: items that are not valid as price (like specific animals or garments) can be valid as rent if they are specified. There is a discussion about muqayadah (barter) and the meaning of price. Finally, there is a ruling from Abu Yusuf about rent in the form of a fals (copper coin): if its value changes before possession, the rent remains that fals; but if it becomes obsolete, the value of the benefit must be paid. Animals are only valid as rent if specifically identified.

Key Terms
إجارة (ijarah): A contract for the sale of a known benefit for a known rent.
منفعة (manfa'ah): The benefit or usufruct that is the subject of the ijarah contract.
أجرة (ujrah): The rent or consideration paid for the benefit in an ijarah contract.
ثمن (thaman): The price in a sale; used as the benchmark for what can be rent.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which of the following conditions is NOT required for rent in the form of a measured item (mawzun)?
A) Specification of quantity
B) Specification of quality
C) Specification of place of delivery if there is transport cost
D) Specification of the term (ajal)

Key Takeaway
The core principle of ijarah is that rent follows the rules of price, but with flexibility: specified non-fungibles that cannot serve as price can still serve as rent.

Ijarah — Hire and Lease
intermediate
8 min
Validity of Lease Term: Specified Duration and the Dispute on Lifespan
Ruling on specifying term in ijarah with intra-Hanafi dispute on excessive duration.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rule that a lease is valid for any known term and explain the dispute regarding terms beyond the usual human lifespan.

Core Idea
A lease is valid for any known term — even beyond normal lifespan — because benefits are known by the term.

This lesson examines the fundamental requirement that the term of a lease must be known for the contract to be valid. The Hanafi school generally considers any specified term sufficient, but there is a notable difference of opinion on setting a term longer than a typical human lifespan. We will trace the reasoning and see which view is adopted for fatwa.

Guided Path
1
Identify the basic ruling on term specification
The text states that benefit in ijarah is known by specifying the term, so a lease is valid for any known term, whether long or short, future or immediate.
This is the default Hanafi position.
2
Locate the intra-Hanafi dispute on excessive terms
Some scholars (Qadi Abu 'Ismah) argue that a term beyond the usual lifespan is invalid because the usual is treated as certain. Others (al-Khassaf) permit it.
The dispute centres on whether the possibility of death makes the term uncertain.
3
Examine the proof and response
The permissive view relies on the fact that the term is explicitly known; the mere risk of death does not create uncertainty in the contract. The opposing view treats the statistical likelihood as a legal certainty.
The text then presents a practical case from al-Khaniyyah to illustrate the preferred view.
4
Determine the mufta bihi
The fatwa is given on the narration that the first lessee cannot rescind the lease, implying that a long-term lease is valid and must be honoured.
Thus the permissive position is adopted by later authorities.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

المدة ذكر في فتاوى أهل سمرقند أنه لا يفسخ العقد، وذكر في شرح الطحاوي أنه يفسخ العقد ويحدد على ما زاد. ولو كانت الأرض بحال لا يمكن فسخها بأن كانت مزروعة لم تحصد فمن وقت الزيادة تجب إلى انتهاء المدة. وقد وقعت حادثة الفتوى في واقف شرط في كتاب وقفه أن لا يؤاجر وقفه من متجوه ولا من ظالم ولا من حاكم فأجر الناظر الوقف منهم. وعجلوا الأجرة قدر أجرة المثل هل يجوز هذا العقد لأن الواقف إنما منع خوفاً على الأجرة من الضياع وعدم حصول النفع للفقراء أو لا العقد
He said, may Allah have mercy on him: And the benefit is known by specifying the term, like residence and cultivation, so it is valid for a known term, meaning whatever term it may be, because if the term is known, the benefit is known, so it is permissible, whether the term is long or short, or delayed (i.e. starting in the future) or advanced (i.e. immediate). And because benefits become known only by specifying a term. And some said: It is not permissible to set a term that a person would not normally live to, because the usual is like certain as far as rulings are concerned, so it becomes like established, so it is not permissible, and Qadi Abu 'Ismah used to give fatwa accordingly. And some scholars, including al-Khassaf, permit setting a term that one would not normally live to. He said in al-Khaniyyah: A man said to another, 'I lease my riding animal to you tomorrow for a dirham,' then he leased it today, tomorrow, and the day after to someone else for three days. When tomorrow came, the first lessee wanted to rescind the second lease. Our companions differed: in one narration, he rescinds the lease—Nasir adopted this; in another narration, he does not have the right to rescind—and al-Faqih Abu Ja'far, al-Faqih Abu al-Layth, and Shams al-A'imma al-Halwani adopted this, and upon it is the fatwa. So the first one takes his term, and the second takes what remains. In the second... [PAGE_006] The Book of Ijarah. The term like residence and cultivation, so it is valid for a known term, and it should not be increased in awqaf beyond three years. Al-Walwalijiyyah: He leased his house as a deferred lease by saying, 'I lease my house to you for the month of Shawwal,' while they are in Ramadan, then he sold it to someone else. The sale is suspended on the consent of the lessee. And in al-Khulasah: 'I lease my house to you tomorrow,' the lessor can sell it today and the lease is rescinded. Three. He said, may Allah have mercy on him: (And it should not be increased in awqaf beyond three years) meaning it should not be increased beyond this period for fear that the lessee might claim it as his own if the term is prolonged. And some mentioned the legal stratagem to allow exceeding the three years: to contract multiple contracts, each contract for one year, and write in the document that so-and-so leased the waqf for such-and-such years in such-and-such contracts. And Sadr al-Islam said that the stratagem is to raise the matter to the judge so that he may permit it. This is if the waqif did not specify a term. If the waqif specified a term, then it is as per his condition, whether short or long, because the condition of the waqif is to be observed; so the commentator transmitted. And in al-Khaniyyah: If the waqif stipulated that it should not be leased for more than one year, his condition must be observed, and one does not give fatwa permitting such a lease for more than one year. al-Dhakhirah added: Unless leasing it for more than a year is more beneficial for the poor, then it may be leased for more than a year if the waqif did not stipulate anything. Al-Faqih Abu Ja'far said: I permit it for three years but not beyond that. And al-Sadr al-Shahid Husam al-Din used to say: He gives fatwa for agricultural lands permitting three years unless the interest is against it, and for non-agricultural lands, he gives fatwa against permitting more than a year unless the interest is for it. And this matter differs with time and place. And by 'lack of permission' is meant lack of validity, and it was said it is valid but rescinded; al-Nasafi mentioned this. And the lease of waqf and property of an orphan is not permissible except at the fair rent (ujrat al-mithl). So if one leases for less than the fair rent, the lessee is bound to pay the full fair rent, and upon this is the fatwa; thus in Qadikhan. And if one leases a waqf and then the rent decreases, the lease is not rescinded. And if the fair rent increases after some time, it is mentioned in the fatawa of the people of Samarqand that the contract is not rescinded, and in Sharh al-Tahawi that the contract is rescinded and a new contract is made at the increased rate. And if the land is in a condition that cannot be rescinded because it is sown and not yet harvested, then from the time of increase the enhanced rent is due until the end of the term. This is if the increase is unanimous. He said in Sharh al-Tahawi: As for private property (amlak), the contract is not rescinded due to decrease or increase of the fair rent, by agreement of the narrations. And in al-Tatarakhaniyyah in the chapter on who is liable for the ongoing rent: Someone was asked about a person who leased a house to a man, and the house is a waqf for another and his children, and the lessee spent on repairing the house by order of the lessor. He said: If the lessor has authority over the waqf, then the lessee owes the fair rent and cannot recover what he spent; if he has no authority over the waqf, he is a volunteer and cannot recover anything, end. And there occurred a fatwa incident: a waqif stipulated in his waqf deed that the waqf should not be leased to an influential person, nor to a wrongdoer, nor to a judge. Then the administrator leased it to such people, and they paid the rent in advance at the fair rate. Is this contract valid? Because the waqif only prohibited out of fear for the loss of rent and lack of benefit to the poor, or not? The contract...
Source pages p. 5

Commentary
This passage contains two main rulings. First, the benefit in ijarah is known by specifying the term (muddah). Any term is valid, long or short, future or immediate, because benefits are only known by fixing a term. There is a difference of opinion among Hanafi scholars regarding setting a term beyond the usual lifespan: some prohibit it based on the principle that the usual is like certain, while others (like al-Khassaf) permit it. The preferred view is that the first lessee's lease is not automatically rescinded, and he completes his term. Second, for waqf properties, the lease should not exceed three years to prevent the lessee from claiming ownership. However, legal stratagems exist: contracting multiple one-year leases or obtaining a judge's permission. If the waqif specified a term, it must be observed. Various scholars have differing views on whether to allow more than three years, and the practice may vary by time and place. Additionally, waqf and orphan property must be leased at fair market rent; if leased for less, the lessee must pay the difference. Changes in market rent during the lease term raise questions about rescission, with differing opinions from Samarqand and Sharh al-Tahawi. Private property leases are not rescinded due to rent changes. The passage concludes with a fatwa incident about leasing waqf to prohibited persons when they pay the fair rent.

Key Terms
مدة (muddah): The specified term or duration of the ijarah contract.
أجر مثل (ujrat al-mithl): The fair market rent for the property.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the preferred Hanafi view, what is the ruling if a lease is for a term of 100 years?
A) Invalid because the lessee will likely die before.
B) Valid because the term is known.
C) Valid only if the lessee is a young person.
D) Invalid because it exceeds three years.

Key Takeaway
A known term makes the benefit known, so any term is valid; the permissive view on long terms is adopted for fatwa.

Ijarah — Hire and Lease
intermediate
