Waqf Leasing: Three-Year Limit and Legal Stratagems
Ruling on waqf leasing limits, stratagems, and ujrat al-mithl requirement.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the default three-year limit on waqf leases, describe accepted legal stratagems to extend the term, and apply the requirement of ujrat al-mithl.

Core Idea
Waqf leases default to three years to prevent ownership claims, but stratagems allow longer terms when beneficial.

The second part of the passage addresses leasing of waqf property. To protect the endowment, the default maximum term is three years, though scholars have developed stratagems to extend this. They also discuss changes in market rent and the requirement to lease at fair value. Understanding these rulings is crucial for managing waqf properties effectively.

Guided Path
1
Identify the default limit on waqf leases
The text states that waqf should not be leased for more than three years to prevent the lessee from claiming ownership over time.
This is a protective measure.
2
Learn the legal stratagems (hiyal) to extend the term
Two stratagems are mentioned: (1) contracting multiple one-year leases in a single document, and (2) obtaining a judge's permission to exceed three years.
These are accepted to facilitate beneficial long-term leases.
3
Consider the waqif's stipulation
If the waqif specified a maximum term, that condition must be observed. If no term is specified, the default three-year limit applies, but can be exceeded for greater benefit.
The waqif's condition overrides the default.
4
Note the requirement of ujrat al-mithl
Waqf and orphan property must be leased at fair market rent. If leased for less, the lessee must pay the difference. Changes in market rent during the term are handled differently according to some scholars.
This ensures the endowment is not undervalued.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال رحمه الله : والمنفعة تعلم ببيان المدة كالسكنى والزراعة فتصح على مدة معلومة) أي مدة كانت لأن المدة إذا كانت معلومة كانت المنفعة معلومة فيجوز ، طالت المدة أو قصرت أو تأخرت بأن كانت مضافة أو تقدمت بأن كانت متصلة بوقت العقد، ولأن المنافع لا تصير معلومة إلا بضرب المدة. وقال بعضهم : لا يجوز أن يضرب إلى مدة لا يعيش إليها عادة لأن الغالب كالمتحقق في حق الأحكام فصار كالثابت بعد فلا تجوز وبه كان يفتي القاضي أبو عصمة. وبعض العلماء، فيجوز ضرب المدة التي لا يعيش إلى مثلها، ومنهم الخصاف . قال في الخانية : رجل قال لآخر أجرتك دابتي غداً بدرهم ثم أجرها اليوم وغداً وبعد غد من غيره ثلاثة أيام فجاء الغد وأراد المستأجر الأول أن يفسخ الإجارة الثانية اختلف أصحابنا في رواية يفسخ الإجارة أخذ نصير وفي رواية ليس له أن يفسخ وبه أخذ الفقيه أو جعفر والفقيه أو الليث وشمس الأئمة الحلواني وعليه الفتوى، فيستوفي الأول مدته والثاني ما بقي له. وفي الثانية وبه  كتاب الإجارة المدة كالسكنى والزراعة فتصح على مدة معلومة ولم تزد في الأوقاف على ثلاث سنين الولوالجية : أجر داره إجارة مضافة بأن قال أجرتك داري مدة شوال وهما في رمضان ثم باعها من آخر فالبيع موقوف على إجارة المستأجر. وفي الخلاصة: أجرتك داري غداً فللمؤجر بيعها اليوم وتنتقض الأجارة. ثلاث قال رحمه الله : (ولم تزد في الأوقاف على ثلاث سنين) يعني لا يزاد على هذه المدة خوفاً من دعوى المستأجر أنها ملكه إذا تطاولت المدة. وذكر بعضهم الحيلة في جواز الزيادة على سنين أن يعقد عقوداً كل عقد على سنة ويكتب في الكتاب أن فلان بن فلان استأجر وقف كذا كذا سنة في كذا كذا عقداً. وذكر صدر الإسلام أن الحيلة فيه أن يرفع الأمر إلى الحاكم حتى يجيزه. هذا إذا لم ينص الواقف على مدة، فلو نص الواقف على مدة فهو على ما شرط، قصرت المدة أو طالت لأن شرط الواقف يراعى ؛ كذا نقله الشارح. وفي الخانية : وإن كان الواقف شرط أن لا يؤجر أكثر من سنة يجب مراعاة شرطه، ولا يفتي بجواز هذه الإجارة أكثر من سنة . زاد في الذخيرة إلا إذا كانت إجارتها أكثر من سنة أنفع للفقراء فحينئذ تؤجر أكثر من سنة إن لم يشترط الواقف شيئاً. قال الفقيه أبو جعفر : أجوزها في الثلاثة ولا أجوزها في أكثر من ذلك، والصدر الشهيد حسام الدين كان يقول : يفتي في الضياع بالجواز في ثلاث سنين إلا إذا كانت المصلحة في عدم الجواز وفي غير الضياع يفتي بعدم الجواز فيما زاد على سنة إلا إذا كانت المصلحة في الجواز وهذا أمر يختلف باختلاف الزمان والمواضع. والمراد بعدم الجواز عدم الصحة وقيل تصح وتفسخ ؛ ذكره النسفي. وإجارة الوقف ومال اليتيم لا يجوز إلا بأجر المثل، فلو أجر بدون أجرة المثل يلزم المستأجر تمام الأجرة وعليه الفتوى؛ كذا في قاضيخان . وإذا استأجر الوقف فرخصت الأجرة لا تفسخ الإجارة، وإن زادت أجرة مثلها بعد مضي بعض المدة ذكر في فتاوى أهل سمرقند أنه لا يفسخ العقد، وذكر في شرح الطحاوي أنه يفسخ العقد ويحدد على ما زاد. ولو كانت الأرض بحال لا يمكن فسخها بأن كانت مزروعة لم تحصد فمن وقت الزيادة تجب إلى انتهاء المدة. هذا إذا زادت عند الكل. قال في شرح الطحاوي : أما في الأملاك لا يفسخ برخص أجرة المثل ولا بزيادته باتفاق الروايات. وفي التتارخانية في باب من يجب الأجر الجاري سئل عمن آجر منزلاً لرجل والمنزل وقف على الآخر وعلى أولاده فأنفق المستأجر في عمارة المنزل بأمر المؤجر قال : إن كان للمؤجر ولاية على الوقف كان على المستأجر أجرة مثله ولا يرجع بما أنفق، وإن لم يكن له ولاية على الوقف كان متطوعاً ولا يرجع بشيء اهـ. وقد وقعت حادثة الفتوى في واقف شرط في كتاب وقفه أن لا يؤاجر وقفه من متجوه ولا من ظالم ولا من حاكم فأجر الناظر الوقف منهم. وعجلوا الأجرة قدر أجرة المثل هل يجوز هذا العقد لأن الواقف إنما منع خوفاً على الأجرة من الضياع وعدم حصول النفع للفقراء أو لا العقد
He said, may Allah have mercy on him: And the benefit is known by specifying the term, like residence and cultivation, so it is valid for a known term, meaning whatever term it may be, because if the term is known, the benefit is known, so it is permissible, whether the term is long or short, or delayed (i.e. starting in the future) or advanced (i.e. immediate). And because benefits become known only by specifying a term. And some said: It is not permissible to set a term that a person would not normally live to, because the usual is like certain as far as rulings are concerned, so it becomes like established, so it is not permissible, and Qadi Abu 'Ismah used to give fatwa accordingly. And some scholars, including al-Khassaf, permit setting a term that one would not normally live to. He said in al-Khaniyyah: A man said to another, 'I lease my riding animal to you tomorrow for a dirham,' then he leased it today, tomorrow, and the day after to someone else for three days. When tomorrow came, the first lessee wanted to rescind the second lease. Our companions differed: in one narration, he rescinds the lease—Nasir adopted this; in another narration, he does not have the right to rescind—and al-Faqih Abu Ja'far, al-Faqih Abu al-Layth, and Shams al-A'imma al-Halwani adopted this, and upon it is the fatwa. So the first one takes his term, and the second takes what remains. In the second... [PAGE_006] The Book of Ijarah. The term like residence and cultivation, so it is valid for a known term, and it should not be increased in awqaf beyond three years. Al-Walwalijiyyah: He leased his house as a deferred lease by saying, 'I lease my house to you for the month of Shawwal,' while they are in Ramadan, then he sold it to someone else. The sale is suspended on the consent of the lessee. And in al-Khulasah: 'I lease my house to you tomorrow,' the lessor can sell it today and the lease is rescinded. Three. He said, may Allah have mercy on him: (And it should not be increased in awqaf beyond three years) meaning it should not be increased beyond this period for fear that the lessee might claim it as his own if the term is prolonged. And some mentioned the legal stratagem to allow exceeding the three years: to contract multiple contracts, each contract for one year, and write in the document that so-and-so leased the waqf for such-and-such years in such-and-such contracts. And Sadr al-Islam said that the stratagem is to raise the matter to the judge so that he may permit it. This is if the waqif did not specify a term. If the waqif specified a term, then it is as per his condition, whether short or long, because the condition of the waqif is to be observed; so the commentator transmitted. And in al-Khaniyyah: If the waqif stipulated that it should not be leased for more than one year, his condition must be observed, and one does not give fatwa permitting such a lease for more than one year. al-Dhakhirah added: Unless leasing it for more than a year is more beneficial for the poor, then it may be leased for more than a year if the waqif did not stipulate anything. Al-Faqih Abu Ja'far said: I permit it for three years but not beyond that. And al-Sadr al-Shahid Husam al-Din used to say: He gives fatwa for agricultural lands permitting three years unless the interest is against it, and for non-agricultural lands, he gives fatwa against permitting more than a year unless the interest is for it. And this matter differs with time and place. And by 'lack of permission' is meant lack of validity, and it was said it is valid but rescinded; al-Nasafi mentioned this. And the lease of waqf and property of an orphan is not permissible except at the fair rent (ujrat al-mithl). So if one leases for less than the fair rent, the lessee is bound to pay the full fair rent, and upon this is the fatwa; thus in Qadikhan. And if one leases a waqf and then the rent decreases, the lease is not rescinded. And if the fair rent increases after some time, it is mentioned in the fatawa of the people of Samarqand that the contract is not rescinded, and in Sharh al-Tahawi that the contract is rescinded and a new contract is made at the increased rate. And if the land is in a condition that cannot be rescinded because it is sown and not yet harvested, then from the time of increase the enhanced rent is due until the end of the term. This is if the increase is unanimous. He said in Sharh al-Tahawi: As for private property (amlak), the contract is not rescinded due to decrease or increase of the fair rent, by agreement of the narrations. And in al-Tatarakhaniyyah in the chapter on who is liable for the ongoing rent: Someone was asked about a person who leased a house to a man, and the house is a waqf for another and his children, and the lessee spent on repairing the house by order of the lessor. He said: If the lessor has authority over the waqf, then the lessee owes the fair rent and cannot recover what he spent; if he has no authority over the waqf, he is a volunteer and cannot recover anything, end. And there occurred a fatwa incident: a waqif stipulated in his waqf deed that the waqf should not be leased to an influential person, nor to a wrongdoer, nor to a judge. Then the administrator leased it to such people, and they paid the rent in advance at the fair rate. Is this contract valid? Because the waqif only prohibited out of fear for the loss of rent and lack of benefit to the poor, or not? The contract...
Source pages p. 5

Commentary
This passage contains two main rulings. First, the benefit in ijarah is known by specifying the term (muddah). Any term is valid, long or short, future or immediate, because benefits are only known by fixing a term. There is a difference of opinion among Hanafi scholars regarding setting a term beyond the usual lifespan: some prohibit it based on the principle that the usual is like certain, while others (like al-Khassaf) permit it. The preferred view is that the first lessee's lease is not automatically rescinded, and he completes his term. Second, for waqf properties, the lease should not exceed three years to prevent the lessee from claiming ownership. However, legal stratagems exist: contracting multiple one-year leases or obtaining a judge's permission. If the waqif specified a term, it must be observed. Various scholars have differing views on whether to allow more than three years, and the practice may vary by time and place. Additionally, waqf and orphan property must be leased at fair market rent; if leased for less, the lessee must pay the difference. Changes in market rent during the lease term raise questions about rescission, with differing opinions from Samarqand and Sharh al-Tahawi. Private property leases are not rescinded due to rent changes. The passage concludes with a fatwa incident about leasing waqf to prohibited persons when they pay the fair rent.

Key Terms
وقف (waqf): A charitable endowment, the property of which cannot be sold or given away; its usufruct is for beneficiaries.
أجر مثل (ujrat al-mithl): The fair market rent for the property.
حيلة (hilah): A legal stratagem to achieve a permissible outcome while technically complying with restrictions.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following is a valid legal stratagem to lease a waqf property for more than three years?
A) Sign a single contract for five years with a condition that the lessee will not claim ownership.
B) Write multiple one-year lease contracts in one document.
C) Lease at a rent much higher than ujrat al-mithl.
D) Lease to a government official.

Key Takeaway
Waqf leases default to three years to protect the endowment, but stratagems and judicial permission can allow longer terms when beneficial.

Ijarah — Hire and Lease
beginner
8 min
The Three-Year Limit for Waqf Leases
Ruling on default lease duration and hiyal

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the default maximum lease term for waqf properties, explain the rationale, and describe the legal tricks used to extend the term.

Core Idea
A waqf lease beyond three years risks ownership claims; hiyal such as annual renewals or judicial permission allow extension when beneficial.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq establishes the default ruling that leases of waqf property should not exceed three years. The commentator explains the reason—preventing the lessee from claiming ownership—and then provides two legal strategies (hiyal) to extend the term if needed. The ruling changes if the founder explicitly stipulated a period.

Guided Path
1
Identify the default ruling
The matn states that leases of awqaf should not exceed three years. This is the default rule.
The three-year limit is specific to waqf; private property has no such restriction.
2
Understand the rationale
The reason is 'خوفاً من دعوى المستأجر أنها ملكه' – fear that the lessee might claim ownership if the period is long.
This rationale is crucial for understanding later flexibility.
3
Explore the legal tricks (hiyal)
Two tricks: (1) Make separate annual contracts, each for one year, and record them as multiple contracts. (2) Refer the matter to a judge for permission to exceed three years.
These tricks preserve the form while achieving the desired duration.
4
Note the exception for founder's stipulation
If the waqf founder stipulated a specific term (e.g., two years or ten years), that condition must be observed, irrespective of the three-year rule.
The principle: شرط الواقف يراعى (the founder's condition is observed).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الإجارة المدة كالسكنى والزراعة فتصح على مدة معلومة ولم تزد في الأوقاف على ثلاث سنين الولوالجية : أجر داره إجارة مضافة بأن قال أجرتك داري مدة شوال وهما في رمضان ثم باعها من آخر فالبيع موقوف على إجارة المستأجر. وفي الخلاصة: أجرتك داري غداً فللمؤجر بيعها اليوم وتنتقض الأجارة. ثلاث قال رحمه الله : (ولم تزد في الأوقاف على ثلاث سنين) يعني لا يزاد على هذه المدة خوفاً من دعوى المستأجر أنها ملكه إذا تطاولت المدة. وذكر بعضهم الحيلة في جواز الزيادة على سنين أن يعقد عقوداً كل عقد على سنة ويكتب في الكتاب أن فلان بن فلان استأجر وقف كذا كذا سنة في كذا كذا عقداً. وذكر صدر الإسلام أن الحيلة فيه أن يرفع الأمر إلى الحاكم حتى يجيزه. هذا إذا لم ينص الواقف على مدة، فلو نص الواقف على مدة فهو على ما شرط، قصرت المدة أو طالت لأن شرط الواقف يراعى ؛ كذا نقله الشارح. وفي الخانية : وإن كان الواقف شرط أن لا يؤجر أكثر من سنة يجب مراعاة شرطه، ولا يفتي بجواز هذه الإجارة أكثر من سنة . زاد في الذخيرة إلا إذا كانت إجارتها أكثر من سنة أنفع للفقراء فحينئذ تؤجر أكثر من سنة إن لم يشترط الواقف شيئاً. قال الفقيه أبو جعفر : أجوزها في الثلاثة ولا أجوزها في أكثر من ذلك، والصدر الشهيد حسام الدين كان يقول : يفتي في الضياع بالجواز في ثلاث سنين إلا إذا كانت المصلحة في عدم الجواز وفي غير الضياع يفتي بعدم الجواز فيما زاد على سنة إلا إذا كانت المصلحة في الجواز وهذا أمر يختلف باختلاف الزمان والمواضع. والمراد بعدم الجواز عدم الصحة وقيل تصح وتفسخ ؛ ذكره النسفي. وإجارة الوقف ومال اليتيم لا يجوز إلا بأجر المثل، فلو أجر بدون أجرة المثل يلزم المستأجر تمام الأجرة وعليه الفتوى؛ كذا في قاضيخان . وإذا استأجر الوقف فرخصت الأجرة لا تفسخ الإجارة، وإن زادت أجرة مثلها بعد مضي بعض المدة ذكر في فتاوى أهل سمرقند أنه لا يفسخ العقد، وذكر في شرح الطحاوي أنه يفسخ العقد ويحدد على ما زاد. ولو كانت الأرض بحال لا يمكن فسخها بأن كانت مزروعة لم تحصد فمن وقت الزيادة تجب إلى انتهاء المدة. هذا إذا زادت عند الكل. قال في شرح الطحاوي : أما في الأملاك لا يفسخ برخص أجرة المثل ولا بزيادته باتفاق الروايات. وفي التتارخانية في باب من يجب الأجر الجاري سئل عمن آجر منزلاً لرجل والمنزل وقف على الآخر وعلى أولاده فأنفق المستأجر في عمارة المنزل بأمر المؤجر قال : إن كان للمؤجر ولاية على الوقف كان على المستأجر أجرة مثله ولا يرجع بما أنفق، وإن لم يكن له ولاية على الوقف كان متطوعاً ولا يرجع بشيء اهـ. وقد وقعت حادثة الفتوى في واقف شرط في كتاب وقفه أن لا يؤاجر وقفه من متجوه ولا من ظالم ولا من حاكم فأجر الناظر الوقف منهم. وعجلوا الأجرة قدر أجرة المثل هل يجوز هذا العقد لأن الواقف إنما منع خوفاً على الأجرة من الضياع وعدم حصول النفع للفقراء أو لا العقد فأجيب بالجواز أخذاً من قول صاحب الوجيز إذا شرط الواقف مدة وإن كان نفع الفقراء في غيره يخالف شرط الواقف ويؤجره بخلافه
The Book of Ijarah. The period (of lease) is like residence and agriculture, so it is valid for a known period, and it should not be increased in endowments beyond three years. Al-Walwaliji: He leased his house with a deferred lease, saying 'I leased you my house for the month of Shawwal' while they are in Ramadan, then he sold it to another; the sale is suspended until the lessee's lease (is sorted). In al-Khulasa: 'I leased you my house tomorrow' – the lessor may sell it today and the lease is annulled. Three. He (the author) said: (And it should not be increased in endowments beyond three years), meaning do not increase beyond this period for fear of the lessee claiming it is his property if the period is prolonged. Some mentioned the legal trick to allow increase beyond years: that he contracts each contract for a year and writes in the document that so-and-so leased a certain waqf for such-and-such years in such-and-such contracts. Sadr al-Islam mentioned that the trick is to refer the matter to the judge so that he permits it. This applies if the waqf founder did not stipulate a period; if he did stipulate a period, then it is according to his condition, whether short or long, because the founder's condition is observed; as quoted by the commentator. In al-Khaniyya: If the founder stipulated not to lease for more than a year, his condition must be observed, and a fatwa is not given permitting such a lease for more than a year. Al-Dhakhira added: Unless leasing for more than a year is more beneficial for the poor, then it may be leased for more than a year if the founder did not stipulate anything. Al-Faqih Abu Ja'far said: I permit it for three years and do not permit it for more than that. Al-Sadr al-Shahid Husam al-Din used to say: A fatwa is given in agricultural lands for permissibility for three years unless the benefit is in non-permissibility; and in non-agricultural lands, a fatwa is given for non-permissibility beyond one year unless the benefit is in permissibility. This matter varies with time and place. And what is meant by non-permissibility is lack of validity; it is said that it is valid but then rescinded; mentioned by al-Nasafi. Leasing waqf and the property of an orphan is not permissible except for the fair rent; if he leases for less than the fair rent, the lessee is required to pay the full rent, and the fatwa is upon this; as in Qadikhan. If one leases waqf and the rent decreases, the lease is not annulled; if its fair rent increases after some time, it was mentioned in the fatwa of the people of Samarkand that the contract is not annulled; and it was mentioned in Sharh al-Tahawi that the contract is annulled and a new contract is made at the increased rate. But if the land is in a state that cannot be annulled, such as being sown but not harvested, then from the time of increase the increased rent is due until the end of the period. This applies when the increase is agreed by all. In Sharh al-Tahawi: As for private properties, the lease is not annulled by a decrease or increase of the fair rent by agreement of the narrations. In al-Tatar Khaniyya, in the chapter on who bears the recurring rent, he was asked about someone who leased a house to a man, and the house is a waqf for another and his children, and the lessee spent on repairing the house by order of the lessor. He said: If the lessor had authority over the waqf, then the lessee owes the fair rent and does not get reimbursement for what he spent; if he did not have authority over the waqf, then he is a volunteer and does not get anything back. A fatwa incident occurred: a founder stipulated in his waqf deed that his waqf should not be leased to an arrogant person, nor to a tyrant, nor to a ruler; then the administrator leased the waqf to such persons, and they paid the rent in advance at the fair rent. Is this contract valid? Because the founder only prohibited out of fear for the rent being lost and the benefit not reaching the poor? Or is the contract invalid? The answer: it is valid, taking from the statement of the author of al-Wajiz: if the founder stipulates a period, even if the benefit for the poor lies in something else, one may go against the founder's condition and lease it contrary to it.
Source pages p. 6

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement from the Book of Ijarah concerning the lease of waqf properties. The matn states that just as lease for residential or agricultural use is valid for a known period, in the case of awqaf (endowments) the lease should not exceed three years. The sharh explains the rationale: to prevent the lessee from claiming ownership after a long tenure. The passage then provides legal tricks (hiyal) to extend the term, such as renewing annually or seeking a judge's approval. It also discusses scenarios where the waqf founder stipulated a specific term, which must then be observed. There is ikhtilaf among later scholars: some like Abu Ja'far permit three years only, while others like Husam al-Din differentiate between agricultural and non-agricultural lands, allowing flexibility based on benefit (maslaha). The passage also covers rules about leasing at the fair rent (ajr al-mithl), the effect of rent changes during the lease, and a specific case where the founder prohibited leasing to certain persons but the administrator did so for the benefit of the poor; the fatwa allowed it. Throughout, the authority weight is from later fatwa collections (fatawa mutakhkhirin) rather than the Zahir al-Riwayah, reflecting post-classical developments.

Key Terms
وقف (waqf): An endowment of property for charitable purposes
إجارة (ijarah): A lease contract for the use of an asset in exchange for rent
أجر المثل (ajr al-mithl): The fair market rent for a property

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the default maximum lease term for a waqf property if the founder did not stipulate a period?
A) One year
B) Three years
C) Five years
D) No limit

Key Takeaway
The default three-year limit on waqf leases is a precaution against ownership claims, but can be circumvented through annual contracts or judicial permission.

Ijarah — Hire and Lease
intermediate
12 min
Extending Waqf Leases: Ikhtilaf and the Role of Benefit
Intra-Hanafi dispute on lease duration and fatwa on overriding founder's stipulation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the ikhtilaf among later Hanafi scholars on extending waqf leases beyond three years, and apply the principle of benefit (maslaha) to determine the operative view.

Core Idea
Later Hanafi scholars differ on exceeding three years; some allow three, others allow more if beneficial; the fatwa incident shows benefit can override the founder's stipulation.

This part of the commentary presents the views of later Hanafi jurists on the restriction. Abu Ja'far permits only three years; Husam al-Din distinguishes agricultural lands (three years) from non-agricultural (one year), with benefit as a deciding factor. The passage also includes a fatwa where the administrator leased to prohibited persons because it benefited the poor, and the answer permitted it, showing that benefit can override a founder's condition.

Guided Path
1
Identify the views of Abu Ja'far and Husam al-Din
Abu Ja'far permits only three years. Husam al-Din permits three for agricultural lands and one for non-agricultural, but both can be extended if benefit (maslaha) requires.
Note that both are later Hanafi authorities, not from the founding three imams.
2
Understand the distinction between land types
Husam al-Din differentiates: agricultural lands (ضياع) can be leased up to three years; non-agricultural (غير الضياع) up to one year, unless benefit dictates otherwise.
This distinction reflects economic reality: agricultural leases need longer terms for crop cycles.
3
Analyze the fatwa incident
A founder prohibited leasing to tyrants, but the administrator did so because the poor benefited. The fatwa allowed it, citing the principle from al-Wajiz that the founder's condition can be ignored if the poor's benefit lies elsewhere.
This shows that benefit (maslaha) can override even explicit stipulations of the waqf founder.
4
Extract the overarching principle
The underlying principle is that the purpose of waqf—benefiting the poor—can sometimes override ancillary conditions. This is consistent with the Hanafi emphasis on istihsan.
This principle is not unlimited; it applies when benefit is clear and the condition was not the primary intent.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الإجارة المدة كالسكنى والزراعة فتصح على مدة معلومة ولم تزد في الأوقاف على ثلاث سنين الولوالجية : أجر داره إجارة مضافة بأن قال أجرتك داري مدة شوال وهما في رمضان ثم باعها من آخر فالبيع موقوف على إجارة المستأجر. وفي الخلاصة: أجرتك داري غداً فللمؤجر بيعها اليوم وتنتقض الأجارة. ثلاث قال رحمه الله : (ولم تزد في الأوقاف على ثلاث سنين) يعني لا يزاد على هذه المدة خوفاً من دعوى المستأجر أنها ملكه إذا تطاولت المدة. وذكر بعضهم الحيلة في جواز الزيادة على سنين أن يعقد عقوداً كل عقد على سنة ويكتب في الكتاب أن فلان بن فلان استأجر وقف كذا كذا سنة في كذا كذا عقداً. وذكر صدر الإسلام أن الحيلة فيه أن يرفع الأمر إلى الحاكم حتى يجيزه. هذا إذا لم ينص الواقف على مدة، فلو نص الواقف على مدة فهو على ما شرط، قصرت المدة أو طالت لأن شرط الواقف يراعى ؛ كذا نقله الشارح. وفي الخانية : وإن كان الواقف شرط أن لا يؤجر أكثر من سنة يجب مراعاة شرطه، ولا يفتي بجواز هذه الإجارة أكثر من سنة . زاد في الذخيرة إلا إذا كانت إجارتها أكثر من سنة أنفع للفقراء فحينئذ تؤجر أكثر من سنة إن لم يشترط الواقف شيئاً. قال الفقيه أبو جعفر : أجوزها في الثلاثة ولا أجوزها في أكثر من ذلك، والصدر الشهيد حسام الدين كان يقول : يفتي في الضياع بالجواز في ثلاث سنين إلا إذا كانت المصلحة في عدم الجواز وفي غير الضياع يفتي بعدم الجواز فيما زاد على سنة إلا إذا كانت المصلحة في الجواز وهذا أمر يختلف باختلاف الزمان والمواضع. والمراد بعدم الجواز عدم الصحة وقيل تصح وتفسخ ؛ ذكره النسفي. وإجارة الوقف ومال اليتيم لا يجوز إلا بأجر المثل، فلو أجر بدون أجرة المثل يلزم المستأجر تمام الأجرة وعليه الفتوى؛ كذا في قاضيخان . وإذا استأجر الوقف فرخصت الأجرة لا تفسخ الإجارة، وإن زادت أجرة مثلها بعد مضي بعض المدة ذكر في فتاوى أهل سمرقند أنه لا يفسخ العقد، وذكر في شرح الطحاوي أنه يفسخ العقد ويحدد على ما زاد. ولو كانت الأرض بحال لا يمكن فسخها بأن كانت مزروعة لم تحصد فمن وقت الزيادة تجب إلى انتهاء المدة. هذا إذا زادت عند الكل. قال في شرح الطحاوي : أما في الأملاك لا يفسخ برخص أجرة المثل ولا بزيادته باتفاق الروايات. وفي التتارخانية في باب من يجب الأجر الجاري سئل عمن آجر منزلاً لرجل والمنزل وقف على الآخر وعلى أولاده فأنفق المستأجر في عمارة المنزل بأمر المؤجر قال : إن كان للمؤجر ولاية على الوقف كان على المستأجر أجرة مثله ولا يرجع بما أنفق، وإن لم يكن له ولاية على الوقف كان متطوعاً ولا يرجع بشيء اهـ. وقد وقعت حادثة الفتوى في واقف شرط في كتاب وقفه أن لا يؤاجر وقفه من متجوه ولا من ظالم ولا من حاكم فأجر الناظر الوقف منهم. وعجلوا الأجرة قدر أجرة المثل هل يجوز هذا العقد لأن الواقف إنما منع خوفاً على الأجرة من الضياع وعدم حصول النفع للفقراء أو لا العقد فأجيب بالجواز أخذاً من قول صاحب الوجيز إذا شرط الواقف مدة وإن كان نفع الفقراء في غيره يخالف شرط الواقف ويؤجره بخلافه
The Book of Ijarah. The period (of lease) is like residence and agriculture, so it is valid for a known period, and it should not be increased in endowments beyond three years. Al-Walwaliji: He leased his house with a deferred lease, saying 'I leased you my house for the month of Shawwal' while they are in Ramadan, then he sold it to another; the sale is suspended until the lessee's lease (is sorted). In al-Khulasa: 'I leased you my house tomorrow' – the lessor may sell it today and the lease is annulled. Three. He (the author) said: (And it should not be increased in endowments beyond three years), meaning do not increase beyond this period for fear of the lessee claiming it is his property if the period is prolonged. Some mentioned the legal trick to allow increase beyond years: that he contracts each contract for a year and writes in the document that so-and-so leased a certain waqf for such-and-such years in such-and-such contracts. Sadr al-Islam mentioned that the trick is to refer the matter to the judge so that he permits it. This applies if the waqf founder did not stipulate a period; if he did stipulate a period, then it is according to his condition, whether short or long, because the founder's condition is observed; as quoted by the commentator. In al-Khaniyya: If the founder stipulated not to lease for more than a year, his condition must be observed, and a fatwa is not given permitting such a lease for more than a year. Al-Dhakhira added: Unless leasing for more than a year is more beneficial for the poor, then it may be leased for more than a year if the founder did not stipulate anything. Al-Faqih Abu Ja'far said: I permit it for three years and do not permit it for more than that. Al-Sadr al-Shahid Husam al-Din used to say: A fatwa is given in agricultural lands for permissibility for three years unless the benefit is in non-permissibility; and in non-agricultural lands, a fatwa is given for non-permissibility beyond one year unless the benefit is in permissibility. This matter varies with time and place. And what is meant by non-permissibility is lack of validity; it is said that it is valid but then rescinded; mentioned by al-Nasafi. Leasing waqf and the property of an orphan is not permissible except for the fair rent; if he leases for less than the fair rent, the lessee is required to pay the full rent, and the fatwa is upon this; as in Qadikhan. If one leases waqf and the rent decreases, the lease is not annulled; if its fair rent increases after some time, it was mentioned in the fatwa of the people of Samarkand that the contract is not annulled; and it was mentioned in Sharh al-Tahawi that the contract is annulled and a new contract is made at the increased rate. But if the land is in a state that cannot be annulled, such as being sown but not harvested, then from the time of increase the increased rent is due until the end of the period. This applies when the increase is agreed by all. In Sharh al-Tahawi: As for private properties, the lease is not annulled by a decrease or increase of the fair rent by agreement of the narrations. In al-Tatar Khaniyya, in the chapter on who bears the recurring rent, he was asked about someone who leased a house to a man, and the house is a waqf for another and his children, and the lessee spent on repairing the house by order of the lessor. He said: If the lessor had authority over the waqf, then the lessee owes the fair rent and does not get reimbursement for what he spent; if he did not have authority over the waqf, then he is a volunteer and does not get anything back. A fatwa incident occurred: a founder stipulated in his waqf deed that his waqf should not be leased to an arrogant person, nor to a tyrant, nor to a ruler; then the administrator leased the waqf to such persons, and they paid the rent in advance at the fair rent. Is this contract valid? Because the founder only prohibited out of fear for the rent being lost and the benefit not reaching the poor? Or is the contract invalid? The answer: it is valid, taking from the statement of the author of al-Wajiz: if the founder stipulates a period, even if the benefit for the poor lies in something else, one may go against the founder's condition and lease it contrary to it.
Source pages p. 6

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement from the Book of Ijarah concerning the lease of waqf properties. The matn states that just as lease for residential or agricultural use is valid for a known period, in the case of awqaf (endowments) the lease should not exceed three years. The sharh explains the rationale: to prevent the lessee from claiming ownership after a long tenure. The passage then provides legal tricks (hiyal) to extend the term, such as renewing annually or seeking a judge's approval. It also discusses scenarios where the waqf founder stipulated a specific term, which must then be observed. There is ikhtilaf among later scholars: some like Abu Ja'far permit three years only, while others like Husam al-Din differentiate between agricultural and non-agricultural lands, allowing flexibility based on benefit (maslaha). The passage also covers rules about leasing at the fair rent (ajr al-mithl), the effect of rent changes during the lease, and a specific case where the founder prohibited leasing to certain persons but the administrator did so for the benefit of the poor; the fatwa allowed it. Throughout, the authority weight is from later fatwa collections (fatawa mutakhkhirin) rather than the Zahir al-Riwayah, reflecting post-classical developments.

Key Terms
وقف (waqf): An endowment of property for charitable purposes
إجارة (ijarah): A lease contract for the use of an asset in exchange for rent
أجر المثل (ajr al-mithl): The fair market rent for a property

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the fatwa incident in this lesson, why was the lease to a tyrant considered valid despite the founder's prohibition?
A) Because the founder's condition was invalid.
B) Because the poor benefited more, and the condition was only precautionary.
C) Because the tyrant was a relative of the founder.
D) Because the lease was approved by a judge.

Key Takeaway
The three-year limit is not absolute; later Hanafi scholars permit extensions based on benefit, and even the founder's condition can be overridden for the poor's welfare.

Specifying the Benefit in Ijarah by Tasmia
Definition and ruling on tasmia

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions under which a benefit is validly specified in an ijarah contract through detailed description (tasmia).

Core Idea
Specification of the benefit removes ambiguity; missing details invalidate the ijarah.

In Hanafi law, the benefit (manfa'ah) in an ijarah contract must be known to avoid gharar. The author explains that one method is tasmia—explicitly detailing the nature of the work, the object, and the duration. This lesson unpacks what is required for a valid specification.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Recognize that the ruling is about how the benefit becomes known in an ijarah contract. The permissible methods are tasmia and ishara.
Tasmia is detailed description.
2
List the elements of specification
When hiring for dyeing and sewing, the elements that must be clarified include: the cloth, the dye, the amount and type of dye, the type of sewing, the thread, who rides the animal, the load capacity, and the distance.
These remove uncertainty.
3
Apply the condition to a counter-example
The commentator gives the example of hiring donkeys of conveyors (dawab al-allaqin) and declares it invalid because time and place are not stated.
This illustrates the consequence of insufficient specification.
4
State the fiqh consequence
If the specification is complete, the contract is valid; if incomplete, the contract is fasid (voidable).
The rent is owned only upon utilization or ability to utilize, not by contract alone.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أو بالتسمية كالاستئجار على صبغ الثوب وخياطته أو بالإشارة كالاستئجار على نقل هذا الطعام إلى كذا والأجرة لا تملك بالعقد بل بالتعجيل أو بشرطه أو بالاستيفاء أو بالتمكن منه قال رحمه الله: (أو بالتسمية كالاستئجار على صبغ الثوب وخياطته) يعني المنفعة تعلم بالتسمية فيما ذكر من الصبغ والخياطة كما ذكر المؤلف، وكذلك استئجار الدابة للحمل والركوب، ولأنه إذا بين المصبوغ والصبغ وقدر ما يصبغ به وجنسه وجنس الخياطة والخيط ومن يركب على الدابة والقدر المحمول عليها والمسافة صارت المنفعة معلومة بلا شبهة فصح النوع الاستئجار على العلم كالقصارة ،ونحوه وبه يعلم فساد إجارة دواب العلاقين في ديارنا لعدم بيان الوقت والموضع . قال رحمه الله: (أو بالإشارة كالاستئجار على نقل هذا الطعام إلى كذا) يعني تكون المنفعة معلومة بالإشارة كما ذكر لأنه إذا علم المنقول والمكان المنقول إليه صارت المنفعة معلومة، وهذا النوع قريب من النوع الأول.
Or by specification, like hiring for dyeing a garment and sewing it; or by indication, like hiring to carry this food to such place. And the rent is not owned by the contract but by advance payment, or by stipulation, or by utilization, or by being enabled to utilize. He (the author) said: (Or by specification like hiring for dyeing a garment and sewing it) meaning the benefit is known by specification in what was mentioned of dyeing and sewing, as the author mentioned. Likewise, hiring an animal for carrying loads and riding, because if he clarifies the dyed item, the dye, the amount to dye with, its type, the type of sewing, the thread, who will ride the animal, the load capacity, and the distance, the benefit becomes known without doubt, so the type of hiring for knowledge (like fulling) is valid, and similarly, one knows the invalidity of hiring the donkeys of the conveyors in our lands due to lack of clarification of time and place. He (the author) said: (Or by indication like hiring to carry this food to such place) meaning the benefit is known by indication as mentioned because when the transported item and the place it is transported to are known, the benefit becomes known, and this type is similar to the first type.
Source pages p. 7

Commentary
This passage is a definition and ruling on how the benefit (manfa'ah) must be specified in an ijarah contract. The matn gives two methods: specification (tasmia), e.g., hiring a tailor to dye and sew a specific garment, and indication (ishara), e.g., hiring someone to carry this specific food to a place. The sharh elaborates: for specification, the details must be sufficient to remove ambiguity, such as describing the cloth, the dye, the stitching, the thread, the animal, the load, and the distance. For indication, pointing to the specific item and place makes the benefit known. The commentator uses this to criticize the common practice of hiring 'donkeys of the conveyors' (dawab al-allaqin) in his region, because the time and place are not stipulated, rendering the contract invalid. The passage also mentions that the rent is not owned by the contract itself—a separate ruling that will be expanded later. This lesson focuses on the methods of knowing the benefit.

Key Terms
تسمية (tasmia): Specifying the benefit in an ijarah contract through detailed description
منفعة (manfa'ah): The usufruct or benefit that is the subject of the ijarah contract

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why did the commentator declare the hiring of 'dawab al-allaqin' (donkeys of conveyors) invalid?
A) Because donkeys cannot be hired
B) Because the time and place were not specified
C) Because the load was not known
D) Because the contract was oral

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi law, the benefit in ijarah must be known through detailed specification (tasmia) to validate the contract.

Knowing the Benefit by Indication (Ishara)
Definition and ruling on ishara

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain how the benefit in an ijarah contract is made known through physical indication (ishara) and apply it to a scenario.

Core Idea
Pointing to the object and destination makes the benefit clear and valid.

In addition to verbal specification, the benefit can be made known by physically indicating the item and the place. The author gives the example of hiring someone to carry 'this food to such place'. This lesson examines the validity of indication and its requirements.

Guided Path
1
Identify the method
Ishara is pointing to the specific item (e.g., this food) and the specific location (e.g., to Kada).
2
Understand the condition
The item and destination must be physically present or clearly identifiable. Indication removes ambiguity.
The contract is valid if the object is known by pointing.
3
Compare with tasmia
The commentator says this type is similar to tasmia, meaning the same level of certainty is achieved.
Both methods prevent gharar.
4
Apply the ruling
If the indication is clear, the contract is sahih; if ambiguous (e.g., 'carry some food to some place'), it is fasid.
The rent is owned upon utilization.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

Or by specification, like hiring for dyeing a garment and sewing it; or by indication, like hiring to carry this food to such place. Key Terms
إشارة (ishara): Making the benefit known by pointing to the object or place
منفعة (manfa'ah): The usufruct or benefit that is the subject of the ijarah contract

Checkpoint
Why is indication (ishara) sufficient to make the benefit known in an ijarah contract?
A) Because pointing removes all uncertainty

C) Because the contract is oral

When Is Rent Owned? Hanafi vs Shafi'i
Ruling that rental payment is not owned by the contract itself, but by one of four events: advance payment, stipulation, utilization, or enablement.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the four Hanafi methods of owning rental payment and explain why the Shafi'i position of immediate ownership is rejected.

Core Idea
In Hanafi fiqh, rent is not owned by contract alone; it is only owned by payment, stipulation, utilization, or enablement.

This lesson examines a key difference between the Hanafi and Shafi'i schools in the law of ijarah. The learned author of Kanz al-Daqa'iq states that rent is not owned by the contract itself but by specific events. We will unpack the Hanafi position, the intra-Hanafi nuances, and the Shafi'i counter-argument.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core ruling
Read the matn: 'Rent is not owned by the contract but by advance payment, or its condition, or utilization, or being enabled.' Understand that this is the fundamental Hanafi position.
Note the contrast with sale, where ownership transfers immediately.
2
Understand the four events
Define each: ta'jil (advance payment), shart (stipulation), istifa' (actual utilization), and tamkin (enablement to utilize). Each is a separate cause for ownership.
Tamkin is unique: it is sufficient even without actual use, as per the apparent meaning of the text.
3
Explore intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
Notice the contradictions from al-Khulasa and al-Atabiyya. Some hold that tamkin alone is not enough in certain contexts (e.g., out-of-city travel). Distinguish between in-city and out-of-city scenarios.
This shows that the Hanafi school has nuances within it.
4
Analyze the Shafi'i position and its proof
Imam al-Shafi'i argues that rent is owned immediately by analogy to sale, as ijarah is a commutative contract.
The Shafi'i proof is qiyas on buyu'.
5
Examine the Hanafi response
The Hanafi rebuttal is rational: the benefit is non-existent at contract time, so owning rent immediately would be ownership without a countervalue. Ownership is deferred out of necessity.
This is a dalil aqli (rational proof) based on the nature of benefits.

قال رحمه الله : ( والأجرة لا تملك بالعقد بل بالتعجيل أو بشرطه أو بالاستيفاء أو بالتمكن منه) يعني الأجرة لا تملك بنفس العقد، سواء كانت عيناً أو ديناً، وإنما تملك بالتعجيل أو بشرطه أو باستيفاء المعقود عليه وهي المنفعة، أو بالتمكن من الاستيفاء بتسليم العين المستأجرة في المدة، اهـ كلام الشارح والظاهر من إطلاق الماتن والشارح أن الأجرة تملك بالتمكن من الاستيفاء في المدة، سواء استعملها في المدة ،أو لا، ويخالفه ما في الخلاصة حيث قال : استأجر دابة ليركبها إليها مكان كذا مثلاً فحبسها في بيته لم تجب الأجرة .اهـ. والظاهر من إطلاق المؤلف رحمه الله تعالى أن الأجرة تجب باستيفاء المنفعة، سواء كان ذلك في مدة الإجارة أو بعد مدة الإجارة، وسواء استأجرها ليركبها في المصر أو خارجه. ويخالفه ما ذكره بعض العلماء حيث قال : ولو ذكر مدة ومسافة فركبها إلى ذلك المكان بعد مضي المدة لم تجب الأجرة اهـ. وفي العتابية : هذا إذا استأجرها ليركبها خارج المصر، ولو كان ليركبها في المصر وحبسها في بيته تجب الأجرة. قال في المحيط والتمكن من الاستيفاء في غير المدة المضاف إليها لا يكفي لوجوب الأجرة، وكذا التمكن في غير المكان لا يكفي لوجوب الأجرة، فلو قال رحمه الله تعالى أو بالتمكن منه في المدة واستوفى لكان أولى. وقال الإمام الشافعي: تملك بنفس العقد ويجب تسليمها عند تسليم العين المستأجرة لأنها عقد معاوضة. ولنا أنه عقد معاوضة فيقتضي المساواة بينهما وذلك بتقابل البدلين في الملك والتسليم وأحد البدلين وهو المنفعة لم يصر . مملوكاً بنفس العقد لاستحالة ثبوت الملك في المعدوم. ولو ملك الأجرة لملكها من غير بدل وهو ليس من قضية المعاوضة فتأخر الملك فيه ضرورة جواز العقد لأن المنفعة عوض لا يبقى زمانين، والمنفعة إنما جعلت موجودة في حق الإيجاب والقبول وما ثبت للضرورة يتقدر بقدرها . لا يقال لو لم
He (the author) said: (And the rent is not owned by the contract but by advance payment, or by its condition, or by utilization, or by being enabled to utilize). Meaning: rent is not owned by the mere contract, whether it is a specific thing or a debt; rather, it is owned by advance payment, or by stipulation, or by utilizing the subject matter which is the benefit, or by being enabled to utilize through delivery of the leased property during the term. End of the commentator's words. And the apparent meaning from the absolute wording of the author and the commentator is that rent is owned by being enabled to utilize during the term, whether the lessee actually uses it during the term or not. But what is in al-Khulasa contradicts this, where it says: He hired a donkey to ride to a certain place, for example, then he kept it in his house – rent is not due. End. And the apparent meaning from the absolute wording of the author is that rent is due by utilizing the benefit, whether that occurs during the lease term or after the lease term, and whether he hired it to ride within the city or outside it. But what some scholars mentioned contradicts this: they said: If he specified a period and a distance, and he rode it to that place after the period had passed, rent is not due. End. In al-Atabiyya: This applies if he hired it to ride outside the city; but if he hired it to ride within the city and kept it in his house, rent is due. In al-Muhit: Being enabled to utilize outside the period to which it is added is not sufficient for rent to be due; similarly, being enabled outside the place is not sufficient for rent to be due. So if the author had said 'or by being enabled to utilize during the period and he did utilize', it would have been better. Imam al-Shafi'i said: (Rent) is owned by the mere contract and must be delivered when the leased property is delivered, because it is a commutative contract. Our proof: It is a commutative contract, so it requires equality between the two parties, which necessitates the exchange of two countervalues in ownership and delivery, but one of the two countervalues – the benefit – does not become owned by the mere contract due to the impossibility of establishing ownership over a non-existent thing. If rent were owned (by the contract), it would be owned without a countervalue, which is not required by commutative exchange. Therefore, its ownership is deferred out of necessity for the validity of the contract, because the benefit is a countervalue that does not remain for two time periods, and the benefit is only considered existing for the purpose of offer and acceptance, and that which is established out of necessity is limited to its extent. It cannot be said that...
Source pages p. 7

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute over when the rental payment (ujra) becomes the property of the lessor. The Hanafi position, as stated in the matn, is that rent is not owned by the contract itself but by one of four events: advance payment (ta'jil), stipulation (shart), utilization (istifa') of the benefit, or being enabled (tamkin) to utilize the leased property. The Sharh elaborates on differences within the Hanafi school regarding whether tamkin alone suffices or if actual utilization is required, and whether utilization after the lease term is valid. The commentary mentions specific cases from al-Khulasa and al-Atabiyya that show nuance based on location (in-city vs. out-of-city travel) and timing. Then Imam al-Shafi'i's position is presented: rent is owned immediately upon contract and must be paid upon delivery of the leased asset. The Hanafi response is a rational proof: a commutative contract requires exchange, but the benefit is non-existent at the time of contract, so ownership cannot transfer to the non-existent. If rent were owned immediately, the lessor would receive it without giving anything in return (since the benefit does not exist yet). Thus, rent ownership is deferred out of necessity, limited to the extent required for contract validity. The passage cuts off mid-argument at the page break, but the Hanafi position is clear.

Key Terms
تمكن (tamkin): The lessee being enabled to utilize the leased property during the lease term, even if not actually used
استيفاء (istifa'): Actual utilization of the leased benefit
تعجيل (ta'jil): Advance payment of rent, which is one of the ways rent becomes owned

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the basis for rejecting the Shafi'i view that rent is owned by the contract itself?
A) Because the contract is not valid until the rent is paid
B) Because the benefit is non-existent at contract time, so ownership cannot transfer
C) Because the lessor can cancel the contract anytime
D) Because the lessee must give consent

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, rent is not owned by the contract alone; ownership is triggered by advance payment, stipulation, utilization, or enablement to utilize, reflecting the principle that ownership of a non-existent benefit is impossible.

Ijarah — Hire and Lease
intermediate
15 min
When is the Wage Owned in Ijarah?
States Hanafi ruling on wage ownership and proof

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on when the wage (ujrah) becomes owned in ijarah and explain the rational proof that distinguishes it from the Shafi'i position.

Core Idea
The wage is not owned by contract alone because the benefit is non-existent at formation.

In Hanafi fiqh, the rental wage is not automatically owned upon signing the ijarah contract. Instead, ownership transfers only through one of four mechanisms: advance payment, stipulating advance payment, receipt of the benefit, or ability to receive it. This lesson unpacks the ruling, the rational proof based on the nature of benefit, and the inter-madhhab dispute with Imam al-Shafi'i.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Hanafi ruling and its four triggers
Find the statement that the wage is not owned by the contract alone. Then list the four events that do cause ownership: advance payment, its condition, receipt of benefit, or ability to receive.
The triggers are: al-ta'jil, shart al-ta'jil, al-istifa', al-tamakkan.
2
Understand the rational proof (dalil aqli)
Analyze the argument that a commutative contract requires equality of counter-values. Since the benefit is non-existent at contract time, it cannot be owned, so the wage cannot be owned immediately. The benefit is treated as existent only for contract formation, not for ownership.
Key phrase: 'استحالة ثبوت الملك في المعدوم' (impossibility of establishing ownership of non-existent).
3
Examine the Shafi'i objection and the Hanafi response
State the Shafi'i position: the wage is owned by contract itself, like a sale. Then see how the Hanafi refutes it: immediate ownership would mean owning the wage without a counter-value, violating the commutative nature. The benefit's existence is fictional only for formation.
The Hanafi response uses the principle 'ما ثبت للضرورة يتقدر بقدرها' (what is established by necessity is limited).
4
Consider intra-Hanafi disagreements on related details
Note that Abu Yusuf and Muhammad differ on whether ibra (release) is valid before the wage is owed, and on monthly vs yearly hire. Also consider whether ability to receive alone suffices or only receipt.
For example, Muhammad allows ibra from monthly wage when Ramadan enters; Abu Yusuf requires term to end.
5
Apply the ruling to a practical scenario
Take a scenario: A hires B's car for a month. B demands immediate payment. Under Hanafi, B cannot demand the wage until A uses the car or is able to use it, unless they agreed on advance payment.
The mufta bihi: wage is not owned by contract; details depend on circumstances.

قال رحمه الله: (والأجرة لا تملك بالعقد بل بالتعجيل أو بشرطه أو بالاستيفاء أو بالتمكن منه) يعني الأجرة لا تملك بنفس العقد، سواء كانت عيناً أو ديناً، وإنما تملك بالتعجيل أو بشرطه أو باستيفاء المعقود عليه وهي المنفعة، أو بالتمكن من الاستيفاء بتسليم العين المستأجرة في المدة، اهـ كلام الشارح والظاهر من إطلاق الماتن والشارح أن الأجرة تملك بالتمكن من الاستيفاء في المدة، سواء استعملها في المدة، أو لا، ويخالفه ما في الخلاصة حيث قال : استأجر دابة ليركبها إليها مكان كذا مثلاً فحبسها في بيته لم تجب الأجرة .اهـ. والظاهر من إطلاق المؤلف رحمه الله تعالى أن الأجرة تجب باستيفاء المنفعة، سواء كان ذلك في مدة الإجارة أو بعد مدة الإجارة، وسواء استأجرها ليركبها في المصر أو خارجه. ويخالفه ما ذكره بعض العلماء حيث قال : ولو ذكر مدة ومسافة فركبها إلى ذلك المكان بعد مضي المدة لم تجب الأجرة اهـ. وفي العتابية : هذا إذا استأجرها ليركبها خارج المصر، ولو كان ليركبها في المصر وحبسها في بيته تجب الأجرة. قال في المحيط والتمكن من الاستيفاء في غير المدة المضاف إليها لا يكفي لوجوب الأجرة، وكذا التمكن في غير المكان لا يكفي لوجوب الأجرة، فلو قال رحمه الله تعالى أو بالتمكن منه في المدة واستوفى لكان أولى. وقال الإمام الشافعي: تملك بنفس العقد ويجب تسليمها عند تسليم العين المستأجرة لأنها عقد معاوضة. ولنا أنه عقد معاوضة فيقتضي المساواة بينهما وذلك بتقابل البدلين في الملك والتسليم وأحد البدلين وهو المنفعة لم يصر مملوكاً بنفس العقد لاستحالة ثبوت الملك في المعدوم. ولو ملك الأجرة لملكها من غير بدل وهو ليس من قضية المعاوضة فتأخر الملك فيه ضرورة جواز العقد لأن المنفعة عوض لا يبقى زمانين، والمنفعة إنما جعلت موجودة في حق الإيجاب والقبول وما ثبت للضرورة يتقدر بقدرها . لا يقال لو لم يجعل المعدوم موجوداً في حق العقد والأجرة لما جاز الإيجار بالدين لأنا نقول : إنما جاز الإيجار بالدين لأن العقد لم ينعقد في حق المنفعة فلم يصر ديناً في المدة وإنما ينعقد في حق الارتباط، وعند انعقاد العقد وهو زمان حدوثها تصير هي مقبوضة فلا يكون ديناً بدین أصلاً. ولو كان العقد ينعقد في حق المنفعة لما جازت الإجارة بالدين المؤجل أصلاً كما لا يجوز السلم به، ولو جاز أن يجعل المعدوم كالمستوفي لجاز ذلك في السلم أيضاً. وإذا عجلها أو اشترط تعجيلها فقد التزمه بنفسه وأبطل المساواة التي اقتضاها العقد . قال في العناية : واعترض بأن شرط التعجيل فاسد لأنه يخالف مقتضى العقد وفيه منفعة لأحد المتعاقدين وله مطالب فيفسد العقد. والجواب أن كونه مخالفاً إما أن يكون من حيث كونه إجارة أو من حيث كونه معاوضة، والأول مسلم وليس شرط التعجيل باعتباره والثاني ممنوع فإن تعجيل البدل واشتراطه لا يخالف من حيث المعاوضة. وفي المحيط : وحينئذ فللمؤجر حبس المنافع حتى يستوفي الأجرة ويطالبه بها ويحبسه وحقه الفسخ أن الحاكم يعجل .اهـ. ولو أجر إجارة مضافة واشترط تعجيل الأجرة حيث يكون الشرط باطلاً ولا يلزم للحال شيء لأن امتناع وجوب الأجرة ليس بمقتضى العقد بل بالتصريح بالإضافة إلى وقت في المستقبل، والمضاف إلى وقت لا يكون موجوداً قبل ذلك الوقت فلا يتغير هذا المعنى بالشرط، وفيما نحن فيه إنما لا يجب لاقتضاء العقد المساواة وقد بطل بالتصريح، لا يقال يصح الإبراء عن الأجرة بعد العقد ولو لم يملكها لما صح . بها، وهذا لو تزوج امرأة بسكنى داره سنة وسلم ليس لها أن تمنع نفسها ولو لم تملك المنفعة لمنعت نفسها لأنا نقول : لا يصح الإبراء عن الثاني لعدم وجوبه كالمضاف بخلاف الدين المؤجل لأنه ثابت في الذمة فجاز الإبراء عنه والجواب على قول محمد أنه وجد سبيه فجاز الإبراء عنه كالإبراء عن القصاص بعد الجرح والرهن والكفالة للوثيقة فلا يشترط فيه حقيقة الوجوب، ألا ترى أنهما جائزان في البيع المشروط فيه الخيار وبالدين الموعود وجازت الكفالة بالدرك. وإنما لم يكن للمرأة أن تحبس نفسها بعد تسليم الدار إليها لأنه أوفى ما سمى لها برضاها . وكذا يصح الارتهان والكفالة وفي المحيط ولو وهب المؤجر أجرة رمضان هل يجوز؟ قال محمد: إن استأجره سنة لا يجوز، وإن استأجره مشاهرة يجوز إذا دخل رمضان ولا يجوز قبله. وعن أبي يوسف لا يجوز إلا بعد مضي المدة، ولو مضى من السنة نصفها ثم أبرأه عن الجميع أو وهبها منه فإنه يبرأ عن الكل في قول محمد، وعند أبي يوسف بريء عن النصف لا يبرأ عن النصف اهـ .. وعبر المؤلف بقوله لا تملك لأن لفظ محمد في الجامع الأجرة لا تملك بنفس العقد. قال صاحب النهاية : الأجرة لا تجب بالعقد معناه لا يجب تسليمها وأداؤها بمجرد العقد وليس بواضح لأن نفي وجوب التسليم لا يستلزم نفي الملك كالمبيع فإنه يملكه المشتري بمجرد العقد ولا يجب تسليمه ما لم يقبض الثمن والصواب أن يقال : معناه لا تملك لأن محمداً ذكر في الجامع الصغير أن الأجرة لا تملك وما لا يملك لا يجب ايفاؤه . فإن قلت : فإذا لم يستلزم
He (the author) said, may Allah have mercy on him: '(And the wage is not owned by the contract, but by advance payment, or by its condition, or by receipt, or by ability to receive)' meaning the wage is not owned by the contract itself, whether it is a specific object or a debt. It is only owned by advance payment, or by its condition, or by receipt of the contracted thing, which is the benefit, or by ability to receive by delivery of the leased object within the term. End of the commentator's speech. And the apparent meaning from the absolute expression of the matn and the commentator is that the wage is owned by ability to receive within the term, whether he uses it within the term or not. This is contradicted by what is in al-Khulasa where he said: He hired an animal to ride to a certain place, and he detained it in his house, the wage is not due. The apparent meaning from the absolute expression of the author, may Allah have mercy on him, is that the wage is due by the receipt of the benefit, whether that is within the lease term or after the lease term, and whether he hired it to ride inside the city or outside. This is contradicted by what some scholars mentioned, who said: If he specified a term and a distance, and he rode it to that place after the term passed, the wage is not due. And in al-'Atabiyya: This is if he hired it to ride outside the city; if he hired it to ride inside the city and detained it in his house, the wage is due. He said in al-Muhit: Ability to receive outside the term attached to it is not sufficient to make the wage obligatory, and similarly ability to receive in a different place is not sufficient to make the wage obligatory. So if he (the author) had said 'or by ability to receive within the term and receipt' it would be better. And Imam al-Shafi'i said: It is owned by the contract itself, and it must be delivered upon delivery of the leased object because it is a commutative contract. And we have: It is a commutative contract, so it necessitates equality between them, and that is by the mutuality of the two counter-values in ownership and delivery, and one of the counter-values, which is the benefit, does not become owned by the contract itself because it is impossible to establish ownership of a non-existent thing. And if he owned the wage, he would own it without a counter-value, and that is not from the requirement of commutation. So ownership is delayed out of necessity for the validity of the contract because the benefit is a counter-value that does not persist for two moments. The benefit is only treated as existent for the purpose of offer and acceptance, and what is established by necessity is limited to its extent. It cannot be said: If the non-existent is not treated as existent for the contract and the wage, then hiring for a debt would not be valid. We say: It is only valid because the contract is not concluded in respect of the benefit, so it does not become a debt in the term; it is only concluded in respect of the linkage, and at the conclusion of the contract, which is the time of its occurrence, it becomes received, so it is not a debt for a debt at all. And if the contract were concluded in respect of the benefit, then hiring for a deferred debt would not be valid at all, just as salam is not valid with it. And if it were permissible to treat the non-existent as received, it would also be permissible in salam. And if he advances payment or stipulates its advancement, he has committed himself and voided the equality that the contract required. He said in al-'Inaya: An objection is raised: the condition of advance payment is invalid because it contradicts the requirement of the contract and contains a benefit for one of the two contracting parties and he has a claim, so it invalidates the contract. The answer: its being contradictory is either in respect of its being an ijarah or in respect of its being a commutation; the first is accepted, and the condition of advance payment is not considered under it, and the second is rejected, for accelerating the counter-value and stipulating it does not contradict from the perspective of commutation. And in al-Muhit: Then the lessor has the right to withhold the benefits until he receives the wage, and he can demand it and detain him, and his right is to rescind that the judge should expedite. And if he made a forward ijarah and stipulated advance payment of the wage, the condition is invalid and nothing is due immediately because the prevention of the obligation of the wage is not due to the contract's requirement but due to explicit stipulation of addition to a future time, and what is added to a time does not exist before that time, so this meaning is not changed by the condition. And in our case, it is not due because the contract requires equality, and that has been voided by explicit stipulation. It cannot be said that the release from the wage after the contract is valid, and if he did not own it, it would not be valid. And this is like if a man marries a woman on the condition of residing in his house for a year and he delivers it, she does not have the right to withhold herself; if she did not own the benefit, she would withhold herself. We say: The release from the second is not valid because it is not due, like the forward; unlike a deferred debt because it is established in the liability, so release from it is valid. And the answer according to Muhammad is that cause exists, so release is valid, like release from qisas after injury, and pledge and suretyship for documentation; actual obligation is not a condition. Do you not see that they are both valid in a sale with an option and in a promised debt, and suretyship for defects is valid. And the woman's inability to withhold herself after delivery of the house to her is because he has fulfilled what he named for her with her consent. And similarly, pledging and suretyship are valid. And in al-Muhit: If the lessor grants the wage of Ramadan, is it permissible? Muhammad said: If he rented it for a year, it is not permissible; if he rented it monthly, it is permissible when Ramadan enters, and not before. From Abu Yusuf, it is not permissible except after the term passes. And if half the year passes and then he released him from the whole or granted it to him, he is released from the whole according to Muhammad; according to Abu Yusuf, he is released from half, not from the other half. And the author expressed 'not owned' because Muhammad's wording in al-Jami' is 'the wage is not owned by the contract itself.' The author of al-Nihaya said: 'The wage is not due by the contract' means it is not obligatory to deliver and pay it by the mere contract. And this is not clear because the negation of obligation of delivery does not entail negation of ownership, like the sold item, which the buyer owns by the contract itself but its delivery is not obligatory until he receives the price. The correct answer is: It means not owned because Muhammad mentioned in al-Jami' al-Saghir that the wage is not owned, and what is not owned is not obligatory to deliver. If you say: If it does not entail...
Source pages p. 7

Commentary
This passage contains the Hanafi ruling on when the wage (ujrah) becomes owned in an ijarah contract. The author states that the wage is not owned by the mere contract; it is owned by one of four things: (1) advance payment (ta'jil), (2) stipulating advance payment (shart al-ta'jil), (3) receipt of the benefit (istifa'), or (4) ability to receive the benefit (tamakkan). The commentator then explores the nuances. He notes that the apparent meaning of the matn and commentary is that ability to receive within the term makes the wage owed, even if the lessee does not actually use the asset. However, he cites a contrary view from al-Khulasa that if the lessee detains the animal at home, the wage is not due. Further, there is disagreement on whether receipt after the term or outside the locale makes the wage due. The commentator suggests the author should have specified 'or by ability to receive within the term and receipt.' Then comes the Shafi'i objection: the wage is owned by the contract itself, just as in a sale. The Hanafi response is detailed: a commutative contract requires equality, but the benefit is non-existent at contract time; owning the wage immediately would mean owning it without a counter-value. The benefit is treated as existent only by necessity for the contract's formation, and necessity is limited. The passage also discusses the validity of a condition for advance payment (it does not invalidate the contract because it does not violate the commutative nature), and various intra-Hanafi issues: (a) whether a forward ijarah with stipulation of advance payment is valid (the condition is invalid due to the forward nature), (b) the validity of ibra' (release) from the wage before it is owed—Muhammad and Abu Yusuf differ on whether ibra' is valid when the wage is not yet owned, with analogies to qisas and suretyship, and (c) the permissibility of gifting the wage of Ramadan in monthly vs annual hire. The passage concludes with a note on the correct wording: the wage is not 'owned' by contract, not just 'not due'. This lesson covers a core Hanafi principle with extensive debate and application.

Key Terms
الأجرة (al-ujrah): The wage or rental payment in an ijarah contract.
المنفعة (al-manfa'ah): The benefit that is the object of the ijarah.
التعجيل (al-ta'jil): Payment of the wage in advance.
الاستيفاء (al-istifa'): Receipt of the benefit.
التمكن (al-tamakkan): Ability to receive the benefit.
الإبراء (al-ibra'): Release from debt.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the primary reason the wage (ujrah) is not owned by the ijarah contract alone?
A) Because the contract is not valid unless payment is made
B) Because the benefit (manfa'ah) is non-existent at the time of contract
C) Because the lessor has the right to withhold the asset
D) Because the wage must be paid in advance by custom

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, the wage in ijarah is not owned by the contract alone; it becomes owned only by advance payment, its condition, receipt of benefit, or ability to receive, due to the non-existence of the benefit at contract formation.

Validity of Hire Against Debt and Condition of Prompt Payment
Hire against debt and prompt payment condition

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi school permits hire against a debt and evaluate the validity of a condition requiring prompt payment of the hire fee.

Core Idea
Hire against debt is valid because the benefit is not a debt at contract; a prompt payment condition is valid as it does not contradict the exchange.

This passage from Al-Bahr al-Raiq addresses two important issues in Hanafi ijarah law: hiring against a debt and stipulating prompt payment. The author begins by justifying the permissibility of hire against a debt by clarifying that the contract does not transfer ownership of the benefit at the moment of contract—it is merely a binding promise. He then defends the validity of a condition requiring immediate payment, countering the objection that such a condition contradicts the nature of hire. The discussion reveals the Hanafi emphasis on the commutative essence of the contract over its hire-specific features.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two rulings
Locate the two core issues in the passage: (1) whether hire against a debt is permissible, and (2) whether a condition of prompt payment is valid and whether it affects the contract.
Both rulings are defended against hypothetical objections.
2
Analyze the reasoning for hire against debt
Examine why the author says hire against a debt is allowed. The key premise: the contract does not create a debt of benefit at the moment of contract; it is only a binding promise. Therefore, it is not a sale of a non-existent item.
Contrast with salam, where the item sold is non-existent at contract.
3
Analyze the objection and response for prompt payment
Read the objection: the condition of prompt payment contradicts the nature of hire and benefits one party, thus invalidating the contract. The response distinguishes between the contract as a hire (where delayed payment is usual) and as a commutative exchange (where prompt payment is neutral). The condition does not harm the exchange aspect.
The refutation relies on analyzing the contract in two dimensions.
4
Explore sub-rulings
Note the additional rulings: the lessor may withhold benefits until payment, and in a future hire, a prompt payment condition is void because nothing is due yet. Also note the discussion on exemption from hire fee before it is due, drawing analogy to marriage dower and security contracts.
These illustrate the practical implications of the core principles.
5
Summarize the Hanafi position
Conclude that the Hanafi school upholds the validity of hire against debt and the condition of prompt payment, and the contract remains sound. The thamarah al-khilaf (practical difference) is that a contrary view would render the contract corrupt.
This is the mufta bihi position in the later Hanafi tradition.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الإجارة
يجعل المعدوم موجوداً في حق العقد والأجرة لما جاز الإيجار بالدين لأنا نقول : إنما جاز الإيجار بالدين لأن العقد لم ينعقد في حق المنفعة فلم يصر ديناً في المدة وإنما ينعقد في حق الارتباط، وعند انعقاد العقد وهو زمان حدوثها تصير هي مقبوضة فلا يكون ديناً بدین أصلاً. ولو كان العقد ينعقد في حق المنفعة لما جازت الإجارة بالدين المؤجل أصلاً كما لا يجوز السلم به، ولو جاز أن يجعل المعدوم كالمستوفي لجاز ذلك في السلم أيضاً. وإذا عجلها أو اشترط تعجيلها فقد التزمه بنفسه وأبطل المساواة التي اقتضاها العقد . قال في العناية : واعترض بأن شرط التعجيل فاسد لأنه يخالف مقتضى العقد وفيه منفعة لأحد المتعاقدين وله مطالب فيفسد العقد. والجواب أن كونه مخالفاً إما أن يكون من حيث كونه إجارة أو من حيث كونه معاوضة، والأول مسلم وليس شرط التعجيل باعتباره والثاني ممنوع فإن تعجيل البدل واشتراطه لا يخالف من حيث المعاوضة. وفي المحيط : وحينئذ فللمؤجر حبس المنافع حتى يستوفي الأجرة ويطالبه بها ويحبسه وحقه الفسخ أن الحاكم يعجل .اهـ. ولو أجر إجارة مضافة واشترط تعجيل الأجرة حيث يكون الشرط باطلاً ولا يلزم للحال شيء لأن امتناع وجوب الأجرة ليس بمقتضى العقد بل بالتصريح بالإضافة إلى وقت في المستقبل، والمضاف إلى وقت لا يكون موجوداً قبل ذلك الوقت فلا يتغير هذا المعنى بالشرط، وفيما نحن فيه إنما لا يجب لاقتضاء العقد المساواة وقد بطل بالتصريح، لا يقال يصح الإبراء عن الأجرة بعد العقد ولو لم يملكها لما صـ صح . بها، وهذا لو تزوج امرأة بسكنى داره سنة وسلم ليس لها أن تمنع نفسها ولو لم تملك المنفعة لمنعت نفسها لأنا نقول : لا يصح الإبراء عن الثاني لعدم وجوبه كالمضاف بخلاف الدين المؤجل لأنه ثابت في الذمة فجاز الإبراء عنه والجواب على قول محمد أنه وجد سبيه فجاز الإبراء عنه كالإبراء عن القصاص بعد الجرح والرهن والكفالة للوثيقة فلا يشترط فيه حقيقة الوجوب، ألا ترى أنهما جائزان في البيع المشروط فيه الخيار وبالدين الموعود وجازت الكفالة بالدرك. وإنما لم يكن للمرأة أن تحبس نفسها بعد تسليم الدار إليها لأنه أوفى ما سمى لها برضاها .
Book of Hire. Making non-existent existent with respect to the contract and the hire fee, since hire against debt is permitted. We say: Hire against debt is only permitted because the contract is not concluded with respect to the benefit, so it does not become a debt during the period; it is only concluded with respect to the binding obligation. At the conclusion of the contract, which is the time of its occurrence, the benefit becomes received, so it is not a debt against a debt at all. If the contract were concluded with respect to the benefit, then hire against deferred debt would not be permitted at all, just as salam is not permitted against it. And if it were permissible to make non-existent like received, then that would also be permitted in salam. And if he pays promptly or stipulates prompt payment, then he has committed himself and nullified the equality required by the contract. In al-‘Inayah: An objection was raised that the condition of prompt payment is invalid because it contradicts the requirement of the contract and benefits one party, and thus invalidates the contract. The answer: That it is contradictory either with respect to it being a hire or with respect to it being a commutative exchange. The first is admitted, but the condition of prompt payment is not considered in that regard; the second is denied, because prompt payment of the substitute and stipulating it does not contradict the commutative aspect. In al-Muhit: Then the lessor has the right to withhold the benefits until he receives the hire fee, and he may demand it and imprison him, and he has the right of rescission if the judge accelerates it. End. If he gave a future hire contract and stipulated prompt payment of the hire fee, the condition is void and nothing is due immediately, because the non-obligation of the hire fee is not a requirement of the contract but due to express addition to a future time, and what is added to a time does not exist before that time, so this meaning does not change with the condition. In our current case, it is not due because the contract requires equality, and that has been nullified by express stipulation. It should not be said that exemption from the hire fee after the contract is valid even if he does not own it, because he [؟] . And this is like if a man marries a woman in exchange for residing in his house for a year, and he hands it over, she cannot restrain herself, even if she does not own the benefit, she would restrain herself. We say: Exemption from the second is not valid because it is not obligatory, like the future contract, unlike deferred debt because it is established in the dhimmah, so exemption from it is valid. The answer according to Muhammad: It is a cause, so exemption from it is valid, like exemption from retaliation after wounds, and pledge and guarantee as security, so true obligation is not required in it. Do you not see that both are valid in sale with a condition of option and with promised debt, and guarantee of liability is valid. And the woman could not restrain herself after handing over the house to her because he fulfilled what he named with her consent.
Source pages p. 8

Commentary
This passage opens a discussion on the nature of the hire contract. The author explains why it is permissible to hire against a debt, contrary to a hypothetical objection. The key point is that the contract does not establish ownership of the benefit at the moment of the contract; it is a binding promise. Therefore, it is not a sale of a non-existent item. Then the condition of prompt payment is discussed: the objection that this condition is invalid because it contradicts the nature of hire is refuted by distinguishing between the contract as a hire and as a commutative exchange. The condition only concerns the timing of payment, which does not harm the exchange aspect. Various sub-rulings are given, including hire with future commencement and the permissibility of exemption from the fee before it is due, with an analogy to marriage dower. The passage also touches on the right of the lessor to withhold benefits until payment.

Key Terms
الإجارة (al-ijarah): A contract for the use of a benefit in exchange for a payment (ujrah).
الإيجار بالدين (al-ijar bi al-dayn): Hiring something in exchange for a debt (deferred payment).
التعجيل (al-ta'jil): Prompt payment of the hire fee at the time of contract.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, why is it permissible to hire against a debt (al-ijar bi al-dayn)?
A) Because the benefit is treated as existing at the time of contract.
B) Because the contract does not establish ownership of the benefit at the time of contract; it is a binding promise.
C) Because the debt is already owed, so it cancels out.
D) Because the hire fee is not considered a debt at all.

Key Takeaway
Hire against a debt is valid because the benefit is not a debt at the moment of contract, and a condition of prompt payment is valid because it does not contradict the commutative essence of the exchange.
