Ijarah — Hire and Lease
intermediate
8 min
The Hire Fee is Not Owned by Contract Alone
Ruling with proof on hire fee ownership and rebuttal of the sale analogy.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on ownership of the hire fee and explain why the fee is not owned by the contract alone.

Core Idea
The hire fee is not owned by contract; ownership requires actual receipt or empowerment.

This passage from Al-Bahr al-Raiq establishes a fundamental distinction between sale and hire: in sale, ownership transfers by contract, but in hire, the fee is not owned until the lessor receives it or is empowered to receive it. This distinction affects many subsidiary rulings, including the validity of exemption (ibra') and the lessor's right to demand payment. Let us walk through the evidence and reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling on hire fee ownership
The author states that the hire fee is not owned by the contract alone. This is the core ruling derived from Imam Muhammad's statement in Al-Jami' al-Saghir.
The wording 'la tumlak' (not owned) is crucial.
2
Examine the proof from Muhammad's statement
Imam Muhammad explicitly said 'the hire fee is not owned by the contract itself.' This is the primary textual proof (dalil) for the ruling.
The statement is from Al-Jami' al-Saghir, a source of Zahir al-Riwayah.
3
Analyze the objection based on analogy with sale
An opponent argues that negating obligation (la tajib) does not necessarily negate ownership, as in sale where ownership is established by contract even before delivery.
This objection is answered by showing that Muhammad intended non-ownership.
4
Understand the Hanafi response
The correct interpretation is that 'la tajib' means 'la tumlak' (not owned). The author of Al-Nihayah explains that if the fee were owned, it would be obligatory to deliver, but since it is not owned, its fulfillment is not obligatory. Also, the general term 'obligation' is not used to mean 'ownership' specifically.
The response clarifies the linguistic and legal point.
5
Note the consequence
Since the hire fee is not owned by contract, the lessor cannot demand payment until the lessee actually receives the benefit or is empowered (tamakkun) to receive it.
This has practical implications for when rent becomes due.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وكذا يصح الارتهان والكفالة وفي المحيط ولو وهب المؤجر أجرة رمضان هل يجوز؟ قال محمد: إن استأجره سنة لا يجوز، وإن استأجره مشاهرة يجوز إذا دخل رمضان ولا يجوز قبله. وعن أبي يوسف لا يجوز إلا بعد مضي المدة، ولو مضى من السنة نصفها ثم أبرأه عن الجميع أو وهبها منه فإنه يبرأ عن الكل في قول محمد، وعند أبي يوسف بريء عن النصف لا يبرأ عن النصف اهـ .. وعبر المؤلف بقوله لا تملك لأن لفظ محمد في الجامع الأجرة لا تملك بنفس العقد. قال صاحب النهاية : الأجرة لا تجب بالعقد معناه لا يجب تسليمها وأداؤها بمجرد العقد وليس بواضح لأن نفي وجوب التسليم لا يستلزم نفي الملك كالمبيع فإنه يملكه المشتري بمجرد العقد ولا يجب تسليمه ما لم يقبض الثمن والصواب أن يقال : معناه لا تملك لأن محمداً ذكر في الجامع الصغير أن الأجرة لا تملك وما لا يملك لا يجب ايفاؤه . فإن قلت : فإذا لم يستلزم نفي الوجوب نفي الملك كان أعم منه وذكر العام وإرادة الخاص ليس بمجاز شائع لعدم دلالة الأعم على الأخص أصلاً. وقال صاحب الهداية : الأجرة لا تجب بالعقد. قال تاج الشريعة : أي وجوب الأداء، أما نفس الوجوب فيثبت بنفس العقد. وقال صاحب الكفالة؛ المراد نفس الوجوب لا الأداء وبيان ذلك إجمالاً وتفصيلاً. أما إجمالاً فلأن الأجرة لو كانت عبداً وجوب فأعتقه المؤجر قبل وجود أحد المعاني الثلاثة لا يعتق، فلو كان نفس الوجوب ثابتاً لصح الإعتاق كما في البيع .اهـ. وإذا لم يتملك بنفس العقد ليس له أن يطالبه بالأجرة. وفي المحيط : لو طالبه بالأجرة عيناً وقبض جاز لتضمينه تعجيل الأجرة. وقال أيضاً: وإذا لم يوجد أحد هذه الأمور يأخذ الأجرة يوماً فيوماً في العقار، وفي المسافات كل مرحلة. وفي المنتقى : رجل استأجر دابة بالكوفة إلى الري بدراهم أي النقدين يجب على المستأجر ـ قال - نقد الكوفة لأنه مكان العقد فينصرف مطلق الدراهم إلى المتعارف فيها. وفي العتابية : وإذا عجل الأجرة إلى ربها لا يملك الاسترداد، ولو كانت الأجرة عيناً فأعارها ثم أودعها إلى رب الدار فهو كالتعجيل اهـ. وفي شرح الطحاوي: الأجرة لا تخلو إما أن تكون معجلة أو مؤجلة أو منجمة أو مسكوتاً عنها فإن كانت معجلة فإن له أن يتملكها وله أن يطالب بها، وإن كانت مؤجلة فليس له أن يطالب إلا بعد الأجل، وإن كانت منجمة فله أن يطالب عند كل نجم، وإن كانت مسكوتاً عنها تقدم بيان ذلك في العقار وفي المسافة إذا امتنع من الحمل فيما بقي يجبر عليه اهـ بالمعنى. وفي النسفية : استأجر حانوتاً مدة معلومة بأجرة معلومة وسكن . فخرب الحانوت في بعض المدة وتعطل وكان يمكنه الانتقال فلم يفعل وسكن المدة تلزمه جميع الأجرة، ولو استأجره ليحمل هذا إلى موضع كذا فحمل نصف الطريق وأعاده إلى مكانه الأول فلا أجر له استأجر دابة إلى مكة فلم يركبها ومضى راجلاً، إن كان بغير عذر في الدابة فعليه الأجرة، وإن كان لعذر في الدابة لا أجر عليه طالبه بالأجرة بعد المدة فقال قصرت في العمل فلك بعض الأجرة وقال لم أقصر فله الأجرة كاملة. استأجره ليحمل له العصير فحمله فإذا هو خمر قال أبو يوسف : لا أجر له. وقال محمد: إن علم أنه خمر فلا أجر له، وإن لم يعلم فله الأجر. وفي الذخيرة من الفصل السابع والعشرين في الاختلاف: لو اختلف المستأجر والآجر بعد شهر والمفتاح مع المستأجر وقال لم أقدر على فتحه وقال المؤجر بل قدرت على فتحه وسكنت ولا بينة لهما يحكم الحال، وإن أقاما بينة فالبينة بينة رب المنزل اهـ. وفي القنية : تسليم المفتاح في المصر مع التخلية ،قبض، وفي السواد ليس بقبض. وفي فتاوى الولوالجي : ولو استأجر داراً على عبد بعينه ثم وهب العبد من المستأجر قبل القبض وقال المستأجر قبلت كان ذلك إقالة. ومراد المصنف الإجارة المنجزة لأن المضافة لا تملك الأجرة فيها بشرط التعجيل. وقوله أو بالاستيفاء أو بالتمكن منه يعني يجب الاستيفاء للمنفعة أو بالتمكن وإن لم يستوف . وفي الهداية : وإذا قبض المستأجر الدار فعليه الأجرة وإن لم يسكن .
And similarly, pledging and guaranteeing are valid. In al-Muhit: If the lessor gifted the hire fee of Ramadan, is it permissible? Muhammad said: If he hired for a year, it is not permissible; if he hired monthly, it is permissible when Ramadan enters, and not before. From Abu Yusuf: It is not permissible except after the period has passed. If half of the year passed, then he exempted him from the whole or gifted it to him, he is exempt from all in Muhammad's view, and according to Abu Yusuf, he is exempt from half, not exempt from half. End. The author expressed by saying 'does not own' because the wording of Muhammad in al-Jami' is 'the hire fee is not owned by the contract itself'. The author of al-Nihayah said: 'The hire fee is not obligated by the contract' means its delivery and payment are not obligated solely by the contract. It is not clear because negating the obligation of delivery does not necessitate negating ownership, like the sold item: the buyer owns it by the contract alone, but its delivery is not obligatory until he pays the price. The correct thing is to say: it means it is not owned, because Muhammad mentioned in al-Jami' al-Saghir that the hire fee is not owned, and what is not owned, its fulfillment is not obligatory. If you say: since negating obligation does not necessitate negating ownership, it is more general, and mentioning the general while intending the specific is not a common metaphor because the general does not indicate the specific at all. The author of al-Hidayah said: The hire fee is not obligated by the contract. Taj al-Shari'ah said: That is, the obligation of performance; but the obligation itself is established by the contract itself. The author of al-Kifalah said: What is meant is the obligation itself, not performance. Explanation in summary and detail. In summary: if the hire fee were a slave that is obligatory, and the lessor freed him before the occurrence of one of the three meanings, he would not be freed; if the obligation itself were established, the freeing would be valid as in sale. End. And if he does not own by the contract itself, he cannot demand the hire fee from him. In al-Muhit: If he demanded the hire fee in cash and received it, it is permissible because it implies prompt payment. He also said: If none of these matters exist, he takes the hire fee day by day in real estate, and in distances, each stage. In al-Muntaqa: A man hired an animal from Kufa to Rayy for dirhams (one of the two currencies); the obligatory currency for the hirer—he said—is the currency of Kufa because it is the place of the contract, so absolute dirhams refer to the customary there. In al-‘Utbiyah: If he paid the hire fee promptly to its owner, he cannot reclaim it; and if the hire fee was a specific item, and he lent it then deposited it with the landlord, it is like prompt payment. End. In Sharh al-Tahawi: The hire fee is either prompt, deferred, in installments, or not mentioned; if prompt, he may own it and demand it; if deferred, he cannot demand except after the term; if installments, he may demand at each installment; if not mentioned, the explanation has preceded for real estate and for distance if he refrains from carrying what remains, he is compelled to. End (paraphrased). In al-Nasafiyyah: He hired a shop for a known period for a known fee and lived in it. The shop collapsed during part of the period and became useless, and he could have moved but did not, and lived through the period, so the full fee is obligatory. If he hired him to carry this to a certain place, and he carried half the way and returned it to its original place, he has no fee. If he hired an animal to Mecca and did not ride it and went on foot; if without an excuse concerning the animal, the fee is upon him; if there was an excuse concerning the animal, there is no fee. If he demanded the fee after the period and said 'I fell short in the work, so you have some fee,' and he said 'I did not fall short,' so he has the full fee. He hired him to carry grape juice, and he carried it and it turned out to be wine. Abu Yusuf said: He has no fee. Muhammad said: If he knew it was wine, he has no fee; if he did not know, he has the fee. In al-Dhakhirah from the twenty-seventh chapter on disagreement: If the hirer and the lessor disagree after a month, and the key is with the hirer, and he said 'I could not open it' and the lessor said 'You could open it and lived in it,' and there is no evidence for either, the current state is judged. If they produce evidence, the evidence of the landlord is preferred. End. In al-Qunyah: Delivery of the key in the city with vacating is possession; in the rural area, it is not possession. In Fatawa al-Walwaliji: If he hired a house for a specific slave, then the lessor gifted the slave to the hirer before possession, and the hirer said 'I accept,' that is a rescission. What the author means is immediate hire, because for future hire, the fee is not owned with the condition of prompt payment. And his saying 'or by actual receipt or by empowerment' means the benefit is obligated by actual receipt or by empowerment even if he did not actually receive. In al-Hidayah: If the hirer takes possession of the house, the fee is upon him even if he does not reside.
Source pages p. 8

Commentary
This passage continues the discussion on the hire fee. It begins with a brief note on the validity of pledging and guaranteeing in conjunction with hire. Then it presents a dispute between Imam Muhammad and Imam Abu Yusuf regarding the exemption (hiba or ibra) from hire fee for a specific month. The crux is whether the fee is owned by the contract. The author explains that according to Muhammad, the hire fee is not owned by the contract alone. This is supported by the statement from al-Jami' al-Saghir. There is a discussion on whether 'la tajib' means no obligation to deliver or no ownership. The correct interpretation is that the fee is not owned. Consequently, the lessor cannot demand the fee until actual receipt or empowerment. Various cases are then cited from authoritative texts: types of hire fee (immediate, deferred, installments), the obligation when the property is destroyed, hire of animals, disputes over possession, delivery of keys, etc. The passage concludes with a clarification that the author refers to immediate hire (al-ijarah al-munajjazah) and that for future hire (al-mudhafah) with condition of prompt payment, the ruling differs.

Key Terms
الإبراء (al-ibra'): Exemption from a debt or obligation, here the hire fee.
الوجوب (al-wujub): Obligation; here distinguished between obligation of performance (wujub al-ada') and obligation of existence (wujub al-dhimmah).
التمكن (al-tamakkun): Empowerment or ability to take possession of the benefit.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, the statement 'the hire fee is not obligated by the contract' (la tajib) means:
A) The fee is never owed.
B) The fee is not owned by contract, and ownership requires receipt.
C) The fee is owned but not payable.
D) The fee is both owned and payable by contract.

Key Takeaway
The hire fee is not owned by the contract alone; ownership requires actual receipt or empowerment, distinguishing hire from sale.

Exemption from Hire Fee and Practical Cases
Expansion on the ruling of exemption (ibra') and various practical cases in hire.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rulings on exemption from hire fee in monthly vs yearly contracts and distinguish the positions of Muhammad and Abu Yusuf.

Core Idea
Exemption from hire fee is valid only when the fee is owned; in monthly hire, after the month begins, but in yearly hire, only after the year ends.

This passage continues by examining the validity of exempting the lessee from hire fee before the full period. The dispute between Muhammad and Abu Yusuf hinges on when the fee becomes owned. Practical cases like destruction of property, hire of animals, and disputes over possession illustrate the application of these rules. Let us analyze the key points.

Guided Path
1
Identify the types of hire: monthly vs yearly
The passage distinguishes between monthly (mushaharah) and yearly (sanah) hire contracts for the purpose of exemption.
This distinction is crucial for the dispute.
2
Understand Muhammad's view on ibra'
Muhammad holds that in monthly hire, exemption is valid when the month has begun (e.g., Ramadan), but not before. In yearly hire, exemption is not valid until the entire year has passed. If half the year passed and he exempts the whole, he is exempt from all according to Muhammad.
Muhammad considers monthly installments as owned gradually.
3
Understand Abu Yusuf's view
Abu Yusuf holds that exemption is not valid until after the entire period has passed, regardless of monthly or yearly. Thus, exemption after half a year only covers half.
Abu Yusuf does not recognize partial ownership during the period.
4
Apply the ruling to the case of partial period
The passage gives an example: if half of a yearly hire has passed and the lessor exempts the whole, Muhammad says the lessee is free from all (since the passed half is owned and the future half is not yet owed? Actually, Muhammad's view is that exemption is valid for the whole because the fee is not owned in advance, so exemption releases from future obligation? This needs careful reading. The text says: 'If half of the year passed, then he exempted him from the whole or gifted it to him, he is exempt from all in Muhammad's view.' This seems to indicate that exemption is valid for the entire remaining amount because the fee is not yet owned, so the debt is not yet established. However, Abu Yusuf says he is exempt from half only, meaning the fee for the passed half is owned and can be exempted.
The difference turns on whether the fee is owned piecemeal.
5
Distinguish other cases
The passage lists many cases: shop collapse (full rent if tenant could have moved but didn't), hire of animal (no fee if not used due to animal's excuse), carriage of wine (fee depends on knowledge), disputes over possession (key delivery). Each case applies the general principle that fee is due when benefit is actually received or empowered.
These cases illustrate the flexibility of the rule.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وكذا يصح الارتهان والكفالة وفي المحيط ولو وهب المؤجر أجرة رمضان هل يجوز؟ قال محمد: إن استأجره سنة لا يجوز، وإن استأجره مشاهرة يجوز إذا دخل رمضان ولا يجوز قبله. وعن أبي يوسف لا يجوز إلا بعد مضي المدة، ولو مضى من السنة نصفها ثم أبرأه عن الجميع أو وهبها منه فإنه يبرأ عن الكل في قول محمد، وعند أبي يوسف بريء عن النصف لا يبرأ عن النصف اهـ .. وعبر المؤلف بقوله لا تملك لأن لفظ محمد في الجامع الأجرة لا تملك بنفس العقد. قال صاحب النهاية : الأجرة لا تجب بالعقد معناه لا يجب تسليمها وأداؤها بمجرد العقد وليس بواضح لأن نفي وجوب التسليم لا يستلزم نفي الملك كالمبيع فإنه يملكه المشتري بمجرد العقد ولا يجب تسليمه ما لم يقبض الثمن والصواب أن يقال : معناه لا تملك لأن محمداً ذكر في الجامع الصغير أن الأجرة لا تملك وما لا يملك لا يجب ايفاؤه . فإن قلت : فإذا لم يستلزم نفي الوجوب نفي الملك كان أعم منه وذكر العام وإرادة الخاص ليس بمجاز شائع لعدم دلالة الأعم على الأخص أصلاً. وقال صاحب الهداية : الأجرة لا تجب بالعقد. قال تاج الشريعة : أي وجوب الأداء، أما نفس الوجوب فيثبت بنفس العقد. وقال صاحب الكفالة؛ المراد نفس الوجوب لا الأداء وبيان ذلك إجمالاً وتفصيلاً. أما إجمالاً فلأن الأجرة لو كانت عبداً وجوب فأعتقه المؤجر قبل وجود أحد المعاني الثلاثة لا يعتق، فلو كان نفس الوجوب ثابتاً لصح الإعتاق كما في البيع .اهـ. وإذا لم يتملك بنفس العقد ليس له أن يطالبه بالأجرة. وفي المحيط : لو طالبه بالأجرة عيناً وقبض جاز لتضمينه تعجيل الأجرة. وقال أيضاً: وإذا لم يوجد أحد هذه الأمور يأخذ الأجرة يوماً فيوماً في العقار، وفي المسافات كل مرحلة. وفي المنتقى : رجل استأجر دابة بالكوفة إلى الري بدراهم أي النقدين يجب على المستأجر ـ قال - نقد الكوفة لأنه مكان العقد فينصرف مطلق الدراهم إلى المتعارف فيها. وفي العتابية : وإذا عجل الأجرة إلى ربها لا يملك الاسترداد، ولو كانت الأجرة عيناً فأعارها ثم أودعها إلى رب الدار فهو كالتعجيل اهـ. وفي شرح الطحاوي: الأجرة لا تخلو إما أن تكون معجلة أو مؤجلة أو منجمة أو مسكوتاً عنها فإن كانت معجلة فإن له أن يتملكها وله أن يطالب بها، وإن كانت مؤجلة فليس له أن يطالب إلا بعد الأجل، وإن كانت منجمة فله أن يطالب عند كل نجم، وإن كانت مسكوتاً عنها تقدم بيان ذلك في العقار وفي المسافة إذا امتنع من الحمل فيما بقي يجبر عليه اهـ بالمعنى. وفي النسفية : استأجر حانوتاً مدة معلومة بأجرة معلومة وسكن . فخرب الحانوت في بعض المدة وتعطل وكان يمكنه الانتقال فلم يفعل وسكن المدة تلزمه جميع الأجرة، ولو استأجره ليحمل هذا إلى موضع كذا فحمل نصف الطريق وأعاده إلى مكانه الأول فلا أجر له استأجر دابة إلى مكة فلم يركبها ومضى راجلاً، إن كان بغير عذر في الدابة فعليه الأجرة، وإن كان لعذر في الدابة لا أجر عليه طالبه بالأجرة بعد المدة فقال قصرت في العمل فلك بعض الأجرة وقال لم أقصر فله الأجرة كاملة. استأجره ليحمل له العصير فحمله فإذا هو خمر قال أبو يوسف : لا أجر له. وقال محمد: إن علم أنه خمر فلا أجر له، وإن لم يعلم فله الأجر. وفي الذخيرة من الفصل السابع والعشرين في الاختلاف: لو اختلف المستأجر والآجر بعد شهر والمفتاح مع المستأجر وقال لم أقدر على فتحه وقال المؤجر بل قدرت على فتحه وسكنت ولا بينة لهما يحكم الحال، وإن أقاما بينة فالبينة بينة رب المنزل اهـ. وفي القنية : تسليم المفتاح في المصر مع التخلية ،قبض، وفي السواد ليس بقبض. وفي فتاوى الولوالجي : ولو استأجر داراً على عبد بعينه ثم وهب العبد من المستأجر قبل القبض وقال المستأجر قبلت كان ذلك إقالة. ومراد المصنف الإجارة المنجزة لأن المضافة لا تملك الأجرة فيها بشرط التعجيل. وقوله أو بالاستيفاء أو بالتمكن منه يعني يجب الاستيفاء للمنفعة أو بالتمكن وإن لم يستوف . وفي الهداية : وإذا قبض المستأجر الدار فعليه الأجرة وإن لم يسكن .
And similarly, pledging and guaranteeing are valid. In al-Muhit: If the lessor gifted the hire fee of Ramadan, is it permissible? Muhammad said: If he hired for a year, it is not permissible; if he hired monthly, it is permissible when Ramadan enters, and not before. From Abu Yusuf: It is not permissible except after the period has passed. If half of the year passed, then he exempted him from the whole or gifted it to him, he is exempt from all in Muhammad's view, and according to Abu Yusuf, he is exempt from half, not exempt from half. End. The author expressed by saying 'does not own' because the wording of Muhammad in al-Jami' is 'the hire fee is not owned by the contract itself'. The author of al-Nihayah said: 'The hire fee is not obligated by the contract' means its delivery and payment are not obligated solely by the contract. It is not clear because negating the obligation of delivery does not necessitate negating ownership, like the sold item: the buyer owns it by the contract alone, but its delivery is not obligatory until he pays the price. The correct thing is to say: it means it is not owned, because Muhammad mentioned in al-Jami' al-Saghir that the hire fee is not owned, and what is not owned, its fulfillment is not obligatory. If you say: since negating obligation does not necessitate negating ownership, it is more general, and mentioning the general while intending the specific is not a common metaphor because the general does not indicate the specific at all. The author of al-Hidayah said: The hire fee is not obligated by the contract. Taj al-Shari'ah said: That is, the obligation of performance; but the obligation itself is established by the contract itself. The author of al-Kifalah said: What is meant is the obligation itself, not performance. Explanation in summary and detail. In summary: if the hire fee were a slave that is obligatory, and the lessor freed him before the occurrence of one of the three meanings, he would not be freed; if the obligation itself were established, the freeing would be valid as in sale. End. And if he does not own by the contract itself, he cannot demand the hire fee from him. In al-Muhit: If he demanded the hire fee in cash and received it, it is permissible because it implies prompt payment. He also said: If none of these matters exist, he takes the hire fee day by day in real estate, and in distances, each stage. In al-Muntaqa: A man hired an animal from Kufa to Rayy for dirhams (one of the two currencies); the obligatory currency for the hirer—he said—is the currency of Kufa because it is the place of the contract, so absolute dirhams refer to the customary there. In al-‘Utbiyah: If he paid the hire fee promptly to its owner, he cannot reclaim it; and if the hire fee was a specific item, and he lent it then deposited it with the landlord, it is like prompt payment. End. In Sharh al-Tahawi: The hire fee is either prompt, deferred, in installments, or not mentioned; if prompt, he may own it and demand it; if deferred, he cannot demand except after the term; if installments, he may demand at each installment; if not mentioned, the explanation has preceded for real estate and for distance if he refrains from carrying what remains, he is compelled to. End (paraphrased). In al-Nasafiyyah: He hired a shop for a known period for a known fee and lived in it. The shop collapsed during part of the period and became useless, and he could have moved but did not, and lived through the period, so the full fee is obligatory. If he hired him to carry this to a certain place, and he carried half the way and returned it to its original place, he has no fee. If he hired an animal to Mecca and did not ride it and went on foot; if without an excuse concerning the animal, the fee is upon him; if there was an excuse concerning the animal, there is no fee. If he demanded the fee after the period and said 'I fell short in the work, so you have some fee,' and he said 'I did not fall short,' so he has the full fee. He hired him to carry grape juice, and he carried it and it turned out to be wine. Abu Yusuf said: He has no fee. Muhammad said: If he knew it was wine, he has no fee; if he did not know, he has the fee. In al-Dhakhirah from the twenty-seventh chapter on disagreement: If the hirer and the lessor disagree after a month, and the key is with the hirer, and he said 'I could not open it' and the lessor said 'You could open it and lived in it,' and there is no evidence for either, the current state is judged. If they produce evidence, the evidence of the landlord is preferred. End. In al-Qunyah: Delivery of the key in the city with vacating is possession; in the rural area, it is not possession. In Fatawa al-Walwaliji: If he hired a house for a specific slave, then the lessor gifted the slave to the hirer before possession, and the hirer said 'I accept,' that is a rescission. What the author means is immediate hire, because for future hire, the fee is not owned with the condition of prompt payment. And his saying 'or by actual receipt or by empowerment' means the benefit is obligated by actual receipt or by empowerment even if he did not actually receive. In al-Hidayah: If the hirer takes possession of the house, the fee is upon him even if he does not reside.
Source pages p. 8

Commentary
This passage continues the discussion on the hire fee. It begins with a brief note on the validity of pledging and guaranteeing in conjunction with hire. Then it presents a dispute between Imam Muhammad and Imam Abu Yusuf regarding the exemption (hiba or ibra) from hire fee for a specific month. The crux is whether the fee is owned by the contract. The author explains that according to Muhammad, the hire fee is not owned by the contract alone. This is supported by the statement from al-Jami' al-Saghir. There is a discussion on whether 'la tajib' means no obligation to deliver or no ownership. The correct interpretation is that the fee is not owned. Consequently, the lessor cannot demand the fee until actual receipt or empowerment. الإبراء (al-ibra'): Exemption from a debt or obligation, here the hire fee.
الوجوب (al-wujub): Obligation; here distinguished between obligation of performance (wujub al-ada') and obligation of existence (wujub al-dhimmah).
التمكن (al-tamakkun): Empowerment or ability to take possession of the benefit.

Checkpoint
In the dispute between Muhammad and Abu Yusuf regarding exemption from yearly hire fee, which of the following is true?
A) Muhammad says exemption is valid at any time.
B) Abu Yusuf says exemption is valid only after the year ends.
C) Muhammad says exemption is valid after half the year.
D) Both agree exemption is invalid before the year ends.

Key Takeaway
Exemption from hire fee is only valid when the fee is owned; thus, in yearly hire, ownership accrues only after the full period, so exemption before that is invalid according to Abu Yusuf.

Four Constraints on the Condition of Tammakun in Ijarah
Explains the four constraints on tammakun from al-Nihayah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the four constraints on tammakun and apply them to determine when rent is obligatory in ijarah.

Core Idea
Rent is only due when the lessee can actually benefit, subject to four constraints.

In Hanafi fiqh, the obligation of rent in an ijarah contract depends not just on the contract's existence but on the lessee's ability to benefit (tammakun). This lesson, drawn from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq's commentary on Kanz al-Daqa'iq, unpacks the four constraints that restrict when rent becomes due. Understanding these constraints is essential for correctly applying the rules of ijarah in practice.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core condition
Recognize that tammakun (ability to benefit) is the key condition for rent to be obligatory. If the lessee cannot benefit, no rent is due.
This is the baseline rule before considering constraints.
2
List the four constraints
From al-Nihayah, enumerate the four constraints: (1) actual ability to benefit, (2) validity of the ijarah contract, (3) ability at the place of contract, and (4) ability within the term.
Each constraint restricts when tammakun triggers rent.
3
Understand each constraint's scenario
For each constraint, examine the scenario that violates it and the legal consequence (rent not due). For example, prevention by owner or third party, invalid contract, delivery at wrong place, or delayed utilization.
Focus on the examples given: usurpation, premises occupied with belongings, delivery in Baghdad instead of Kufa, taking animal after term.
4
Apply the constraints to a hypothetical
Given a real-life rental scenario, determine whether rent is due by checking if all four constraints are satisfied. If any is missing, rent is not obligatory.
Practice identifying which constraint is violated.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الإجارة بالتمكن منه فإن غصبها غاصب منه سقطت الأجرة ولرب الدار والأرض طلب متمكناً قال في النهاية : وهذه مقيدة بقيود : أحدها التمكن فإذا لم يتمكن بأن منعه المالك أو الأجنبي أو سلم الدار مشغولة بمتاعه لا تجب الأجرة. الثاني أن تكون الإجارة صحيحة فإن كانت فاسدة فلا بد من حقيقة الانتفاع والثالث أن التمكن إنما يجب أن يكون في مكان العقد حتى لو استأجرها للكوفة فسلمها في بغداد حين مضت المدة فلا أجر عليه. والرابع أن يكون من الاستيفاء في المدة لو استأجر دابة إلى الكوفة في هذا اليوم وذهب بعد مضي اليوم بالدابة ولم يركب لم يجب الأجرة لأنه إنما تمكن بعد مضي المدة.
The book of Ijarah. With the ability to benefit from it, if a usurper usurps it from him, the rent falls, and the owner of the house and land seeks [payment] when the lessee is able to benefit. He said in al-Nihayah: This is restricted by four constraints: First: ability to benefit; if he is not able to benefit, because the owner or a third party prevents him, or he surrenders the house occupied with his belongings, the rent is not obligatory. Second: the ijarah must be valid; if it is invalid, then actual benefit is necessary. Third: ability to benefit must be at the place of the contract; so if he hired it for Kufa and he surrendered it in Baghdad when the term has passed, no rent is due on him. Fourth: [the ability to benefit] must be from the utilization within the term; if he hired an animal to go to Kufa on this day, and he went after the day has passed with the animal and did not ride, the rent is not obligatory because he only had ability to benefit after the term had passed.
Source pages p. 10

Commentary
This passage explains the condition of tammakun (ability to benefit) for the obligation of rent. The commentator quotes al-Nihayah to enumerate four constraints. The first constraint is that the lessee must actually be able to benefit; if prevented by owner or third party, no rent. The second is that the contract must be valid; if it is fasid, actual benefit is required. The third is that the ability must be at the place of the contract; delivery at a different place after the term does not obligate rent. The fourth is that the ability must occur within the term; if the animal is taken after the term, rent is not due. These constraints ensure that rent is only payable when the lessee genuinely has the opportunity to utilize the leased item.

Key Terms
التمكن (al-tammakun): The ability to benefit from the leased property without hindrance.
الإجارة (al-ijarah): A contract of hiring or leasing, where one party provides benefit in exchange for rent.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which of the following is NOT one of the four constraints on tammakun?
A) The lessee must actually be able to benefit.
B) The ijarah must be valid.
C) The lessee must pay rent in advance.
D) The ability to benefit must be at the place of contract.

Key Takeaway
Rent in ijarah is only obligatory when the lessee has actual ability to benefit, subject to four constraints restricting that condition.

Dispute Over Rent Liability When an Agent Hires a House
Intra-Hanafi dispute on rent liability in agency hire.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between the positions of Abu Yusuf and Muhammad regarding rent liability in agency hire contracts and identify the basis of their disagreement.

Core Idea
In agency hire, possession attribution determines rent liability: agent pays per Abu Yusuf, principal pays per Muhammad.

When an agent hires a house for his principal, who bears the rent? This lesson examines an intra-Hanafi dispute between Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani recorded in al-Muhit. Their disagreement centers on whether the agent's possession is attributed to the principal, affecting the obligation to pay rent. Understanding this dispute sharpens your ability to apply Hanafi principles of agency (wakalah) and possession (qabd).

Guided Path
1
State the scenario
A man orders a person to hire a house for him for a full year. The agent hires it, takes possession, and the principal lives in it for the entire period. The question is: who must pay the rent to the lessor?
2
Identify Abu Yusuf's position
Abu Yusuf rules that the rent is on the agent (al-ma'mur), not the principal. His reasoning: the agent is the one who actually took possession and used the dwelling, so he is liable.
Quote: 'الأجرة على المأمور'
3
Identify Muhammad's position
Muhammad rules that the rent is on the principal (al-muwakkil). His reasoning: the agent's possession is like the principal's own possession because of agency. The agent is considered a usurper (ghasib) of the dwelling, so no rent is due on him.
Quote: 'الأجر على الموكل' and 'قبض وكيله كقبض نفسه'
4
Understand the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference: under Abu Yusuf, the agent must pay the rent; under Muhammad, the principal must pay. This affects legal recourse for the lessor.
5
Note the absence of tarjih
The passage from al-Muhit does not specify which view is mufta bihi. Later Hanafi works may give preference, but here both positions are recorded as valid within the school.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وفي المحيط : أمر رجلاً أن يستأجر له داراً سنة كاملة فاستأجرها وتسلمها الوكيل وسكنها هو سنة قال أبو يوسف : لا أجر على المؤجر والأجرة على المأمور. وقال محمد : الأجر على الموكل لأن قبض وكيله كقبض نفسه والمأمور غاصب للسكنى فلا يجب عليه أجر .
And in al-Muhit: A man ordered a person to hire a house for him for a full year, so he hired it, and the agent took possession, and he (the principal) lived in it for a year. Abu Yusuf said: There is no rent on the lessor, and the rent is on the commanded person (the agent). Muhammad said: The rent is on the principal because the taking of possession by his agent is like his own taking, and the commanded person is a usurper of the dwelling, so no rent is due on him.
Source pages p. 10

Commentary
This passage from al-Muhit presents a dispute between Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani regarding an agent who hires a house for his principal. The principal lives in the house for the whole year. Abu Yusuf holds that the lessor (owner) is not liable for rent; rather the agent must pay the rent. Muhammad holds that the principal must pay because the agent's possession is attributed to the principal, and the agent is considered a usurper of the dwelling, so he does not owe rent. This is an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf.

Key Terms
الوكيل (al-wakil): An agent appointed to act on behalf of another.
المأمور (al-ma'mur): The commanded person, here the agent who was told to hire.
الموكل (al-muwakkil): The principal who appoints the agent.
غاصب (ghasib): Usurper; one who wrongfully takes possession.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Yusuf in this passage, who is liable for the rent?
A) The principal (al-muwakkil)
B) The agent (al-ma'mur)
C) The lessor (al-mu'jir)
D) No one

Key Takeaway
In an agency hire, Hanafi masters differ on rent liability: Abu Yusuf charges the agent due to actual possession, while Muhammad charges the principal due to legal attribution through agency.

Effect of Ghasb on Rent Obligation and Contract Dissolution
Ruling on rent falling due to ghasb and dispute on dissolution

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the rule that rent drops when the lessee loses the ability to benefit due to ghasb, explain the intra-Hanafi dispute on whether the contract dissolves, and apply the principle to analogous cases.

Core Idea
Rent is tied to ability to benefit; ghasb removes that ability, so rent drops proportionally.

This lesson examines a key principle in Hanafi ijarah: the lessee's obligation to pay rent depends on their ability to benefit from the leased asset. When a usurper (ghasib) takes over the property, that ability is lost, and the rent falls accordingly. However, there is a notable intra-Hanafi disagreement on whether the contract itself dissolves or remains intact. The passage also provides several practical applications to illustrate how this principle operates in different scenarios.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Core Ruling on Ghasb and Rent
Locate the statement in the source that if a usurper (ghasib) takes the leased asset for the entire term, the rent drops completely; if for part of the term, it drops proportionally.
The ruling is in the first sentence: فإن غصبها غاصب منه سقطت الأجرة.
2
Understand the Condition of Tammakun (Ability to Benefit)
The reason for the rent drop is the loss of ability to benefit (tammakun al-intifa'), which is a condition for the rent obligation. Reflect on why this condition is central to Hanafi ijarah.
The text says لزوال التمكن من الانتفاع وهو شرط لوجوب الأجرة.
3
Analyze the Intra-Hanafi Dispute on Contract Dissolution
Note the two views: Al-Hidayah holds that the contract dissolves (tansakh) by ghasb, while Fakhr al-Islam and al-Fadli hold that it does not dissolve. Consider the basis of each view.
If it dissolves, the lessee cannot claim remaining period; if not, he can resume use after usurpation ends.
4
Trace the Practical Consequence of the Dispute
According to the second view, the lessee has the right to reside for the remaining term even after the usurpation ends, and the lessor cannot prevent him.
فإذا أراد المستأجر أن يسكن بقية المدة ليس للمؤجر منعه.
5
Apply the Principle to the Furu' Cases
Walk through each of the cited cases: the usurper who denies ownership, the cleaner/dyer who denies then returns the item, the hirer who denies the contract halfway, and the natural disasters or delayed delivery. In each, determine how the rule of rent dropping applies.
Key: the focus is on when rent is due and when it is not based on benefit.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال رحمه الله : (فإن غصبها غاصب منه سقطت الأجرة) يعني إذا غصب العين المستأجرة في جميع المدة غاصب سقطت الأجرة ولو في بعضها فبقدره لزوال التمكن من الانتفاع وهو شرط لوجوب الأجرة كما بين. وهل تنفسخ بالغصب؟ قال صاحب الهداية : تنفسخ . وقال فخر الإسلام في فتاواه والفضلي : لا تنفسخ . فإذا أراد المستأجر أن يسكن بقية المدة ليس للمؤجر منعه اهـ. وفي قاضيخان أيضاً جاء المغصوب منه إلى الغاصب وقال الدار داري إن لم تخرج منها فهي عليك كل شهر بمائة درهم قال محمد: إن كان الغاصب منكراً ويقول الدار لي ويسكن مدة فأقام المغصوب منه البينة أنها داره فقضى له بها لا أجر عليه، وإن كان مقراً يلزمه المسمى اهـ. وفي الولوالجية رجل دفع ثوباً إلى قصار ليقصره بأجرة معلومة فجحد القصار الثوب ثم جاء به مقصوراً وأقر قال هذا على وجهين : إن قصره قبل الجحود له الأجر، وإن قصره بعد الجحود لا أجر له ولو كان صباغاً والمسألة بحالها إن صبغه قبل الجحود فله الأجر، وإن صبغه بعده فرب الثوب بالخيار إن شاء أخذ الثوب وأعطاه قيمة ما زاد فيه، وإن شاء ترك الثوب وضمنه قيمة ثوب أبيض .اهـ. وفي التتارخانية : رجل استأجر دابة إلى مكان معلوم فلما بلغ نصف المدة أنكر الإجارة لزمه من الأجرة ما قبل الإنكار ولا يلزم ما بعده وهو قول الثاني. وقال محمد: لا تسقط عنه الأجرة بنفس الإنكار . ولو كان عبداً والمسألة بحالها وقيمة العبد يوم العقد ألفان ويوم الجحود ألف فهلك العبد في يده بعد ما مضت السنة فالأجرة لازمة وتجب كل الأجرة ويجب عليه قيمة العبد، وينبغي أن يكون هذا على قول محمد وعلى قول الثاني لما جحد فقد أسقط الأجر. وفي المحيط: لو غرقت الأرض أو انقطع عنها الشرب أو مرض العبد سقط من الأجر بقدره لفوات التمكن من الانتفاع في المدة، ولو استأجر داراً سنة فلم يسلمها الآجر حتى مضى شهر لم يكن لأحدهما الامتناع عن التسليم في الثاني لأن الإجارة وإن كانت عقداً واحداً حقيقة لكنها عقود متفرقة
He (the author) said, may Allah have mercy on him: (If a usurper usurps it from him, the rent drops) meaning if a usurper usurps the leased asset for the entire term, the rent drops, and if for part of it, then proportionally, due to the loss of ability to benefit, which is a condition for rent obligation as explained. And does the contract dissolve by usurpation? The author of al-Hidayah said: It dissolves. And Fakhr al-Islam in his Fatawa and al-Fadli said: It does not dissolve. So if the lessee wants to reside for the remaining term, the lessor cannot prevent him, end quote. In Qadikhan also: The one from whom it was usurped came to the usurper and said: The house is mine; if you do not leave it, it is on you at one hundred dirhams per month. Muhammad said: If the usurper denies and says the house is mine and resides for a period, and the victim proves by evidence that it is his house and judgment is given for him, no rent is due on him. But if he acknowledges, the stipulated rent is binding on him, end quote. In al-Walwaljiyya: A man gave a cloth to a cleaner to clean it for a known wage, and the cleaner denied the cloth, then brought it cleaned and acknowledged. He said: This is two ways: if he cleaned it before denial, he gets the wage; if he cleaned it after denial, no wage for him. And if he was a dyer, and the case is the same, if he dyed it before denial, he gets the wage; if he dyed it after, the owner of the cloth has the option: if he wishes, he takes the cloth and gives him the value of the increase, and if he wishes, he leaves the cloth and holds him liable for the value of a white cloth, end quote. In al-Tatarkhaniyya: A man hired an animal to a known place. When he reached halfway, he denied the ijarah. The rent before the denial is due on him, and what after is not due; this is the statement of the second (Abu Yusuf). And Muhammad said: Rent does not fall from him by mere denial. And if it was a slave, and the case is the same, and the value of the slave on the day of contract is two thousand and on the day of denial is one thousand, and the slave perished in his hand after the year passed, the rent is due, and all the rent is obligatory, and he owes the value of the slave. And it should be that this is according to Muhammad's saying, and according to the second's saying, when he denied, he dropped the rent. And in al-Muhit: If the land is flooded, or its irrigation is cut off, or the slave falls ill, proportion of the rent drops due to loss of ability to benefit within the term. And if a man hires a house for a year and the lessor does not hand it over until a month has passed, neither of them can refuse delivery in the second month because the ijarah, though one contract in reality, is multiple separate contracts.
Source pages p. 10

Commentary
This passage addresses the effect of ghasb (usurpation) on the rent and the contract. The commentator explains that if the leased item is usurped for the entire term, rent drops; if partially, proportionally. A dispute arises on whether the contract dissolves: al-Hidayah says it dissolves, while Fakhr al-Islam and al-Fadli say it does not; thus the lessee may continue to use the remaining term if desired. Various fatawa illustrate applications: in Qadikhan, a usurper who denies ownership is not liable for rent if the victim proves ownership; the case of a cleaner who denies then returns the item: wages depend on whether the work was done before or after denial; a dyer who increases value gives the owner an option. In al-Tatarkhaniyya, denial of the contract by the hirer partway through: according to Abu Yusuf, rent after denial is not due; Muhammad says it is still due. Finally, natural disasters causing loss of benefit proportionally reduce rent, and if delivery is delayed by one month, neither party can refuse subsequent delivery because the contract is considered multiple contracts in effect.

Key Terms
الغصب (al-ghasb): Wrongful taking of property without right.
الفسخ (al-faskh): Dissolution of contract.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, if the leased house is usurped for the entire term, what happens to the rent?
A) The rent remains due in full
B) The rent drops entirely
C) The rent is doubled
D) The rent is halved

Key Takeaway
Rent in Hanafi ijarah is conditional on the lessee's ability to benefit; if that ability is lost due to ghasb or other causes, rent drops proportionally, and there is an intra-Hanafi dispute on whether the contract dissolves.

Timing of Rent for House and Land and Camel Hire
Ruling on when rent is due for house/land and camel hire.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state when rent is due for house/land and camel hire and explain the general principle that rent follows benefit.

Core Idea
Rent for houses/land is due daily; rent for camels is due per stage.

In Hanafi ijarah, the timing of rent obligation depends on the type of subject matter. For immovable property and animal hire, the rule is tied to daily use or stages. This lesson covers the general principle and the retraction of Abu Hanifa from his earlier view.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling for house/land and camel hire
Read the statement that the owner can demand rent daily for house/land and after each stage for camel hire. Note that this applies when the contract is absolute (no specified timing).
2
Trace the principle behind the ruling
The passage explains that ijarah is a contract of exchange; ownership of benefits is not established at contract formation, so rent is also not owed until benefit is received. This is the basis for tying rent to receipt of benefit.
3
Understand Abu Hanifa's initial view and retraction
Abu Hanifa initially held that rent is not due until benefit is actually received in all types of ijarah. He later retracted to the view stated here, which is the mufta bihi.
4
Consider the qiyas and istihsan
Qiyas would require rent to be due hour by hour, but that leads to hardship, so it was abandoned for this ruling based on convenience (istihsan).
5
Apply the special case: peak season
If there is a peak season (e.g., a shop in a busy market or a house in Makkah for Hajj), and the property is not delivered at the desired time, the lessee has an option to reduce rent proportionally to remove harm.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الأجرة كل وللجمال كل مرحلة وللخياط والقصار بعد الفراغ من عمله وللخباز يوم يعني مضافة إلى ما يوجد من المنفعة ومن المشايخ من قال : هذا إذا لم يكن في مدة الإجارة وقت يرغب في الإجارة لأجله، فإن كان وقت يرغب في الإجارة لأجله زيادة رغبة كحانوت في سوق رواجه في بعض السنة أو دار بمكة تستأجر سنة لأجل الموسم فلم تسلم في الوقت الذي يرغب لأجله فإنه يخير في بعض الباقي دفعاً للضرر عنه .اهـ. قال رحمه الله: (ولرب الدار والأرض طلب الأجرة كل يوم وللجمال كل مرحلة يعني إذا وقعت الإجارة مطلقة ولم يتعرض فيها لوقت وجوب الإجرة فللمؤجر ما ذكره والأصل فيه أن الإجارة معاوضة والملك في المنافع يمتنع ثبوته زمان العقد فكذا الملك في الأجرة على ما بينا، وكان الإمام أولاً يقول في جميع أنواع الإجارة لا تجب الأجرة حتى يستوفي المنفعة ثم رجع لما ذكر هنا، وكان القياس أن تجب الأجرة ساعة فساعة إلا أنه يفضي إلى الحرج فتركناه لهذا. وفي الخلاصة : امرأة أجرت دارها من زوجها ثم أسكنها فيها لا تجب الأجرة، ولو استأجر داراً شهراً وسكن فيها مع صاحب الدار إلى آخر الشهر فقال المستأجر لا أدفع الأجرة لعدم التخلية فعليه من الأجرة بقدر ما في يده لوجود التخلية فيها .اهـ. ولو عبر بالفاء التفريعية لكان أولى ليفيد أنه متفرع على الاستيفاء والتمكن قال حرمه الله : ( وللخياط والقصار بعد الفراغ من عمله) إذا وقعت الإجارة مطلقة عن وقت وجوب الأجرة فللعامل أن يطالب بعدما ذكر المؤلف . وأطلق في قوله بعد «الفراغ فأفاد أنه لا فرق بينهما إذا عمل في بيت نفسه أو في بيت المستأجر كما ذكره صاحب الهداية وصاحب التجريد، وذكر في المبسوط والفوائد الظهيرية والذخيرة ومبسوط شيخ الإسلام وشرح الجامع الصغير لفخر الإسلام وقاضيخان والتمرتاشي : إذا خاط في بيت المستأجر تجب الأجرة له بحسابه حتى إذا سرق الثوب بعدما خاط بعضه يستحق الأجرة بحسابه واستشهد في الأصل لهذا بما إذا استأجر إنساناً ليبني له حائطاً فبنى بعضه ثم انهدم فله أجر ما بنى فهذا يدل على أنه يستحق الأجرة ببعض العمل إلا أن يشترط فيه التسليم إلى المستأجر . ونقل هذا عن الكرخي وجزم به في غاية البيان فكان هو المذهب، ففي سكنى الدار وقطع المسافة صار مسلماً له بمجرد تسليم الدار، وقطع المسافة وفي الخياطة ونحوها لا يكون مسلماً إليه إلا إذا سلمه إلى صاحبه حقيقة، وفي الخياطة في منزل المستأجر يحصل التسليم بمجرد العمل إذ هو في منزله والمنزل في يده فلا يحتاج إلى تسليم ليده. ويعرف توزيع الأجرة بقول أهل الخبرة بها والخيط والأبرة على الخياط حيث كان العرف ذلك . قال رحمه الله : (وللخباز بعد إخراج الخبز من التنور) يعني إذا أطلق الأجرة ولم يبين وقتها فللخباز أن يطالب بها بعد إخراج الخبز من التنور لأنه بأخراجه قد فرغ من فيملك المطالبة كالخياط إذا فرغ من العمل حتى إذا أخبزه في بيت المستأجر لأنه صار مسلماً إليه بمجرد الإخراج فيستحق الأجرة، وإن كان في منزل الخباز لم يكن مسلماً بمجرد
The rent entirely, and for the camel driver each stage, and for the tailor and cleaner after completion of their work, and for the baker day, meaning attached to what is found of benefit. And some mashayikh said: This is when there is no time in the lease period that is desired for the lease; but if there is a time desired for the lease with increased demand, like a shop in a market that is active part of the year, or a house in Makkah hired for a year for the season, and it is not handed over at the desired time, then he (the lessee) has a choice regarding the remaining part to remove harm from him, end quote. He said, may Allah have mercy on him: (And for the owner of the house and land, he seeks the rent every day, and for the camel driver each stage) meaning if the ijarah is absolute and does not mention a time for the obligation of rent, then the lessor has what was mentioned. The principle is that ijarah is a contract of exchange, and ownership of benefits cannot be established at the time of contract, so likewise ownership of the rent, as we explained. The Imam (Abu Hanifa) initially said in all types of ijarah that rent is not obligatory until benefit is received, then he retracted to what is mentioned here. The analogical reasoning (qiyas) would require rent to be due hour by hour, but that leads to hardship, so we abandoned it for this. In al-Khulasa: A woman rented her house to her husband, then he lived in it with her; rent is not obligatory. And if a man hired a house for a month and lived in it with the owner until the end of the month, and the lessee said 'I will not pay rent due to lack of delivery (takhliya)', he owes rent proportionally for what he used because there is delivery. End quote. And if he used the particle 'fa' (thus) it would be better to indicate that it is a consequence of receipt and ability to benefit. He said, may Allah have mercy on him: (And for the tailor and cleaner after completion of their work) if the ijarah is absolute regarding the time of rent obligation, then the worker can demand after what the author mentioned. And he said generally 'after completion' indicating that there is no difference whether they work in their own house or the lessee's house, as stated by Sahib al-Hidayah and Sahib al-Tajrid. And it is mentioned in al-Mabsut, al-Fawa'id al-Zahiriyya, al-Dhakhira, Mabsut Sheikh al-Islam, Sharh al-Jami' al-Saghir by Fakhr al-Islam, Qadikhan, and al-Tamartashi: If he sews in the lessee's house, the rent is due to him proportionally; even if the cloth is stolen after he sewed some of it, he deserves rent for what he sewed. They use as evidence the case of hiring a person to build a wall; if he builds part then it collapses, he gets wages for what he built. This indicates that he deserves rent for part of the work unless delivery to the lessee is stipulated. This is reported from al-Karkhi and confirmed in Ghayat al-Bayan, so it is the madhhab. In the case of house dwelling and traveling distance, possession is achieved merely by handing over the house or completing the journey. In tailoring and similar, possession is not achieved until it is actually handed over to the owner. But if tailoring is done in the lessee's house, delivery occurs by mere work since it is in his house and the house is in his possession, so no need to hand over. The distribution of rent is determined by the experts, and the thread and needle are on the tailor if that is the custom. He said, may Allah have mercy on him: (And for the baker after removing the bread from the oven) meaning if the rent is absolute and no time specified, the baker can demand after removing the bread from the oven because by doing so he has completed, so he has the right to demand, like the tailor when he completes work. Even if he bakes it in the lessee's house, because it becomes delivered to him by mere removal, so he deserves the rent. But if it was in the baker's house, it is not delivered merely by...
Source pages p. 11

Commentary
This passage details the timing of rent obligation for various types of ijarah. For house/land rental, the owner can demand rent daily; for camel hire, after each stage; for tailor/cleaner, after completion; for baker, after removing bread from the oven. Some scholars add that if there is a peak season and the property was not delivered on time, the lessee has a choice. The commentator then explains the principle: ijarah is a contract of exchange, and ownership of benefits is not established at contract time, so rent is also not owed until benefit is received. Abu Hanifa initially held that rent is not due until benefit is actually received, then changed to this view. Qiyas would suggest rent is due hour by hour, but that is impractical. Various sub-rulings: if a wife rents to her husband and he lives with her, no rent due; if a tenant lives with the owner, rent proportional to use. For tailors, work in the hirer's house results in immediate delivery, so rent is due even if the cloth is stolen later. For bakers, if they bake in the hirer's house, delivery is immediate; if in their own house, not until handed over.

Key Terms
الاستيفاء (al-istifa'): Receiving and utilizing the benefit.
التسليم (al-taslim): Delivery of the benefit to the lessee.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) At the end of the lease period
B) Daily as benefit is received
C) At the beginning of the lease
D) After the tenant moves out

Key Takeaway
Rent for houses and land is due daily, and for camel hire per stage, because rent follows actual receipt of benefit.

Timing of Rent for Tailor and Cleaner
Ruling on when rent is due for tailor and cleaner.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state when a tailor or cleaner is entitled to their wage and explain how the place of work affects delivery.

Core Idea
A tailor or cleaner is entitled to wage after completing the work; delivery occurs immediately if work is done in the hirer's premises.

For artisans like tailors and cleaners, the timing of wage differs from house rentals. The wage is due after completion of the work, with a nuance: if the work is done in the hirer's house, delivery is presumed, so wage is due even if the item is later stolen.

Guided Path
1
State the general rule for tailor/cleaner
The text rules that the worker can demand wage after finishing the work. This applies when the contract does not specify a payment time.
2
Understand the effect of where the work is done
If the tailor sews in the hirer's house, delivery (taslim) occurs upon completion because the house is in the hirer's possession. If done in the tailor's own house, delivery occurs only when the item is handed over.
3
Apply the evidence from hiring a builder
The analogy of hiring a person to build a wall: if part is built then collapses, the builder gets wage for what was built. This supports the idea that partial completion earns partial wage.
4
Consider the role of custom
The distribution of rent for partial work is determined by experts, and the cost of thread and needle is on the tailor if that is the custom.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الأجرة كل وللجمال كل مرحلة وللخياط والقصار بعد الفراغ من عمله وللخباز يوم يعني مضافة إلى ما يوجد من المنفعة ومن المشايخ من قال : هذا إذا لم يكن في مدة الإجارة وقت يرغب في الإجارة لأجله، فإن كان وقت يرغب في الإجارة لأجله زيادة رغبة كحانوت في سوق رواجه في بعض السنة أو دار بمكة تستأجر سنة لأجل الموسم فلم تسلم في الوقت الذي يرغب لأجله فإنه يخير في بعض الباقي دفعاً للضرر عنه .اهـ. قال رحمه الله: (ولرب الدار والأرض طلب الأجرة كل يوم وللجمال كل مرحلة يعني إذا وقعت الإجارة مطلقة ولم يتعرض فيها لوقت وجوب الإجرة فللمؤجر ما ذكره والأصل فيه أن الإجارة معاوضة والملك في المنافع يمتنع ثبوته زمان العقد فكذا الملك في الأجرة على ما بينا، وكان الإمام أولاً يقول في جميع أنواع الإجارة لا تجب الأجرة حتى يستوفي المنفعة ثم رجع لما ذكر هنا، وكان القياس أن تجب الأجرة ساعة فساعة إلا أنه يفضي إلى الحرج فتركناه لهذا. وفي الخلاصة : امرأة أجرت دارها من زوجها ثم أسكنها فيها لا تجب الأجرة، ولو استأجر داراً شهراً وسكن فيها مع صاحب الدار إلى آخر الشهر فقال المستأجر لا أدفع الأجرة لعدم التخلية فعليه من الأجرة بقدر ما في يده لوجود التخلية فيها .اهـ. ولو عبر بالفاء التفريعية لكان أولى ليفيد أنه متفرع على الاستيفاء والتمكن قال حرمه الله : ( وللخياط والقصار بعد الفراغ من عمله) إذا وقعت الإجارة مطلقة عن وقت وجوب الأجرة فللعامل أن يطالب بعدما ذكر المؤلف . وأطلق في قوله بعد «الفراغ فأفاد أنه لا فرق بينهما إذا عمل في بيت نفسه أو في بيت المستأجر كما ذكره صاحب الهداية وصاحب التجريد، وذكر في المبسوط والفوائد الظهيرية والذخيرة ومبسوط شيخ الإسلام وشرح الجامع الصغير لفخر الإسلام وقاضيخان والتمرتاشي : إذا خاط في بيت المستأجر تجب الأجرة له بحسابه حتى إذا سرق الثوب بعدما خاط بعضه يستحق الأجرة بحسابه واستشهد في الأصل لهذا بما إذا استأجر إنساناً ليبني له حائطاً فبنى بعضه ثم انهدم فله أجر ما بنى فهذا يدل على أنه يستحق الأجرة ببعض العمل إلا أن يشترط فيه التسليم إلى المستأجر . ونقل هذا عن الكرخي وجزم به في غاية البيان فكان هو المذهب، ففي سكنى الدار وقطع المسافة صار مسلماً له بمجرد تسليم الدار، وقطع المسافة وفي الخياطة ونحوها لا يكون مسلماً إليه إلا إذا سلمه إلى صاحبه حقيقة، وفي الخياطة في منزل المستأجر يحصل التسليم بمجرد العمل إذ هو في منزله والمنزل في يده فلا يحتاج إلى تسليم ليده. ويعرف توزيع الأجرة بقول أهل الخبرة بها والخيط والأبرة على الخياط حيث كان العرف ذلك . قال رحمه الله : (وللخباز بعد إخراج الخبز من التنور) يعني إذا أطلق الأجرة ولم يبين وقتها فللخباز أن يطالب بها بعد إخراج الخبز من التنور لأنه بأخراجه قد فرغ من فيملك المطالبة كالخياط إذا فرغ من العمل حتى إذا أخبزه في بيت المستأجر لأنه صار مسلماً إليه بمجرد الإخراج فيستحق الأجرة، وإن كان في منزل الخباز لم يكن مسلماً بمجرد
The rent entirely, and for the camel driver each stage, and for the tailor and cleaner after completion of their work, and for the baker day, meaning attached to what is found of benefit. And some mashayikh said: This is when there is no time in the lease period that is desired for the lease; but if there is a time desired for the lease with increased demand, like a shop in a market that is active part of the year, or a house in Makkah hired for a year for the season, and it is not handed over at the desired time, then he (the lessee) has a choice regarding the remaining part to remove harm from him, end quote. He said, may Allah have mercy on him: (And for the owner of the house and land, he seeks the rent every day, and for the camel driver each stage) meaning if the ijarah is absolute and does not mention a time for the obligation of rent, then the lessor has what was mentioned. The principle is that ijarah is a contract of exchange, and ownership of benefits cannot be established at the time of contract, so likewise ownership of the rent, as we explained. The Imam (Abu Hanifa) initially said in all types of ijarah that rent is not obligatory until benefit is received, then he retracted to what is mentioned here. The analogical reasoning (qiyas) would require rent to be due hour by hour, but that leads to hardship, so we abandoned it for this. In al-Khulasa: A woman rented her house to her husband, then he lived in it with her; rent is not obligatory. And if a man hired a house for a month and lived in it with the owner until the end of the month, and the lessee said 'I will not pay rent due to lack of delivery (takhliya)', he owes rent proportionally for what he used because there is delivery. End quote. And if he used the particle 'fa' (thus) it would be better to indicate that it is a consequence of receipt and ability to benefit. He said, may Allah have mercy on him: (And for the tailor and cleaner after completion of their work) if the ijarah is absolute regarding the time of rent obligation, then the worker can demand after what the author mentioned. And he said generally 'after completion' indicating that there is no difference whether they work in their own house or the lessee's house, as stated by Sahib al-Hidayah and Sahib al-Tajrid. And it is mentioned in al-Mabsut, al-Fawa'id al-Zahiriyya, al-Dhakhira, Mabsut Sheikh al-Islam, Sharh al-Jami' al-Saghir by Fakhr al-Islam, Qadikhan, and al-Tamartashi: If he sews in the lessee's house, the rent is due to him proportionally; even if the cloth is stolen after he sewed some of it, he deserves rent for what he sewed. They use as evidence the case of hiring a person to build a wall; if he builds part then it collapses, he gets wages for what he built. This indicates that he deserves rent for part of the work unless delivery to the lessee is stipulated. This is reported from al-Karkhi and confirmed in Ghayat al-Bayan, so it is the madhhab. In the case of house dwelling and traveling distance, possession is achieved merely by handing over the house or completing the journey. In tailoring and similar, possession is not achieved until it is actually handed over to the owner. But if tailoring is done in the lessee's house, delivery occurs by mere work since it is in his house and the house is in his possession, so no need to hand over. The distribution of rent is determined by the experts, and the thread and needle are on the tailor if that is the custom. He said, may Allah have mercy on him: (And for the baker after removing the bread from the oven) meaning if the rent is absolute and no time specified, the baker can demand after removing the bread from the oven because by doing so he has completed, so he has the right to demand, like the tailor when he completes work. Even if he bakes it in the lessee's house, because it becomes delivered to him by mere removal, so he deserves the rent. But if it was in the baker's house, it is not delivered merely by...
Source pages p. 11

Commentary
This passage details the timing of rent obligation for various types of ijarah. For house/land rental, the owner can demand rent daily; for camel hire, after each stage; for tailor/cleaner, after completion; for baker, after removing bread from the oven. Some scholars add that if there is a peak season and the property was not delivered on time, the lessee has a choice. The commentator then explains the principle: ijarah is a contract of exchange, and ownership of benefits is not established at contract time, so rent is also not owed until benefit is received. Abu Hanifa initially held that rent is not due until benefit is actually received, then changed to this view. Qiyas would suggest rent is due hour by hour, but that is impractical. Various sub-rulings: if a wife rents to her husband and he lives with her, no rent due; if a tenant lives with the owner, rent proportional to use. For tailors, work in the hirer's house results in immediate delivery, so rent is due even if the cloth is stolen later. For bakers, if they bake in the hirer's house, delivery is immediate; if in their own house, not until handed over.

Key Terms
الاستيفاء (al-istifa'): Receiving and utilizing the benefit.
التسليم (al-taslim): Delivery of the benefit to the lessee.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a tailor sews a suit in the hirer's house and the suit is then stolen before the hirer takes it, according to the Hanafi madhhab, is the tailor entitled to his wage?
A) Yes, for the work done
B) No, because the suit was stolen
C) Only if the theft was not his fault
D) Yes, only if the hirer had received the suit

Key Takeaway
A tailor/cleaner is entitled to wage after completing work, but delivery is presumed only if work is done in the hirer's premises.

Timing of Rent for Baker
Ruling on when rent is due for baker.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state when a baker is entitled to his wage and explain how the place of baking affects delivery.

Core Idea
A baker is entitled to wage after removing bread from the oven; delivery is immediate if baked in the hirer's house.

For bakers, the wage is due after the bread is taken out of the oven. Similar to tailoring, if the baking is done in the hirer's house, delivery occurs immediately; if in the baker's own house, additional handover is required.

Guided Path
1
State the ruling for baker
The baker can demand his wage after removing the bread from the oven, because that constitutes completion of the work.
2
Analogize to the tailor rule
The baker is treated like the tailor: completion of work triggers the right to wage, but delivery depends on where the work is done.
3
Distinguish based on location
If baking is done in the hirer's house, delivery is immediate by virtue of the baker working in the hirer's premises. If in the baker's house, delivery occurs only when the bread is handed over.

Default Timing for Rent in Absolute Ijara
Default timing of rent demand in absolute ijara

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the default timing for demanding rent in absolute ijara contracts for various service providers and explain the Hanafi reasoning (istihsan) that overrides strict qiyas.

Core Idea
Rent is due customarily per day for land, per stage for transport, and after completion for craftsmen.

In an ijara contract where the payment time is not specified (mutlaqah), when exactly can the lessor demand the rent? The Hanafi school has determined clear defaults based on the type of benefit and custom, avoiding the hardship that would come from a strict hourly breakdown. This lesson unpacks those defaults and the legal reasoning behind them.

Guided Path
1
Identify the types of lessors and their default timing
The matn lists: landlord getting rent daily, camel owner per stage, tailor/launderer after work, baker daily. Note that these timings apply when the contract is absolute (no agreed payment schedule).
Per stage means per journey leg, e.g., from one city to the next.
2
Understand the underlying principle (asl)
The commentary explains that ijara is an exchange contract (mu'awada). Just as ownership of benefits is not transferred at the contract moment, ownership of the rent is also delayed until benefit is provided. This is the basis for not demanding rent upfront.
The analogy (qiyas) is drawn from sale, but benefits are gradual.
3
Examine the Imam's initial position and retraction
Abu Hanifa initially held that rent is not due until the benefit is fully availed. He later retracted to the view that it can be demanded per day/per stage. This shows the evolution within the madhhab.
The retraction is significant: it shifted from strict equivalence to practical custom.
4
Analyze the qiyas vs. istihsan reasoning
Strict qiyas would make rent due hour by hour (saa'atan fa saa'atan), but that leads to hardship (haraj). To avoid hardship, the school adopted istihsan, allowing customary intervals (daily, per stage, after completion).
Istihsan is a valid source of law in Hanafi usul when qiyas leads to difficulty.
5
Apply to exceptions and branch cases
The text gives exceptions: if there is a peak season (e.g., shop in busy month) and the property is not delivered in that season, the lessee may have an option to reduce rent. Also, if the lessor resides with tenant, rent is due proportionally.
These branches show the nuanced application of the default rule.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الأجرة كل وللجمال كل مرحلة وللخياط والقصار بعد الفراغ من عمله وللخباز يوم يعني مضافة إلى ما يوجد من المنفعة ومن المشايخ من قال : هذا إذا لم يكن في مدة الإجارة وقت يرغب في الإجارة لأجله، فإن كان وقت يرغب في الإجارة لأجله زيادة رغبة كحانوت في سوق رواجه في بعض السنة أو دار بمكة تستأجر سنة لأجل الموسم فلم يسلم في الوقت الذي يرغب لأجله فإنه يخير في بعض الباقي دفعاً للضرر عنه .اهـ. قال رحمه الله: (ولرب الدار والأرض طلب الأجرة كل يوم وللجمال كل مرحلة يعني إذا وقعت الإجارة مطلقة ولم يتعرض فيها لوقت وجوب الإجرة فللمؤجر ما ذكره والأصل فيه أن الإجارة معاوضة والملك في المنافع يمتنع ثبوته زمان العقد فكذا الملك في الأجرة على ما بينا، وكان الإمام أولاً يقول في جميع أنواع الإجارة لا تجب الأجرة حتى يستوفي المنفعة ثم رجع لما ذكر هنا، وكان القياس أن تجب الأجرة ساعة فساعة إلا أنه يفضي إلى الحرج فتركناه لهذا. وفي الخلاصة : امرأة أجرت دارها من زوجها ثم أسكنها فيها لا تجب الأجرة، ولو استأجر داراً شهراً وسكن فيها مع صاحب الدار إلى آخر الشهر فقال المستأجر لا أدفع الأجرة لعدم التخلية فعليه من الأجرة بقدر ما في يده لوجود التخلية فيها .اهـ. ولو عبر بالفاء التفريعية لكان أولى ليفيد أنه متفرع على الاستيفاء والتمكن
The rent is daily, and for the camel owner per stage, and for the tailor and launderer after completion of his work, and for the baker daily - meaning attached to what exists of the benefit. And among the scholars, some said: This is when there is no time in the lease period during which there is desire to lease for it. If there is a time desired for lease due to increased demand, like a shop in a market whose prosperity is in part of the year, or a house in Mecca rented for a year for the season, and it was not delivered at the time desired for it, then he is given an option regarding some of the remaining [rent] to repel harm from him. End. He (Allah have mercy on him) said: 'And for the owner of the house and land is the demand for rent every day, and for the camel owner per stage' - meaning when the lease contract is absolute and the time of obligation of rent is not mentioned, then the lessor has what he mentioned. The basis for this is that lease is a contract of exchange, and ownership of benefits cannot be established at the time of contract, likewise ownership of the rent as we explained. The Imam initially used to say in all types of leases that rent is not obligatory until the benefit is availed, then he retracted to what is mentioned here. The analogy would dictate that rent becomes due hour by hour, but that leads to hardship, so we abandoned it for this. In al-Khulasa: A woman leased her house to her husband, then she resided in it - rent is not obligatory. If one rented a house for a month and lived in it with the owner until the end of the month, and the tenant said 'I will not pay rent due to lack of vacating' - then the rent is due proportionally for what he occupied because there was vacating in that. End. And if he had expressed with the particle 'fa' for sequence, it would be better to indicate that it is a branch on extraction and ability.
Source pages p. 11

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof regarding the timing of wage demand in an absolute ijara contract. The matn (base text) summarizes the times when each type of worker can demand their wage: landlord daily, camel owner per stage, tailor/launderer after completion, baker daily. The commentary explains that this applies when the contract is silent on the time of payment. The underlying principle is that ijara is an exchange contract, and just as ownership of benefits is not established at the moment of contract, ownership of the rent is also delayed until the benefit is provided. The commentary notes that Imam Abu Hanifa initially held that rent is not due until the benefit is fully received, but later retracted to the view stated here. The original analogy (qiyas) would have made rent due bit by bit (hourly), but that leads to hardship (haraj), so it was abandoned in favor of this easier ruling. A branch from al-Khulasa illustrates: if a woman rents her house to her husband and then lives in it herself, no rent is due because the benefit is not fully delivered to the husband. Also, if a tenant shares the house with the owner, rent is due proportionally because there is partial vacating.

Key Terms
أجرة (ujrah): Rent or wage in the context of ijara; compensation for a benefit.
إجارة مطلقة (ijarah mutlaqah): A hire contract that does not specify the time of payment.
استيفاء (istifa'): The actual receipt or utilization of the benefit.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In an absolute ijara contract for a house, when can the landlord demand the rent?
A) At the end of the lease
B) Daily
C) After one month
D) At the beginning of the contract

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, the default timing for demanding rent in absolute ijara contracts is daily for land, per stage for transport, and after completion for craftsmen, based on istihsan to avoid hardship.
