Tailor and Launderer Wage Timing
Clarifying wage entitlement for tailors/launderers

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rule for wage entitlement of tailors and launderers, distinguish between the general and detailed positions, and apply the concept of taslim to determine when payment is due.

Core Idea
A tailor's wage is not due upon completion alone; delivery (taslim) is required, except when working on the hirer's premises.

The passage addresses a practical question: when can a tailor or launderer demand payment? The matn seems to say 'after completion,' but the commentary reveals a nuanced rule. Understanding the role of delivery (taslim) and the location of work is crucial for correct application. This lesson unpacks the Hanafi position, its proof, and the operative ruling.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two positions
First, note that the matn and some sources (al-Hidayah) state the wage is due simply after completion (mutlaq). Other sources (Mabsut, etc.) add a condition: delivery (taslim) is required, except when working in the hirer's house. Distinguish these two views.
The 'mutlaq' view is from zahir al-riwayah; the detailed view is from later fatwa works.
2
Understand the proof via qiyas
The detailed view uses qiyas jaliy: the case of a builder who builds part of a wall then it collapses (asl). He is entitled to wage for what he built. Extend to the tailor sewing part of a garment that is stolen. The underlying illa is partial benefit realized through the worker's labour without fault.
The asl is from al-Asl (Imam Muhammad). The illa is jaliyyah (clear effective cause).
3
Apply the concept of taslim
Delivery (taslim) is the act that completes the worker's obligation and triggers full wage entitlement. For hiring a house, taslim is handing over keys; for a tailor, it is physically giving the garment to the owner. However, if the tailor works in the hirer's house, taslim occurs by virtue of the work being done on the hirer's property.
This distinction is key: location changes the requirement of physical handover.
4
Determine the mufta bihi
The later Hanafi authorities (al-Karkhi, Ghayat al-Bayan) affirm the detailed view: proportional wage if working in hirer's house, otherwise full wage upon actual delivery. This is the operative position for fatwa.
Thus, the general statement in the matn is restricted by the detailed view.
5
Note the practical outcome
A tailor working in his own shop is not entitled to payment until he hands over the finished garment. If the garment is stolen after completion but before delivery, he loses his wage. But if he works in the customer's home, he is entitled proportionally even if the garment is stolen partway.
Custom also determines who provides thread/needle, etc.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال رحمه الله : ( وللخياط والقصار بعد الفراغ من عمله) إذا وقعت الإجارة مطلقة عن وقت وجوب الأجرة فللعامل أن يطالب بعدما ذكر المؤلف . وأطلق في قوله بعد «الفراغ فأفاد أنه لا فرق بينهما إذا عمل في بيت نفسه أو في بيت المستأجر كما ذكره صاحب الهداية وصاحب التجريد، وذكر في المبسوط والفوائد الظهيرية والذخيرة ومبسوط شيخ الإسلام وشرح الجامع الصغير لفخر الإسلام وقاضيخان والتمرتاشي : إذا خاط في بيت المستأجر تجب الأجرة له بحسابه حتى إذا سرق الثوب بعدما خاط بعضه يستحق الأجرة بحسابه واستشهد في الأصل لهذا بما إذا استأجر إنساناً ليبني له حائطاً فبنى بعضه ثم انهدم فله أجر ما بنى فهذا يدل على أنه يستحق الأجرة ببعض العمل إلا أن يشترط فيه التسليم إلى المستأجر . ونقل هذا عن الكرخي وجزم به في غاية البيان فكان هو المذهب، ففي سكنى الدار وقطع المسافة صار مسلماً له بمجرد تسليم الدار، وقطع المسافة وفي الخياطة ونحوها لا يكون مسلماً إليه إلا إذا سلمه إلى صاحبه حقيقة، وفي الخياطة في منزل المستأجر يحصل التسليم بمجرد العمل إذ هو في منزله والمنزل في يده فلا يحتاج إلى تسليم ليده. ويعرف توزيع الأجرة بقول أهل الخبرة بها والخيط والأبرة على الخياط حيث كان العرف ذلك
He (Allah have mercy on him) said: 'And for the tailor and launderer after completion of his work.' When the hire contract is absolute regarding the time of obligation of the wage, then the worker can demand [it] after what the author mentioned. And he made absolute in his statement 'after completion', so it indicates that there is no difference between them when he works in his own house or in the house of the hirer, as mentioned by the author of al-Hidayah and the author of al-Tajrid. And it is mentioned in al-Mabsut, al-Fawa'id al-Zahiriyya, al-Dhakhira, Mabsut Shaykh al-Islam, Sharh al-Jami' al-Saghir by Fakhr al-Islam, Qadikhan, and al-Tamartashi: If he sewed in the hirer's house, the wage is due proportionally, so even if the garment was stolen after he sewed part of it, he is entitled to the wage proportionally. This is supported in al-Asl by the case where one hires a person to build a wall for him, and he builds part of it then it collapses: he is entitled to the wage for what he built. This indicates that he is entitled to the wage for part of the work unless delivery to the hirer is stipulated. This was reported from al-Karkhi and affirmed in Ghayat al-Bayan, so it is the madhhab. Thus, in residence of a house and covering distance, delivery (taslim) is achieved by merely handing over the house and covering the distance. In sewing and the like, delivery is not achieved unless he actually hands it over to its owner. But in sewing in the hirer's house, delivery is achieved by merely working because it is in his house and the house is in his possession, so there is no need for delivery into his hand. The distribution of the wage is known by the opinion of experts, and thread and needle are on the tailor where custom is like that.
Source pages p. 11

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof on the wage entitlement of tailors and launderers. The matn states that the tailor can demand his wage after finishing his work. The commentary clarifies that this refers to when the contract is silent on payment time. The author notes that the phrase 'after completion' is absolute, implying no difference between working in one's own home or the hirer's home according to some sources. However, other sources (Mabsut, etc.) differentiate: if the tailor works in the hirer's house, he is entitled to the wage proportionally even if the garment is stolen after partial work. The proof is an analogy from building: if a hired builder builds part of a wall and it collapses, he gets paid for what he built. The key concept is 'taslim' (delivery). For a house rental, delivery occurs when the house is handed over; for a tailor, delivery only occurs when the garment is physically handed to the owner, unless the sewing is done in the owner's house, where delivery happens by virtue of the work being in the owner's premises. The wage distribution is determined by experts, and custom decides who provides thread and needle.

Key Terms
تسليم (taslim): Delivery of the work to the hirer; the act that triggers full wage entitlement.
خياط (khayyat): Tailor; a worker hired for sewing.
قصار (qassar): Launderer; one who washes clothes.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, when does a tailor become entitled to his wage if he works in his own shop?
A) Immediately upon finishing the sewing
B) After handing the garment to the customer
C) Daily
D) At the end of the month

Key Takeaway
A tailor/launderer is entitled to wage only after delivery (taslim) unless the work is done on the hirer's premises, where proportional payment is due for partial work.

Baker's Wage and Liability for Burnt Bread
Explaining when the baker can demand his wage and the ruling on burnt bread

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions under which a baker is entitled to his wage and explain the liability for burnt bread in the Hanafi school, distinguishing the positions of Imam Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn.

Core Idea
The baker's wage is due upon delivery; liability for burning depends on location and timing.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq clarifies two interconnected questions in hiring a baker: when does he become entitled to his wage, and who bears the loss if the bread burns? The answer pivots on delivery (taslim) and location of baking. We'll walk through the rule, the analogy to a tailor, and the intra-Hanafi dispute over baking in the baker's own house.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
The matn states that the baker can demand his wage after removing the bread from the oven when the wage is absolute and no time is specified.
This is the default ruling; it assumes baking occurs at the hirer's premises.
2
Locate the dalil
The proof is an analogy (qiyas) to the tailor: just as the tailor is entitled to his wage upon finishing the garment, the baker is entitled upon completing the baking and removing from the oven. Additionally, delivery (taslim) is a condition for wage entitlement.
The analogy highlights that completion of work triggers wage, but only if delivery occurs.
3
Distinguish by location
If baking occurs in the hirer's house, removal from the oven constitutes delivery (taslim). If in the baker's own house, actual handover to the hirer is required.
Location determines whether removal alone suffices for delivery.
4
Analyze the burning scenarios
Three scenarios: (1) Bread burns after removal in hirer's house: no liability, wage due. (2) Burns in the oven before removal: liability (from al-Nihaya). (3) Burns in baker's own house after removal but before handover: dispute between Imam and Sahibayn.
Consensus exists for scenario (1); scenario (2) is based on a textual principle.
5
Understand the intra-Hanafi dispute
Imam Abu Hanifa holds no wage and no liability for burning in the baker's house. The Sahibayn hold the baker is liable (must compensate) and likely still entitled to wage if he delivers.
The thamarah al-khilaf: owner's ability to claim compensation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال رحمه الله : (وللخباز بعد إخراج الخبز من التنور يعني إذا أطلق الأجرة ولم يبين وقتها فللخباز أن يطالب بها بعد إخراج الخبز من التنور لأنه بأخراجه قد فرغ من فيملك المطالبة كالخياط إذا فرغ من العمل حتى إذا أخبزه في بيت المستأجر لأنه صار مسلماً إليه بمجرد الإخراج فيستحق الأجرة، وإن كان في منزل الخباز لم يكن مسلماً بمجرد الإخراج من التنور فلا بد من التسليم إلى يده. وفي المحيط : استأجر دابة ليطحن عليها كل يوم عشرة أقفزة فوجدها لا تطيق إلا خمسة فله الخيار وعليه الأجر بحساب ما عمل من الأيام ولا يحط من الأجر شيئاً لأن الإجارة وقعت على الوقت لا على العمل فلا توزع الأجرة على العمل، وفي المسئلة إشكال على قول الإمام لأنه إذا استأجر خبازاً ليخبز له اليوم بدرهم يكون فاسداً. والفرق أن مقدار العمل في باب الطحن في العرف والعادة لا يذكر لتعليق العقد بالعمل وإنما يذكر لبيان قوة الدابة فبقيت الإجارة على القوت وفي الخبز يذكر مقدار العمل لتعليق العقد بالعمل لا لبيان قوة الخباز فيصير العقد مجهولاً فيفسد. قال (فإن أخرجه فاحترق فله الأجر ولا ضمان عليه يعني إذا أخرج الخبز من التنور ثم احترق هذا إذا خبز في منزل المستأجر لأنه بمجرد الإخراج صار مسلماً ولا يجب عليه الضمان إذا بعد ذلك بالإجماع لأنه هلك بعد التسليم ولو احترق في التنور قبل الإخراج قال في النهاية : يضمن لأنه جناية يده وإن كان الخباز يخبز في منزل نفسه لا يستحق الأجر بالإخراج ولا يجب عليه الضمان عند الإمام، وعندهما يجب الضمان. وإذا صار ضامناً فالمالك بالخيار إن شاء ضمنه دقيقاً مثل دقيقه ولا أجر له وإن شاء ضمنه الخبز وأعطاه الأجر ولا يجب عليه ضمان الحطب والملح لأن ذلك صار مستهلكاً قبل وجوب الضمان عليه ما وجب عليه الضمان كان رماداً
He (Allah have mercy on him) said: 'And for the baker after taking the bread out of the oven' - meaning when the wage is absolute and its time is not specified, then the baker can demand it after taking the bread out of the oven, because by taking it out he has completed his work and thus has the right to demand, like the tailor when he finishes the work. Even if he baked it in the hirer's house, because it becomes delivered to him by merely taking it out, so he is entitled to the wage. And if it is in the baker's house, it is not delivered by merely taking it out of the oven, so delivery into the hirer's hand is necessary. In al-Muhit: If one hires a donkey to grind ten qafiz daily and finds it can only manage five, he has the option and owes the wage proportional to the days worked, and nothing is deducted from the wage because the contract fell on time, not on work, so the wage is not distributed on work. There is an issue in this question according to the Imam because if one hires a baker to bake for him a dirham's worth today, it is invalid. The difference is that in grinding, the amount of work is not mentioned to attach the contract to the work but to indicate the strength of the donkey, so the contract remains on time; in baking, the amount of work is mentioned to attach the contract to the work, not to indicate the strength of the baker, so the contract becomes uncertain and is invalid. He said: 'And if he took it out and it burned, he gets the wage and no liability upon him' - meaning if he took the bread out of the oven and then it burned. This applies when he baked in the hirer's house because by mere taking out it became delivered, and he is not liable thereafter by consensus because it perished after delivery. If it burned in the oven before taking out, it is said in al-Nihaya: He is liable because it is an act of his hand. And if the baker bakes in his own house, he is not entitled to the wage by taking out and no liability upon him according to the Imam; according to the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), liability is due. If he becomes liable, the owner has the option: if he wishes, he may hold him liable for dough like his dough and no wage for him; and if he wishes, he may hold him liable for bread and pay him the wage. And he is not liable for the firewood and salt because those were consumed before liability became due; when liability became due, they were ashes.
Source pages p. 11

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof and an intra-Hanafi dispute on the baker's wage. The matn states that the baker can demand his wage after removing the bread from the oven. The commentary explains: when the contract is silent, the baker is entitled upon taking the bread out because that constitutes completion of work, analogous to the tailor. If he bakes in the hirer's house, delivery is achieved upon removal; if in his own house, delivery requires actual handover. A branch from al-Muhit discusses hiring a donkey: if it cannot do the expected work, the hirer has an option but pays per day because the contract is on time, not work. The commentator contrasts this with baking where specifying quantity leads to invalidity due to uncertainty. The key part is the burning scenario: if bread burns after removal from the oven (in hirer's house), the baker is entitled to his wage and has no liability because delivery already occurred. If it burns in the oven before removal, he is liable (according to al-Nihaya) because it is his negligence. If he bakes in his own house, the Imam holds that he neither gets the wage nor is liable for the burn; the two Sahibayn hold he is liable. If liable, the owner can claim compensation for dough and pay no wage, or claim for bread and pay the wage. Wood and salt are not compensated because they are consumed before liability.

Key Terms
خباز (khabbaz): Baker; a person hired to bake bread.
تسليم (taslim): Delivery of the baked bread to the hirer, which triggers full wage entitlement and transfers risk.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
A baker hired to bake bread in his own house takes the bread out of the oven, but it catches fire and is destroyed before delivery. According to Imam Abu Hanifa, what is the ruling?
A) The baker is entitled to his wage and must compensate for the bread.
B) The baker is entitled to his wage but no liability.
C) The baker is not entitled to his wage and is not liable.
D) The baker is not entitled to his wage but must compensate.

Key Takeaway
The baker's wage is tied to delivery; liability for burning hinges on location and timing, with an intra-Hanafi disagreement on baking in the baker's own house.

Cook's Wage Timing and the Role of Custom (Urf)
Ruling statement with expansion via customary examples

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the default rule for the cook's wage entitlement and explain how custom (urf) can modify obligations in a hire contract.

Core Idea
The cook's wage is due after serving, but custom can shift the duty to serve.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq addresses a practical issue in hire contracts: when does a cook become entitled to his wage? The default rule is that he can demand payment after serving the food (gharf). However, custom plays a crucial role: if the cook was hired only to cook a specific quantity without serving, then he is not obligated to serve, and his wage is due earlier. The passage then generalizes the principle that in hire contracts, customary practices define the parties' duties.

Guided Path
1
Identify the default rule
The passage states that the cook can demand his wage after gharf (serving). This is the default ruling for a cook hired without specific conditions.
2
Recognize the exception
If the cook is hired to cook a specific pot (without serving), the default does not apply; custom determines whether serving is his duty.
The exception is based on the principle 'al-urf muhakkam' (custom is authoritative).
3
Extract the general principle
The author cites examples from al-Tatarkhaniyya to show that in all hire contracts, customary practices define duties regarding equipment and ancillary tasks, such as providing a saddle for a hired donkey or throwing dust on a grave.
This illustrates the broader Hanafi reliance on urf in mu'amalat.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال رحمه الله : (وللطباخ بعد الغرف) يعني للطباخ أن يطالب بالأجرة بعد الغرف لأن الغرف عليه وهذا إذا طبخ للوليمة أو للعرس، فإن كان يطبخ قدراً خاصاً فليس عليه الغرف لأن العادة لم تجربه والمعتبر هو العرف. وفي التتارخانية : وإن استأجر دابة للحمل ففي الإكاف والجوالق يعتبر العرف ولو للركوب ففي اللجام والسرج يعتبر العرف وفي إدخال الطعام المنزول وإخراج الحمل يعتبر العرف، وإحثاء التراب على القبر على الحفار وحمل الثوب على القصار
He (Allah have mercy on him) said: 'And for the cook after serving (gharf)' meaning the cook can demand the wage after serving because the serving is upon him. This applies when he cooks for a wedding feast. If he cooks a specific pot, then serving is not upon him because custom has not made it so; and the criterion is custom. In al-Tatarkhaniyya: And if one hires a donkey for carrying, then concerning the pack-saddle and saddlebag, custom is considered; if for riding, then concerning the bridle and saddle, custom is considered; and concerning bringing in the food when dismounting and taking out the load, custom is considered; and throwing dust on the grave is upon the grave-digger, and carrying the cloth upon the launderer.
Source pages p. 12

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement that the cook can demand his wage after serving (gharf) the food. The default is that serving is part of the cook's duty. However, if the contract is for a specific pot (e.g., just cooking without serving), then serving is not upon him; custom determines the division of duties. The commentary cites al-Tatarkhaniyya to illustrate the general principle that in hire contracts, customary practices determine obligations such as providing equipment (saddle, etc.) or performing ancillary tasks. For example, for a hired donkey, who provides the saddle depends on custom; similarly, for a grave-digger, throwing dust is part of his job; for a launderer, carrying the cloth is his responsibility.

Key Terms
غرف (gharf): Serving the cooked food; the act of dishing out.
عرف (urf): Custom; used to determine the obligations of parties in a hire contract when not explicitly stated.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Under what condition is the cook not required to serve (gharf) the food?
A) When he is hired for a wedding feast
B) When he is hired to cook a specific pot without serving
C) When he demands his wage early
D) When the food is burnt

Key Takeaway
The cook's wage is due after serving, but custom can override this default; in hire contracts, customary practices determine the parties' obligations.

Brick-maker's Wage Entitlement: Dispute on Completion
Intra-Hanafi dispute on wage entitlement in brick-making contract.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the positions of Imam Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn regarding when a brick-maker's wage becomes due, and apply the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf) to a given scenario.

Core Idea
The brick-maker's wage is due upon completing the work; the Imam and Sahibayn differ on whether erection or stacking completes it.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq examines an intra-Hanafi dispute on when a hired brick-maker becomes entitled to his wage. The matn states the wage is due after iqama (erection), but the commentary reveals a disagreement. Let's explore the reasoning and practical difference.

Guided Path
1
Identify the parties and issue
Recognize that the dispute is between Imam Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) regarding the moment the brick-maker becomes entitled to his wage.
The contract is for making bricks on the hirer's land.
2
State the Imam's position and proof
Imam holds that wage is due after iqama (erection). His proof: the work is completed when benefit is possible; delivery occurs by erection on the hirer's land.
See the hanafi_dalil in the dispute map.
3
State the Sahibayn's position and proof
Sahibayn hold that wage is due only after tashrih (stacking). Their proof: stacking is necessary for preservation and is customary; custom is like a stipulated condition.
Their view is based on istihsan.
4
Analyze the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference appears if bricks are spoiled after iqama but before tashrih: Imam says wage due, loss on hirer; Sahibayn say wage not due, loss on worker.
Also if bricks are destroyed before stacking: loss on hirer (Imam) vs loss on worker (Sahibayn).
5
Apply to a given scenario
Given a scenario, determine the ruling according to each view, considering the status of the land (hirer's or worker's).
If made on worker's own land, wage not due until delivery.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال رحمه الله : (وللبان بعد الإقامة) يعني إذا استأجره ليضرب له لبناً في أرضه يستحق الأجرة إذا أقامه عند الإمام. وقالا : لا يستحق حتى يشرحه لأن التشريج من تمام عمله لأنه لا يؤمن عليه الفساد إلا به، ولأنه هو الذي يتولاه عادة والمعتاد كالمشروط وقولهما استحسان وللإمام أن العمل قد تم بالإقامة والانتفاع به ممكن. وثمرة الخلاف تظهر فيما إذا أفسده المطر ونحوه بعد الإقامة فعنده تجب الأجرة، وعندهما لا تجب. هذا إذا لبن في أرض المستأجر لأنه يصير مسلماً إليه بالإقامة أو بالتشريج على اختلاف الأصلين ولو لبن في أرض نفسه لا تستحق الأجرة حتى يسلمه إليه. وفي الجوهرة وفائدة الخلاف تظهر فيما إذا أتلف اللبن قبل التشريح فعند الإمام هلك مال المستأجر، وعندهما من مال الأجير والتشريج أن يركب بعضه على بعض بعد
He (Allah have mercy on him) said: 'And for the brick-maker after erection (iqama).' Meaning, if one hires him to make bricks for him in his land, he is entitled to the wage when he erects them according to Imam (Abu Hanifa). And the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) said: He is not entitled until he stacks (yusharrih) them, because stacking is part of his complete work, since the bricks cannot be secured from spoilage except by it, and because he is the one who usually does it, and custom is like a condition, and their view is istihsan. For the Imam, the work is completed by erection and benefiting from it is possible. The practical consequence appears if rain or the like spoils them after erection: according to Imam, the wage is due; according to the two, it is not due. This applies if he made bricks in the hirer's land because it becomes delivered to him by erection or by stacking according to the two principles. If he made bricks on his own land, no wage is due until he delivers them to him. In al-Jawhara: The benefit of the difference appears if the bricks are destroyed before stacking: according to Imam, the loss is on the hirer; according to the two, from the worker's property. And al-tashrih is to place some on top of others afterwards.
Source pages p. 12

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the brick-maker's (al-labban) wage entitlement. The matn states that his wage is due after 'iqama' (erecting the bricks). The commentary explains the disagreement: Imam Abu Hanifa holds that erecting the bricks is sufficient completion because the owner can benefit from them at that point. Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (the Sahibayn) argue that stacking (tashrih) the bricks is necessary for their preservation and is customary, so the wage is only due after stacking. Their view is based on istihsan because custom dictates that stacking is part of the work. The practical difference (thamaratal khilaf) appears if rain spoils the bricks after erection: according to Imam, the wage is due (since the work is completed and risk passes to the hirer); according to the Sahibayn, the wage is not due (since the work was incomplete). Also, if the bricks are destroyed before stacking, Imam says the loss is on the hirer (hirer's property), while the Sahibayn say it is from the worker's property (i.e., the worker bears the loss). The commentary also notes that this ruling applies when the bricks are made on the hirer's land; if made on the worker's own land, no wage is due until actual delivery.

Key Terms
إقامة (iqama): Erecting or setting up the bricks in rows; considered by Imam as completion of the work.
تشريج (tashrih): Stacking bricks (placing on top of each other) for drying and preservation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Brick-maker hired to make bricks on the hirer's land erects the bricks but does not stack them. Then rain damages the bricks. According to Imam Abu Hanifa, what is the ruling?
A) The brick-maker is entitled to his full wage; the loss is on the hirer.
B) The brick-maker is not entitled to his wage; the loss is on him.
C) The brick-maker is entitled to half his wage.
D) The contract is void.

Key Takeaway
The brick-maker's wage entitlement depends on completion, but the definition of completion varies between Imam (erection) and Sahibayn (stacking), with practical consequences for loss and custom playing a key role.

When Is a Baker Entitled to Wages and Not Liable for Burnt Bread?
Explains the baker's entitlement to wages and liability when bread burns after removal

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the moment of delivery (taslim) that transfers risk to the hirer, and distinguish the positions of Imam Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn regarding liability when baking occurs in the baker's own house.

Core Idea
Delivery of the bread to the hirer transfers risk; before delivery, the baker bears the loss.

This passage from Al-Bahr al-Raiq addresses a common scenario in hire contracts: a baker burns the bread after removing it from the oven. The key legal concept is delivery (taslim), which determines both the baker's entitlement to wages and his liability for loss. We will examine the conditions under which the baker is liable, including the intra-Hanafi dispute when baking occurs in the baker's own home.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Key Scenarios
Note the two scenarios: baking in the hirer's house vs. baking in the baker's own house.
The ruling differs based on location.
2
Determine the Moment of Delivery
In the hirer's house, removal from the oven constitutes delivery (taslim). The baker earns wages and is not liable after that point.
Consensus on no liability after delivery.
3
Apply the Rule Before Delivery
If the bread burns before removal, the baker is liable because it is a tort of his hand (jinayat al-yad).
Reference to al-Nihayah.
4
Analyze the Intra-Hanafi Dispute
When baking in the baker's own house, Imam Abu Hanifa holds that removal does not constitute delivery; thus no wage and no liability. Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (the Sahibayn) hold the baker liable.
The text says 'عندهما يجب الضمان' – liability is imposed.
5
Consequences of Liability
If the baker becomes liable, the hirer may choose to claim flour (unprocessed) or bread (processed) with wage adjustment. The baker is not liable for consumed items like firewood and salt.
The hirer's options protect both parties.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال (فإن أخرجه فاحترق فله الأجر ولا ضمان عليه يعني إذا أخرج الخبز من التنور ثم احترق هذا إذا خبز في منزل المستأجر لأنه بمجرد الإخراج صار مسلماً ولا يجب عليه الضمان إذا بعد ذلك بالإجماع لأنه هلك بعد التسليم ولو احترق في التنور قبل الإخراج قال في النهاية : يضمن لأنه جناية يده وإن كان الخباز يخبز في منزل نفسه لا يستحق الأجر بالإخراج ولا يجب عليه الضمان عند الإمام، وعندهما يجب الضمان. وإذا صار ضامناً فالمالك بالخيار إن شاء ضمنه دقيقاً مثل دقيقه ولا أجر له، وإن شاء ضمنه الخبز وأعطاه الأجر ولا يجب عليه ضمان الحطب والملح لأن ذلك صار مستهلكاً قبل وجوب الضمان عليه ما وجب عليه الضمان كان رماداً .
He said: If he takes it out and it burns, he gets the wage and no liability upon him. Meaning: if he took the bread out of the oven and then it burns, this is when he baked in the hirer's house, because by mere removal it becomes delivered, and he is not liable thereafter by consensus, because it perished after delivery. If it burned in the oven before removal, he said in al-Nihayah: he is liable because it is a tort of his hand. If the baker bakes in his own house, he does not deserve the wage by removal, nor is he liable according to Imam Abu Hanifa, but according to them (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) he is liable. If he becomes liable, the owner has the choice: if he wishes, he may hold him liable for flour like his flour, and no wage for him; if he wishes, he may hold him liable for bread and give him the wage. He is not liable for the firewood and salt because that was consumed before liability became due; what became liable upon him was ashes.
Source pages p. 12

Commentary
This passage is a ruling-with-proof from the commentary on Kanz al-Daqa'iq. It clarifies the scenario of a hired baker when bread burns. The key point is the concept of delivery (taslim): by removing the bread from the oven, the baker delivers the work to the hirer, so any subsequent damage is not the baker's responsibility. This is explicit if the baking occurs in the hirer's premises. If the bread burns before removal, the baker is liable because the work was not yet delivered. The text also distinguishes between baking in the hirer's house versus the baker's own house. In the latter, Imam Abu Hanifa holds that removal does not constitute delivery because the bread remains in the baker's dominion, so no wage is earned and no liability arises from removal. However, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (the Sahibayn) hold that removal is sufficient for delivery even in the baker's house, so if it burns after removal, the baker is not liable; but if it burns before removal, they differ? Actually the text states: for baking in his own house, at Imam Abu Hanifa he does not deserve wage by removal and is not liable; according to them he is liable. This seems to be about the case of burning before removal? The text is ambiguous. The commentator clarifies the owner's options when the baker is liable: he can claim flour (unprocessed) or bread (processed) with respective adjustments. The firewood and salt are not compensated because they were already consumed and are not part of the work product.

Key Terms
تسليم (taslīm): Delivery of the work product to the hirer, placing it at his risk
ضمان (ḍamān): Legal liability for loss or damage, requiring compensation
جناية اليد (jināyat al-yad): A wrongful act committed by the hand (tort) leading to liability

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
When does the baker become entitled to wages if he bakes in the hirer's house?
A) As soon as he finishes kneading the dough
B) When he removes the bread from the oven
C) When the hirer tastes the bread
D) Only after the hirer acknowledges satisfaction

Key Takeaway
The moment of delivery (taslim) is critical in hire: once the baker removes the bread from the oven, risk passes to the hirer, and the baker is entitled to wages and free from liability, except in the case of baking in the baker's own house where there is an intra-Hanafi dispute.

When Do Hired Workers Earn Their Wages? The Role of Custom (ʿUrf)
Expands matn on ijara completion using cook and brick maker examples, detailing custom's role and internal Hanafi dispute.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain how custom determines completion of work in ijara contracts and apply the Hanafi ruling for cooks and brick makers, distinguishing the positions of Imam Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn.

Core Idea
In Hanafi ijara, wage entitlement depends on delivery; custom defines what counts as delivery, not mere effort.

This lesson explores how the Hanafi school determines when a hired worker becomes entitled to wages, using the examples of a cook and a brick maker. The key is not simply performing work, but completing work in a way that delivers the product to the hirer according to custom. You will see how Imam Abu Hanifa and his two disciples differ on the exact point of completion, and how the principle of custom (urf) resolves many practical disputes.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two workers and their tasks
The passage discusses a cook (tabbakh) who prepares food and a brick maker (labbān) who molds bricks. Their wage entitlement hinges on what constitutes completion.
2
Understand the general principle: wage entitlement = delivery
The text makes clear that entitlement arises upon delivery (taslīm) of the work, not merely performing the task. Custom determines what delivery means in each trade.
For the cook, serving (gharf) is delivery if customary.
3
Analyze the role of custom for the cook
If a cook is hired for a wedding feast, custom expects him to serve the food; thus wage is due after serving. If hired to cook a specific pot, custom does not require serving.
The principle: 'العرف معتبر' (custom is considered).
4
Analyze the brick maker dispute
Imam Abu Hanifa holds that stacking (iqāmah) the wet bricks in rows completes the work. The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) require shaping (tashrīḥ) – placing dried bricks on top of each other – because it prevents spoilage and is customary.
Their view is presented as istihsan (juristic preference).
5
Apply the practical consequence (thamarah)
The difference matters if rain spoils bricks after stacking but before shaping: Imam says wage is due (work complete), Sahibayn say wage not due (work incomplete). Also, if bricks are destroyed before shaping, loss falls on hirer per Imam, on worker per Sahibayn.
Location matters: if bricks made on worker's land, delivery requires physical handover.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال رحمه الله : (وللطباخ بعد الغرف) يعني للطباخ أن يطالب بالأجرة بعد الغرف لأن الغرف عليه وهذا إذا طبخ للوليمة أو للعرس، فإن كان يطبخ قدراً خاصاً فليس عليه الغرف لأن العادة لم تجربه والمعتبر هو العرف. وفي التتارخانية : وإن استأجر دابة للحمل ففي الإكاف والجوالق يعتبر العرف ولو للركوب ففي اللجام والسرج يعتبر العرف وفي إدخال الطعام المنزول وإخراج الحمل يعتبر العرف، وإحثاء التراب على القبر على الحفار وحمل الثوب على القصار . قال رحمه الله : (وللبان بعد الإقامة) يعني إذا استأجره ليضرب له لبناً في أرضه يستحق الأجرة إذا أقامه عند الإمام. وقالا : لا يستحق حتى يشرحه لأن التشريج من تمام عمله لأنه لا يؤمن عليه الفساد إلا به، ولأنه هو الذي يتولاه عادة والمعتاد كالمشروط وقولهما استحسان وللإمام أن العمل قد تم بالإقامة والانتفاع به ممكن. وثمرة الخلاف تظهر فيما إذا أفسده المطر ونحوه بعد الإقامة فعنده تجب الأجرة، وعندهما لا تجب. هذا إذا لبن في أرض المستأجر لأنه يصير مسلماً إليه بالإقامة أو بالتشريج على اختلاف الأصلين ولو لبن في أرض نفسه لا تستحق الأجرة حتى يسلمه إليه. وفي الجوهرة وفائدة الخلاف تظهر فيما إذا أتلف اللبن قبل التشريح فعند الإمام هلك مال المستأجر، وعندهما من مال الأجير والتشريج أن يركب بعضه على بعض بعد الجفاف.
He (the author) said: And for the cook after serving (gharf). Meaning: the cook may demand the wage after serving because the serving is upon him. This is when he cooks for a wedding or a feast. If he cooks a specific pot, then serving is not upon him because custom has not established it, and custom is considered. In al-Tatarkhaniyyah: If he hires an animal for carrying, the custom regarding the packsaddle and saddlebag is considered; if for riding, custom regarding the bridle and saddle is considered; regarding bringing in food and taking out the load, custom is considered; and throwing dust on the grave is upon the digger, and carrying the cloth upon the washer. He (the author) said: And for the brick maker after stacking (iqamah). Meaning: if he hires him to make bricks for him in his land, he deserves the wage when he stacks them, according to Imam Abu Hanifa. But the two disciples said: he does not deserve until he shapes them (tashrih) because shaping completes his work, as it is not safe from corruption without it, and because it is customary for him to do it, and the customary is like the stipulated. Their view is istihsan. For the Imam, the work is completed by stacking and benefit is possible. The fruit of the dispute appears when rain or the like spoils them after stacking: according to him the wage is obligatory, according to them not. This is when he makes bricks in the hirer's land, because it becomes delivered to him by stacking or by shaping according to the two principles. If he makes bricks in his own land, he does not deserve the wage until he delivers it to him. In al-Jawharah: and the benefit of the dispute appears when the bricks are destroyed before shaping: according to Imam, the hirer's property is destroyed; according to them, it is the hiree's property. And tashrih is to place some upon others after drying.
Source pages p. 12

Commentary
This passage is an expansion of the matn on when different types of hired workers become entitled to their wages. The author uses the examples of a cook and a brick maker. For the cook, the key determinant is the act of serving (gharf) - the cook is entitled to wages after he has served the food. But this depends on custom (urf): if the cook is hired for a wedding feast, custom holds that serving is part of his duty, so he is entitled after serving. If he is hired to cook a specific dish in a pot, custom does not require him to serve, so he may be entitled earlier. General principle: custom is considered. The author then cites a passage from al-Tatarkhaniyyah extending this principle to various hiring scenarios (animals, grave digging, washing). For the brick maker, the disciple and Imam differ: Imam Abu Hanifa holds that stacking (placing the wet bricks in rows to dry) completes the work and entitles the worker to wages, because the bricks are then usable. Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (the Sahibayn) hold that shaping (tashrih) is also necessary because it prevents spoilage and is customary. The practical consequence (thamara) is seen if rain spoils the bricks after stacking: if stacking is sufficient, the wage is due despite spoilage; if shaping is required, the wage is not due because the work was not complete. The location of the work also matters: if the bricks are made on the hirer's land, delivery occurs by stacking (or shaping) as per the dispute; if on the worker's own land, delivery is not complete until physical handover. The Imam and disciples also differ on who bears the loss if the bricks are destroyed before shaping: according to Imam, since the work is completed at stacking, the loss is on the hirer; according to them, the worker still owns the bricks, so loss is on him.

Key Terms
العرف (al-ʿurf): Customary practice that determines the scope of work and delivery in hiring contracts
الإقامة (al-iqāmah): Stacking bricks in rows after molding to dry
التشريج (al-tashrīḥ): Shaping or arranging bricks by placing some upon others after drying

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the text, what determines whether a hired cook is entitled to wages after serving the food?
A) The type of contract
B) The cook's personal effort
C) Custom
D) The hirer's satisfaction

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi ijara, wage entitlement is tied to delivery, and delivery is defined by custom, not mere performance.

Right of Retention for Artisans: The Effect Requirement
Establishes the right of artisans with visible effect to retain the object until payment

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on when an artisan may detain the work object and explain the dispute regarding work without a lasting effect.

Core Idea
Artisans whose work leaves a visible effect may detain the object until paid; the correct view extends this even to restorative work.

This lesson explores the Hanafi rule that certain artisans—like dyers and washers—have the right to retain the object of their work until they are paid. The key is whether the work leaves a perceptible effect. We will examine the basis of this right, the disagreement within the school, and its practical application.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Ruling and Its Scope
Read the opening statement: 'Those whose work leaves an effect in the object... may retain it for the wage.' Note that the right is not for all hired workers, only those whose work produces a visible change.
The passage uses dyers (صباغ) and washers (قصار) as examples.
2
Understand the Proof via Qiyas to Sale
The author likens the artisan's position to a seller: in sale, the seller detains the sold item until payment because the consideration is for the item itself. Here, the contract is for a quality (wasf) in the object, so the artisan can detain until paid.
This is a qiyas jaliy (clear analogy).
3
Analyze the Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Zufar argues that work attaching to another's property should not give a retention right, analogizing to sowing seeds on another's land. The majority responds that the attachment is necessary for the work to exist, and the hirer consents to that attachment.
The dispute turns on whether the artisan is 'forced' by the nature of the work.
4
Apply the Rule to Edge Cases
The 'fruit of the dispute' is visible in cases like woodcutting or shaving a slave's head. According to Zufar's view (no lasting effect), no retention; according to the correct view (any visible result), retention is allowed.
The text also notes an exception: if the wage is deferred and work not yet done, no retention.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال رحمه الله : (ومن لعمله أثر في العين كالصباغ والقصار يحبسها للأجر) يعني لمن ذكر أن يحبس العين إذا عمل حتى يستوفي الأجر لأن المعقود عليه وصف في المحل فكان له حق الحبس لاستيفاء البدل كما في البيع . قال في النهاية : القصار إذا ظهر عمله باستعمال النشأ كان له حق الحبس، وإن لم يكن لعمله إلا إزالة الدرن اختلفوا فيه، والأصح أن له الحبس على كل حال لأن البياض كان مستتراً وقد ظهر بفعله بعد أن كان هالكاً. وقال زفر : ليس له الحبس لأنه صار متصلاً بملك الآخر كما لو أمر شخصاً بأن يزرع له أرضه ببذر من عنده قرضاً فزرعها المأمور صار قابضاً باتصاله بملكه فصار كما إذا صبغ في بيت المستأجر . قلنا : اتصال العمل بالمحل ضرورة إقامة العلم فلم يكن راضياً بهذا الاتصال من حيث إنه تسليم بل رضاه في تحقيق عمل الصبغ ونحوه من الأثر في المحل إذ لا وجود للعمل إلا به فكان مضطراً إليه، وليس هذا كصبغه في بيت المستأجر لأن العين في يد المستأجر فيكون راضياً بالتسليم لأنه كان يمكنه التحرز عنه بأن يعمل في غير بيته. وفي الخلاصة: إلا إذا كانت الأجرة مؤجلة وقبل العمل فليس له الحبس .اهـ والمراد بالأثر أن يكون الأثر متصلاً بمحل العمل كالنشاء والصبغ وقبل أن يرى ويعاين في محل العمل وثمرة الخلاف تظهر في كسر الحطب وحلق رأس العبد فليس له الحبس على الأول وله الحبس على الثاني .
He (the author) said: And those whose work leaves an effect in the object, like the dyer and the washer, may retain it for the wage. Meaning: that the mentioned persons may detain the object after working until they receive the wage, because what is contracted is a quality in the object, so they have the right to detain for receiving the consideration, as in sale. In al-Nihayah: The washer, if his work appears by using starch, he has the right to detain. If his work is only removing dirt, they differed; the correct view is that he has the right to detain in any case, because the whiteness was hidden and became apparent by his action after being as if non-existent. Zufar said: he does not have the right to detain, because it became attached to someone else's property, just as if a person ordered someone to sow his land with seeds from the latter as a loan, and the agent sowed it, he becomes possessor by attachment to his property, so it is like if he dyed in the hirer's house. We reply: attachment of the work to the object is necessary for the work's existence, so he was not satisfied with this attachment as delivery; rather his satisfaction is in realizing the work of dyeing and similar effects in the object, since the work has no existence except through it, so he was forced into it. This is not like his dyeing in the hirer's house, because the object is in the hirer's hand, so he is satisfied with delivery because he could have avoided it by working outside his house. In al-Khulasah: Except if the wage is deferred and before work, then he has no right to detain. End. What is meant by effect is that the effect is attached to the work object, like starch and dye, and before it is seen and inspected in the work place. The fruit of the dispute appears in the case of breaking firewood and shaving a slave's head: according to the first (Zufar's view) he has no right to detain; according to the second (the correct view) he has the right to detain.
Source pages p. 13

Commentary
This passage is a ruling from the commentary on the matn concerning the right of retention (habs) for artisans whose work leaves a perceptible effect in the object, such as dyers and washers. The ruling is that they may retain the object until they are paid their wages. The reasoning is that the subject matter of the contract is a quality (wasf) in the object, not the object itself, so the artisan has a right to hold it as security, analogous to the seller's right to withhold the sold item until payment. The text then discusses what constitutes an 'effect'. For a washer, if starch is used (leaving a visible effect), there is no dispute. If only dirt is removed, there is disagreement. The correct view (al-asahh) is that even removal of dirt gives a right to detain because the whiteness was hidden and the action made it apparent. Then it presents Zufar's objection: he analogizes to a case where a person sows seeds on another's land; the seeds become part of the land, so the sower cannot detain. Similarly, the artisan's work is inseparable from the object. The Hanafi response is that the attachment is a necessity (darura) for the work to exist; the hirer's consent is to the effect, not to an unauthorized attachment. The distinction is made with dyeing in the hirer's house (where the hirer controls the premises, so he is considered satisfied with delivery). The text also notes an exception from al-Khulasah: if the wage is deferred and the work is not yet started, there is no right to detain. Finally, the practical difference between Zufar's view and the correct view is shown in cases like woodcutting (breaking firewood) and shaving a slave's head: according to the view that denies retention for non-effect work, there is no right; according to the view that gives retention for any work (even without lasting trace), there is right. The passage does not indicate which is the mufta bihi.

Key Terms
الحبس (al-ḥabs): The right to detain the object of work until payment of wages, a form of possessory lien
الأثر (al-athar): A visible effect or trace left by the artisan's work in the object
الوصف (al-waṣf): The quality or attribute that is the subject matter of the hire contract

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the correct view in the text, does a washer have the right to detain clothes if his work only removes dirt without using starch?
A) Yes, because the whiteness becomes apparent
B) No, because no visible effect remains
C) Yes, only if stated in the contract
D) No, because removing dirt is not considered work

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school grants artisans whose work leaves a perceptible effect the right to detain the object until paid; the correct view extends this even to work that restores a hidden quality.

Liability and Wage Upon Loss of Retained Object
Determines liability and wage when artisan detains and object is lost

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state Imam Abu Hanifa's position on liability and wage when a hired artisan rightfully detains an object and it is accidentally lost, and explain the Sahibayn's alternative view with its practical consequence.

Core Idea
Rightful detention makes the object a trust: no liability but no wage.

This lesson addresses a common scenario in hire contracts (ijarah): the artisan completes work but is not paid, so he retains the object. If the object is then accidentally lost, who bears the loss? Is the artisan still entitled to his wage? Imam Abu Hanifa draws an analogy to sale, ruling that loss before delivery cancels both liability and wage. The Sahibayn differ, holding that the artisan was already liable from the start of work. We will dissect the reasoning and the practical difference.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the ruling
The artisan detains the object rightfully (because he has not been paid). The object is then lost without his fault. The matn rules: no liability on him and no wage.
The ruling applies only when detention is legally permitted.
2
Locate the dalil
The commentator provides an analogy to sale: if the object of sale perishes before delivery, the price drops. Similarly, here the work perished before delivery to the owner, so the wage drops.
This is qiyas jaliy (manifest analogy).
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah (reasoning link)
In both sale and hire, the consideration (price or wage) is due in exchange for delivery of the object or work. Loss before delivery means the countervalue was never received, so the consideration is not owed.
The effective cause (illah) is non-delivery of the promised benefit.
4
Note the ikhtilaf (the Sahibayn's view)
Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani hold that the artisan is liable because the object was already guaranteed (mamdumah) upon him from the moment he took it for work. Detention does not remove that liability. The owner has an option: either claim the unworked value (giving no wage) or the worked value (giving the wage).
For the Sahibayn, liability precedes detention.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf (practical consequence)
Under Imam Abu Hanifa, the owner bears the full loss and the artisan gets nothing. Under the Sahibayn, the owner can shift part of the loss by claiming the worked value, which effectively gives the artisan his wage.
The difference affects risk allocation and the artisan's incentive to safeguard the object.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال رحمه الله : (وإن حبس فضاع فلا ضمان عليه ولا أجر) أما عدم الضمان فلان العين أمانة في يده وله حبس العين شرعاً فلم يكن به متعدياً فلا يجب عليه الضمان ولا يجب الأجر لأن المعقود عليه هلك قبل التسليم وهو يوجب سقوط البدل كما في البيع وهو قول الإمام أحمد وعندهما يضمن العين لأنها كانت مضمومة عليه قبل الحبس فلا يسقط ذلك بالحبس، وصاحب العين بالخيار إن شاء ضمنه قيمته غير معمول ولا أجر له لأن العمل لم يسلم إليه، وإن شاء ضمنه قيمته معمولاً وله الأجر لأن العمل صار مسلماً إليه بتسليم بدله . ولو أتلف الأجير الثوب ويتخير صاحب الثوب في التضمين كما تقدم. وفي المضمرات : فإن ليس له حق الحبس فهلكت ضمنها ضمان الغاصب والمؤاجر يخير إن شاء العين من ضمنه قيمتها معمولاً وأعطاه الأجير أجرته، وإن شاء ضمنه قيمته غير معمول ولا يغطي الأجير اهـ. وفي فتاوى أبي الليث : نساج نسيج ثوباً جاء ليأخذ الأجرة فقال له صاحب الثوب اذهب به إلى منزلك فإذا فرغنا من الجمعة دفعت لك الأجرة فاختلس الثوب من يد النساج في المزاحمة قال : إن كان الحائك دفع الثوب لربه فدفعه للحائك على وجه الرهن وهلك الثوب هلك بالأجرة، وإن دفعه إليه على وجه الوديعة فهلك هلك على الأمانة والأجر على حاله لأنه سلم العمل إلى صاحبه فيقرر عليه الأجر. وفي المنتقى : حائك عمل ثوباً لآخر فتعلق الأمر فيه ليأخذه فأبى الحائك أن يدفعه حتى يأخذ الأجرة فتخرق من يد صاحبه لا حبس
He (the author) said: And if he detains and it is lost, there is no liability on him and no wage. As for no liability, because the object is a trust (amanah) in his hand, and he has the right to detain it legally, so he is not a wrongdoer, thus no liability is due upon him. No wage is due because the subject matter of the contract perished before delivery, which necessitates dropping of the consideration, as in sale. This is the statement of Imam Abu Hanifa. According to them (the two disciples), he is liable for the object because it was guaranteed (mamdumah) upon him before detention, and detention does not remove that. The owner has the choice: if he wishes, he may hold him liable for its value unworked, and no wage for him because the work was not delivered; if he wishes, he may hold him liable for its value worked, and give him the wage because the work became delivered by delivering its substitute. If the hiree destroys the garment, the owner has choice in holding liable as above. In al-Mudmarat: If he has no right to detain and it perishes, he is liable like a usurper, and the owner (hirer) has the choice: if he wishes, he may hold him liable for its value worked and give the wage; if he wishes, hold him liable for its value unworked and not give the wage. End. In Fatawa Abi al-Layth: A weaver wove a cloth, came to take his wage. The owner said: go to your house, when we are done with Friday I will pay you. The cloth was snatched from the weaver's hand in the crowd. He said: if the weaver had given the cloth to its owner and the owner gave it back to the weaver as a pledge (rahn), and it perished, it perishes with the wage (i.e., the wage is lost). If he gave it to him as a deposit (wadi'ah), it perishes as a trust, and the wage remains, because he delivered the work to its owner, so the wage is established. In al-Muntaqa: A weaver wove a cloth for someone, then the matter became complicated for him to take it. The weaver refused to hand it over until he took his wage. It tore in the hand of its owner. No detention?
Source pages p. 13

Commentary
This passage is a ruling on the consequences when an artisan who has the right to retain the object does so, and the object is lost. The matn states: if he detains and it is lost, he is not liable and foregoes his wage. The commentator explains the reasoning: the object is a trust in his hand because he is holding it with the right of detention, so he is not a trespasser. Thus no liability. And since the work perished before delivery to the owner, the wage is forfeited, analogous to a seller losing the item before delivery. This is the position of Imam Abu Hanifa. The Sahibayn disagree: they argue that the artisan already had liability (daman) before detention because he was holding the object for work, and detention does not remove that pre-existing liability. So they hold the artisan liable, but with an option for the owner: if he wants, he can claim the value of the unworked object (no wage) or the value of the worked object (with wage). The text then discusses the scenario if the artisan destroys the object himself (atlf), which follows the same rule. Then it cites other sources: al-Mudmarat states that if the artisan had no right to detain and the object is lost, he is liable as a usurper (ghasib), and the owner has similar choice. Then from Fatawa Abi al-Layth, a case of a weaver: if the owner gave the cloth back to the weaver as a pledge for the wage, loss of the cloth means loss of wage; if as a deposit, the wage remains because delivery was completed. Finally, al-Muntaqa: a weaver refused to hand over cloth until paid, and it tore in the owner's hand; the ruling is not fully given (cut off).

Key Terms
الأمانة (al-amānah): A trust; the object in the artisan's hand is considered a trust when he has the right to detain
المضمومة (al-mamdūmah): Guaranteed; the object is considered under guarantee before detention according to the Sahibayn
تسليم البدل (taslīm al-badal): Delivery of the substitute; if the owner chooses to claim the value of the worked object, that delivery of the substitute is considered delivery of the work

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), if a hired artisan detains an object rightfully and it is lost, what options does the owner have?
A) The owner may demand the artisan pay the full worked value and also receive the wage.
B) The owner may claim the unworked value (no wage) or the worked value (with wage).
C) The owner must accept the loss and cannot claim anything.
D) The owner may only claim the unworked value and forfeit the wage.

Key Takeaway
When an artisan rightfully detains an object and it is lost, Imam Abu Hanifa holds no liability and no wage; the Sahibayn give the owner an option to claim worked value with wage or unworked without.

Intra-Hanafi Dispute on Liability and Wage When Detained Object Perishes
Ruling on liability and wage when detained object perishes

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi positions (Abu Hanifa vs. Sahibayn) regarding liability and wage when a worker lawfully detains an object and it perishes, and explain the thamarah al-khilaf.

Core Idea
When lawful detention leads to loss, Abu Hanifa sees no liability and no wage; the Sahibayn see liability with owner's choice.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq presents a classic intra-Hanafi dispute. The matn states that if a worker detains an object rightfully (e.g., for unpaid wages) and it perishes, he is not liable and loses his wage. Abu Hanifa bases this on the object being a trust. However, the two Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) argue that the object was already a liability before detention, so the worker remains liable and the owner has a choice. Understanding this dispute clarifies the Hanafi approach to risk and compensation in hire contracts.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi (Abu Hanifa) position
Identify that Abu Hanifa holds: no liability (ḍamān) on the worker and no wage (ajr) for him. The object is an amānah (trust) in his hand, and lawful detention does not make him a transgressor.
The matn presents this as the default ruling.
2
Identify the Sahibayn's position
Abu Yusuf and Muhammad hold that the worker is liable for the object because it was already maḍmūnah (liable) before detention. The owner has a choice: claim value unworked (no wage) or value worked (with wage).
Their reasoning: the object was under liability due to non-delivery; detention does not remove that.
3
Analyze the proofs
Abu Hanifa uses qiyas (analogy) to sale: as in sale, if goods perish before delivery, the price drops; similarly here, the wage drops. The Sahibayn consider the worker's prior possession as liable, so detention does not change the nature.
Qiyas jaliy (clear analogy) vs. focus on the nature of possession.
4
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
Practical difference: According to Abu Hanifa, the owner bears loss and the worker gets no wage. According to Sahibayn, the owner can recoup value from the worker, with or without wage.
This affects the distribution of risk in ijara contracts.
5
Consider the mufta bihi and unlawful detention
The matn gives Abu Hanifa's view as primary. Later fatwas sometimes follow Sahibayn when the worker's possession was originally liable. The passage also notes that if the worker had no right to detain (unlawful detention), he is liable as a usurper.
The distinction between lawful and unlawful detention is crucial.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال رحمه الله : (وإن حبس فضاع فلا ضمان عليه ولا أجر) أما عدم الضمان فلان العين أمانة في يده وله حبس العين شرعاً فلم يكن به متعدياً فلا يجب عليه الضمان ولا يجب الأجر لأن المعقود عليه هلك قبل التسليم وهو يوجب سقوط البدل كما في البيع وهو قول الإمام أحمد وعندهما يضمن العين لأنها كانت مضمومة عليه قبل الحبس فلا يسقط ذلك بالحبس، وصاحب العين بالخيار إن شاء ضمنه قيمته غير معمول ولا أجر له لأن العمل لم يسلم إليه، وإن شاء ضمنه قيمته معمولاً وله الأجر لأن العمل صار مسلماً إليه بتسليم بدله . ولو أتلف الأجير الثوب ويتخير صاحب الثوب في التضمين كما تقدم. وفي المضمرات : فإن ليس له حق الحبس فهلكت ضمنها ضمان الغاصب والمؤاجر يخير إن شاء العين من ضمنه قيمتها معمولاً وأعطاه الأجير أجرته، وإن شاء ضمنه قيمته غير معمول ولا يغطي الأجير اهـ.
He (the author) said, may Allah have mercy on him: (And if he detains and it perishes, then there is no liability on him and no wage). As for no liability, because the object is a trust in his hand and he is legally allowed to detain it, so he is not transgressing, therefore liability does not become obligatory. And the wage is not obligatory because the contracted thing perished before delivery, and that necessitates the dropping of the consideration as in sale. And this is the saying of Imam Ahmad (i.e., Abu Hanifa). And according to the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), he is liable for the object because it was already liable to him before detention, so that does not drop by detention. And the owner of the object has a choice: if he wishes, he may hold him liable for its value unworked, and no wage for him because the work was not delivered to him; and if he wishes, he may hold him liable for its value worked, and he has the wage because the work became delivered to him by the delivery of its compensation. And if the worker destroys the garment, the owner of the garment has a choice in holding liable as previously. And in al-Mudmarat: If he does not have the right of detention and it perishes, he is liable with the liability of a usurper, and the hirer (owner) has a choice: if he wishes, he may hold him liable for its value worked and give the worker his wage; and if he wishes, he may hold him liable for its value unworked and not give the worker (wage). End.
Source pages p. 13

Commentary
This passage presents a ruling from the matn and a key intra-Hanafi dispute. The matn states that if a worker detains the object rightfully (i.e., he has the right of detention) and the object perishes while in his possession, he is not liable for its loss and is not entitled to any wage. The commentator explains the reasoning: the object is an amānah (trust) in his hand, and since he is legally allowed to detain it, he is not a transgressor, so no liability. The reason for no wage is that the contracted work perished before delivery to the owner, which drops the obligation of payment, analogous to a sale where the goods perish before delivery. This is the position of Abu Hanifa (referred to as 'Imam Ahmad'). However, the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) hold that the worker is liable for the object because it was already in his possession as a liability (maḍmūnah) before he detained it—since he had not yet delivered it, it was already under his liability—and detaining does not remove that liability. According to them, the owner has a choice: either to claim the value of the object unworked (no wage) or to claim the value worked (including the wage for the worker). The commentator then notes that if the worker himself destroys the object, the owner has the same options. The passage from al-Mudmarat adds: if the worker had no right to detain (i.e., his detention was unlawful), then if it perishes, he is liable as a usurper (ḍamān al-ghāṣib), and the owner again has a choice between the two options mentioned.

Key Terms
ضمان (ḍamān): Liability to compensate for loss or damage of the object.
أمانة (amānah): A trust; possession without liability for loss unless due to negligence or transgression.
مضمومة (maḍmūnah): Something that is under liability; the object is considered liable to the worker because he must deliver it.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Sahibayn in this passage, if a washerman lawfully detains a cloth and it perishes, what options does the owner have?
A) The owner must accept the loss and pay no wage.
B) The owner can choose to claim the value of the cloth unworked (no wage) or value worked (with wage).
C) The owner can only claim the value of the cloth worked and must pay the wage.
D) The owner can force the washerman to replace the cloth.

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, when a worker lawfully detains an object for unpaid wages and it perishes, the default ruling (Abu Hanifa) is no liability and no wage; the Sahibayn differ, giving the owner a choice.

When a Hired Worker May Substitute Another
Ruling on substitution of worker when contract specifies personal service

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on substitution of a hired worker and distinguish between a contract stipulating personal service and an absolute contract.

Core Idea
A hired worker may not substitute another if personal service is stipulated; if absolute, substitution is permitted.

This lesson presents a concise rule from Kanz al-Daqaiq regarding the hired worker's ability to delegate the work. The key distinction lies in whether the contract specifies that the work must be done personally or leaves it open. Understanding this nuance is essential for correctly applying the law of hire (ijara) in practice.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two scenarios
Read the matn carefully: the first ruling covers the case where the worker's personal performance is stipulated; the second covers an absolute contract with no such stipulation.
The Arabic keywords are 'شرط' (stipulated) and 'أطلق' (left absolute).
2
State the ruling for each scenario
When stipulated, the worker cannot use another; when absolute, he may hire another to do the work.
The ruling is a direct consequence of what was contracted: specific personal effort vs. a generic obligation in the worker's liability (dhimmah).
3
Understand the rationale
If the work is from a specific person, another cannot substitute; if the obligation is absolute in the dhimmah, fulfillment can be through another, just like repaying a debt.
The analogy of debt repayment illustrates that the obligation is not tied to a particular individual unless stipulated.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال رحمه الله : (ولا يستعمل غيره إن شرط عمله بنفسه) يعني ليس للأجير أن يستعمل غيره إذا شرط عليه أن يعمل بنفسه لأن المعقود عليه العمل من محل معين فلا يقوم غيره مقامه كما إذا كان المعقود عليه المنفعة كما إذا استأجر رجلاً للخدمة شهراً لا يقوم غيره في الخدمة ولا يستحق به الأجر . قال رحمه الله : ( وإن أطلق له أن يستأجر غيره لأن الواجب عليه عمل مطلق في ذمته ويمكن الإيفاء بنفسه وبغيره كالمأمور بقضاء الدين .
He (the author) said, may Allah have mercy on him: (And he does not use another if the work is stipulated for himself) meaning it is not permissible for the hired worker to use another if it is stipulated that he himself should work, because the contracted thing is the work from a specific person, so another cannot take his place, as if the contracted thing is the benefit, such as if he hired a man for service for a month, another cannot take his place in the service, and he does not deserve the wage by it. He (the author) said, may Allah have mercy on him: (And if it is left absolute, he may hire another because what is obligatory upon him is an absolute work in his liability, and it is possible to fulfill it himself or by another, like the one ordered to repay a debt.)
Source pages p. 14

Commentary
This passage consists of two related rulings from the matn. The first ruling: if a worker is hired specifically to perform the work himself (i.e., the contract stipulates that he must personally do the work), he is not allowed to hire another person to do it instead. The reason is that the contracted subject matter is the work from that specific individual—his personal skill or effort was the basis of the contract. Therefore, no substitute can stand in for him. The commentator draws an analogy: if someone hires a man for service for a month, another cannot take his place and the hired man cannot claim the wage if someone else does the work. The second ruling: if the contract is left absolute (i.e., it is not specified that the worker must do it himself), then he is allowed to hire another to perform the work. This is because the obligation is a work that is absolute in his liability (dhimmah), and he can fulfill it either personally or through another, just like a person who is ordered to repay a debt can repay it himself or have someone else repay it on his behalf.

Key Terms
شرط (sharṭ): A stipulation in the contract that the work must be done by the worker himself.
أطلق (aṭlaqa): Leaving the contract absolute, i.e., no stipulation that the worker must do it personally.
ذمة (dhimmah): Liability; the obligation resides in the worker's dhimmah, allowing substitution when absolute.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
A man hires a driver to transport goods for a month. The contract does not mention who drives. Can the driver send another person to drive instead?
A) Yes, because the contract is absolute.
B) No, because driving requires personal skill.
C) Yes, but only if the substitute is licensed.
D) No, because the hirer expects the named driver.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, whether a hired worker may delegate depends entirely on whether the contract stipulates personal service or leaves the obligation absolute.

Proportional Wage for Partial Performance in Hire
Ruling on proportional wage with intra-Hanafi condition

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the rule of proportional wage when some contracted subjects are lost during hire and identify the condition of known subjects that alters the ruling.

Core Idea
Partial performance in a divisible hire earns proportional wage, but only if the subjects were specified.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq addresses a common scenario in hire contracts: the worker is hired to bring a group of people, but some die en route. The author gives the ruling that the worker deserves a proportional wage for those delivered. The commentator then relates a condition from al-Hindwani that this applies only if the family members were known. Understanding this nuance is key to applying the Hanafi rules on partial performance.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the ruling
The act is hiring a worker to bring family members. The ruling: if some die, the worker gets proportional wage for those delivered.
The ruling is stated directly in the matn.
2
Understand the reasoning
The reason given: he fulfilled part of the contracted subject matter, so he deserves wage proportionally. This is based on the divisible nature of the contract.
The wage is apportioned according to the number of persons delivered.
3
Note the condition added by al-Hindwani
Al-Hindwani conditions that the family members must be known (specified) for proportional wage to apply. If unknown, the full wage is due or the contract is void.
This is an intra-Hanafi difference; the matn's position is the relied-upone when known.
4
Connect to other examples on partial performance
The passage includes an additional example from al-Nihaya about carrying wheat, showing how wording affects obligation. This reinforces the principle of proportional wage based on actual work completed.
The text cuts off but the principle is clear.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال رحمه الله : (وإن استأجره ليجيء بعياله فمات بعضهم فجاء بمن بقي فله الأجر بحسابه لأنه أوفى ببعض المعقود عليه فيستحق الأجر بحسابه. قال الفقيه أو جعفر الهندواني : هذا إذا كانوا معلومين حتى يكون الأجر مقابلاً لجملتهم، وإن كانوا غير معلومين يجب الأجر اهـ. وفي الخلاصة : وإذا كانوا غير معلومين فالإجارة فاسدة وفي النهاية نقلاً عن الفضلي : إذا استأجره في المصر ليحمل له الحنطة من القرية فذهب فلم يجد الحنطة فعاد؛ إن كان قال استأجرت منك من المصر حتى أحمل الحنطة . من القرية يجب نصف الأجر بالذهاب، وإن قال استأجرت منك حتى أحمل الحنطة . من القرية لا يجب شيء لأن الإجارة على الحمل لا غير وفي
He (the author) said, may Allah have mercy on him: (And if he hires him to bring his family, and some of them die, and he brings those who remain, then he has the wage proportionally) because he has fulfilled part of the contracted subject matter, so he deserves the wage proportionally. Al-Faqih Abu Ja'far al-Hindwani said: This is if they were known, so that the wage is in consideration of the total; and if they were unknown, then the full wage is obligatory. End. And in al-Khulasa: If they were unknown, the hire is void. And in al-Nihaya, quoting al-Fadli: If he hires him in the city to carry wheat for him from the village, and he goes and does not find the wheat and returns; if he said 'I hired you from the city until I carry the wheat from the village,' then half the wage is due for the going; and if he said 'I hired you to carry the wheat from the village,' then nothing is due because the hire is for the carriage only, and...
Source pages p. 14

Commentary
This passage gives a ruling on a specific scenario: a person hires a worker to bring his family (wives, children) from one place to another. If some family members die during the journey, and the worker brings the remaining ones, he is entitled to a proportional wage based on the number he delivered. The reason is that he fulfilled part of the contracted obligation. The commentator then relates a condition from al-Hindwani: this rule applies only if the family members were known (specified) so that the wage was calculated for the total; if they were unknown, the full wage is due because the contract cannot be apportioned. Al-Khulasa adds that if they are unknown, the hire is void (fasid). The passage then transitions to a different example from al-Nihaya about hiring to carry wheat, illustrating how the wording affects the obligation: if the hire is from the city to the village and back, half the wage is due if the wheat is not found; if the hire is only for carriage (without the return trip), nothing is due because the work was not completed. The text cuts off, but the principle is clear.

Key Terms
عيال (ʿiyāl): Dependents, family members whom one is obliged to support; in this context, they are the subject of transport.
بحسابه (bi-ḥisābihī): Proportionally; the wage is calculated according to the portion of the work completed.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
A man hires a worker to bring his four children. One child dies en route, but the worker brings the other three. How much wage is the worker entitled to according to the matn?
A) The full wage because he made the effort.
B) Three-fourths of the wage proportional to the children delivered.
C) Nothing because the contract was not fully performed.
D) Half the wage because one child died.

Key Takeaway
In a divisible hire contract, if some subjects are lost, the worker earns proportional wage for what he delivered, provided the subjects were specified.
