Ruling on the Hirer's Right to Detain for Wages and Substitution
States the basic ruling of the hirer's right to detain for wages and conditions for substitution

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the hirer's right to detain property for wages and identify the condition that prohibits substitution.

Core Idea
A worker may detain what he produced until paid, but cannot hire a substitute if personal service was stipulated.

This lesson examines the opening of the Book of Ijarah in Kanz al-Daqa'iq. The matn establishes a fundamental right for the hired party to withhold the subject matter of the contract until the wage is paid. It also specifies when substitution is permissible. The commentary then expands with numerous subsidiary cases from later Hanafi works, illustrating the practical application of this principle across different scenarios.

Guided Path
1
Identify the main rule
Read the first part of the matn: 'يحبس للأجر'. This states that the hirer (ajir) has the right to detain the property (the subject matter of the contract) for his wage
This is a right, not an obligation; the hirer may choose to release the property.
2
Recognize the exception on substitution
The phrase 'ولا يستعمل غيره إن شرط عمله بنفسه' indicates that if the contract stipulated the hirer's personal work, he cannot employ a substitute
3
Understand the condition of absolute contract
The phrase 'وإن أطلق له أن يستأجر غيره' means that if the contract was absolute (no stipulation of personal work), he may hire another to perform the work
This is the default ruling: substitution is permitted when not explicitly prohibited.
4
Analyze the proportional wage case
The matn gives a case: if hired to bring family and some die, the hirer gets wage proportionally for those he brings
This illustrates how the right to wage is tied to performance, and the detention right attaches to the completed part.
5
Trace the commentary's furu'
The commentary cites cases from al-Khaniya, al-Hawi, etc., showing how the right of detention applies to weavers, brokers, etc., and when liability for loss arises
These subsidiary rulings demonstrate the scope and limits of the detention right.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الإجارة يحبس للأجر ولا يستعمل غيره إن شرط عمله بنفسه وإن أطلق له أن يستأجر غيره وإن استأجره ليجيء بعياله فمات بعضهم فجاء بمن بقي فله الأجر بحسابه ولا أجر الحامل ضمان على الحائك، وإن تخرق من يدهما فعلى الحائك نصف ضمان الخرق اهـ. وفي الخانية : لو جاء الحائك بالثوب إلى صاحبه فقال له رب الثوب أمسك حتى أفرغ من العمل وأعطيك الأجر فسرق منه لا يضمن اهـ. وفي الخانية : السمسار إذا باع شيئاً من الثياب بأمر ربها وأمسك الثمن حتى ينقد الأجرة فسرق منه الثمن لا يضمن .اهـ. وفي الحاوي : رجل أقرض آخر دراهم فاستأجر منه داره مدة معلومة بأجرة معلومة وجعل الأجر ببعض الدين قصاصاً ومضت مدة الإجارة هل للمقرض أن يحبس العين بعد انقضاء المدة؟ قال : ليس له المنع وفي السغناقي : لو تزوج امرأة على سكنى دار سنة فسلم الدار إليها ليس لها أن تحبس نفسها عنه اهـ. وفي الولوالجية : إذا أجر داره سنة وعجل الأجرة ولم يسلم إلى المستأجر حتى مات الآجر وانفسخ العقد لا يكون للمستأجر ولاية الحبس في الأجرة المعجلة، ولو كانت الإجارة فاسدة وفسخا العقد بسبب الفساد ليس للمستأجر أن يحبس العين بالدين السابق. وفي الخلاصة : وفي الإجارة الفاسدة للمستأجر حق الحبس لاستيفاء الأجرة المعجلة
Book of Ijarah: He detains for the wage and does not use another if his personal work was stipulated, and if it was absolute he may hire another. And if he hired him to come with his family and some died, and he came with those remaining, he gets the wage proportionally. And no wage for the carrier of the book for the reply nor for the carrier of food if he returns it due to death. Guarantee is upon the weaver, and if it tears from both their hands, then upon the weaver is half the guarantee of the tear. And in al-Khaniya: if the weaver brought the garment to its owner and the owner said: hold it until I finish work and give you your wage, and it was stolen, he does not guarantee. And in al-Khaniya: the broker if he sold something of garments by order of its owner and held the price until he pays the wage, and the price was stolen, he does not guarantee. And in al-Hawi: a man lent another dirhams, then hired his house for a known period with a known wage and made the wage a set-off against part of the debt, and the rental period passed: does the lender have the right to detain the property after the period? He said: he does not have the right to prevent. And in al-Sighnaqi: if he married a woman on the condition of dwelling in a house for a year and he surrendered the house to her, she does not have the right to detain herself from him. And in al-Walwalijiyya: if he rented his house for a year and paid the wage in advance and did not surrender to the tenant until the landlord died and the contract was rescinded, the tenant does not have authority of detention over the advanced wage. And if the hire was invalid and they rescinded due to invalidity, the tenant does not have the right to detain the property for the prior debt. And in al-Khulasa: in invalid hire, the tenant has the right of detention to recover the advanced wage.
Source pages p. 14

Commentary
This passage opens the Book of Ijarah with the matn of Kanz al-Daqa'iq, stating that the hired party (ajir) has the right to detain the property for his wage. However, if the contract stipulated his personal work, he cannot employ a substitute. If the contract was absolute, he may hire another. The matn also covers the case of hiring to bring family and proportion of wage, and the carrier of a book or food. The commentary then cites various subsidiary rulings from Hanafi works: the weaver who holds the garment by the owner's request is not liable for theft; a broker holding the price is not liable; a lender cannot detain the house after the rental period; a wife married on condition of dwelling cannot detain herself; etc. These illustrate the Hanafi position on the right of detention (habs) for wages in different contexts.

Key Terms
الإجارة (al-ijarah): A contract of hire or lease for a known benefit in exchange for known compensation.
الحبس (al-habs): The right to detain the property or wage as security for payment.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the matn, what is the ruling regarding the hirer's use of a substitute if the contract stipulated his personal work?
A) He may use a substitute.
B) He may not use a substitute.
C) He must use a substitute.
D) The contract becomes void.

Key Takeaway
The hired party may detain the property for unpaid wages, but cannot delegate the work if personal service was stipulated.

Workers Without Tangible Effect: Porter and Sailor
States that workers whose labor leaves no trace cannot detain for wage.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that porters and sailors cannot detain for wages, and explain the underlying reasoning based on the work being an 'arad (perishable accident).

Core Idea
The porter cannot detain the wage because his work is an accident that perishes—no object to hold.

In Hanafi law, the right to detain the wage depends on whether the hired work leaves a tangible effect. This lesson examines the ruling for porters and sailors, whose labor produces no lasting trace. We will explore the reasoning from the matn and its commentary, and see how this principle applies in practice.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and its subject
State clearly that the porter and sailor do not have the right to detain (habs) the wage. Note that 'detain' here means withholding the goods or vessel as security for payment.
The ruling applies to all workers whose work leaves no trace, e.g., porters, sailors, couriers.
2
Understand the 'illah (effective cause)
The reason given is that the contracted object is the work itself, which is an 'arad (accident) that perishes and cannot be physically held. Since there is no durable object to detain, the right to detain is absent.
This is a qiyas (analogical reasoning) - comparing with workers who produce a tangible object.
3
Contrast with workers who leave a trace
Workers like fullers or washers may have a right to detain because their work leaves a physical effect. The matn mentions a difference of opinion on washing garments, indicating that the ruling is limited to pure service work.
The ikhtilaf on washing shows the nuanced application of the 'illah.
4
Apply to a fatwa scenario
Consider the case of a hired camel driver. If the owner tells him to hold the goods and they perish, the driver is not liable. This reinforces that the driver has no right to detain, and also no guarantee (daman) when acting on instructions.
The fatwa from al-Fatawa illustrates the practical implications.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال رحمه الله : (ومن لا أثر لعمله كالحمال والملاح لا يحبس للأجر) يعني ليس له أن يحبس للأجر لأن المعقود عليه نفس العمل وهو عرض يفنى ولا يتصور بقاؤه، واختلفوا في غسل الثوب حسب اختلافهم في القصار بلا نشاء كما تقدم، وفي شرح القدوري قال أبو يوسف في الحمال إذا طلب الأجرة ما بلغ المنزل قبل أن يضعه ليس له ذلك اهـ. وفي الفتاوى : استأجر جمالاً ليحمل له إلى بلدة كذا بكذا فحمله فقال له صاحب الجمل امسكه عندك فهلك فلا ضمان عليه بلا خلاف .
He said, may Allah have mercy on him: (And those whose work has no effect, like the porter and the sailor, do not detain for the wage) meaning he does not have the right to detain for the wage because the contracted object is the work itself, which is an accident that perishes and cannot be conceived to remain. And they differed regarding washing a garment according to their difference regarding the fuller without starch as previously. And in Sharh al-Quduri, Abu Yusuf said: concerning the porter, if he requests the wage before reaching the house and before putting it down, he does not have that right. And in al-Fatawa: he hired a camel driver to carry for him to such and such town for such and such, and he carried it, then the camel owner said: hold it with you, and it perished, then there is no guarantee on him without disagreement.
Source pages p. 14

Commentary
This matn ruling distinguishes between workers whose labor produces a tangible effect (like laundering) and those whose work is purely service (like carrying). The latter, such as a porter or sailor, cannot detain the wage because their work is not a durable object that can be held. The commentary elaborates that the contracted work is an 'arad (accident) that perishes, so there is no physical thing to detain. It then cites a difference of opinion regarding washing garments, and quotes Abu Yusuf on the porter not being entitled to wage before delivery. A fatwa is also mentioned: if the owner asks the carrier to hold the goods and they perish, the carrier is not liable.

Key Terms
الأجير (al-ajir): The hired worker; here distinguished based on whether work leaves a trace.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why does the porter not have the right to detain the wage according to the matn?
A) Because his work is not complete.
B) Because his work is an accident that perishes and cannot be held.
C) Because he is not trustworthy.
D) Because the wage is not specified.

Key Takeaway
Workers whose labor leaves no tangible effect, like porters and sailors, cannot detain the wage because their work is a perishable accident, not a durable object.

Ruling on Substitution When Personal Work Is Stipulated
Clarifies that the hirer cannot use a substitute if personal work was stipulated

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling when a hired worker is stipulated to work personally and explain the legal consequence of using a substitute.

Core Idea
If personal work is stipulated, the hired worker cannot substitute another and forfeits the wage if he does.

This lesson examines a specific clause in the contract of hire (ijara): the condition that the hired person must perform the work himself. The matn explicitly forbids delegation under such a condition, and the commentary provides a rational analogy (qiyas) to hiring for usufruct. Understanding this ruling clarifies the limits of substitution in service contracts.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and condition
Read the matn: 'ولا يستعمل غيره إن شرط عمله بنفسه'. Identify both the ruling (no substitution) and the condition (personal work stipulated).
The condition triggers the prohibition.
2
Locate the reasoning
The commentary states 'لأن المعقود عليه العمل من محل معين'. Understand that the object of the contract is the work from a specific person.
This is the core legal principle.
3
Analyse the qiyas
The text draws an analogy to hiring for usufruct (e.g., renting a property). Just as another property cannot substitute, another person cannot substitute when the contracted work is from a specific individual.
The illa is the specificity of the person.
4
Determine the consequence
If the hired worker uses a substitute despite the stipulation, he is not entitled to the wage ('لا يستحق به الأجر').
The wage is forfeited, but the contract may still be valid.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال رحمه الله : (ولا يستعمل غيره إن شرط عمله بنفسه يعني ليس للأجير أن يستعمل غيره إذا شرط عليه أن يعمل بنفسه لأن المعقود عليه العمل من محل معين فلا يقوم غيره مقامه كما إذا كان المعقود عليه المنفعة كما إذا استأجر رجلاً للخدمة شهراً لا يقوم غيره في الخدمة ولا يستحق به الأجر .
He said, may Allah have mercy on him: (And he does not use another if his personal work was stipulated) meaning it is not for the hired worker to use another if it was stipulated on him that he work himself, because the contracted object is the work from a specific person, so another does not stand in his place, just as if the contracted object is the usufruct, as if he hired a man for service for a month, another does not stand in his service and he does not deserve the wage through him.
Source pages p. 14

Commentary
This matn ruling explicitly states that when the contract specifies that the hired person must perform the work himself, he cannot employ a substitute. The reasoning, provided in the commentary, is that the contract is based on the work coming from that specific individual. A qiyas (analogy) is drawn with hiring for usufruct (like renting a property): just as the usufruct of a specific property cannot be fulfilled by another property, the work of a specific person cannot be replaced. If he uses a substitute despite the stipulation, he does not earn the wage.

Key Terms
المعقود عليه (al-ma'qud 'alayh): The object of the contract; here it is the work or usufruct.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If someone hires a tailor to sew a shirt with the condition that the tailor sews it himself, what happens if the tailor gives it to another to sew?
A) The tailor is still entitled to the wage.
B) The tailor is not entitled to the wage.
C) The contract becomes void.
D) The tailor must pay the substitute.

Key Takeaway
When a contract stipulates personal work, the hired worker cannot substitute another, and doing so forfeits his entitlement to the wage.

Ruling on Substitution When No Stipulation Is Made
Ruling on delegation in absolute ijara via qiyas to debt repayment.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rule for delegation in ijara when personal work is not stipulated, and apply the qiyas to the debt repayment analogy.

Core Idea
If no personal work is stipulated, the hirer may delegate; the obligation is abstract in the dhimma.

This short matn completes the previous discussion on conditions in ijara. It addresses a key scenario: when the contract does not require the hirer to perform the work himself, may he hire another to do it? The passage states yes, because the obligation is an absolute liability, comparable to a debt.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Ruling
The matn states that if the contract is absolute (no personal condition), the hirer has the right to hire another. The ruling is mubah (permissible).
2
Analyze the Dalil
The proof is a qiyas jaliy: analogy with a person ordered to repay a debt. In both, the obligation is in the dhimma and can be discharged by self or agent.
The analogy is explicit in the text: 'like the one ordered to repay a debt.'
3
Extract the Illa
The effective cause is that the obligation is an absolute liability (dhimma) not a personal service. This is a jaliy illa extracted via tanqih al-manat.
4
Confirm Applicability
This ruling applies only when no personal stipulation exists; if personal work is stipulated, delegation is not allowed.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال رحمه الله : ( وإن أطلق له أن يستأجر غيره لأن الواجب عليه عمل مطلق في ذمته ويمكن الإيفاء بنفسه وبغيره كالمأمور بقضاء الدين . مقامه
He said, may Allah have mercy on him: (And if it was absolute, he has the right to hire another) because the obligation upon him is an absolute work in his liability, and it is possible to fulfill it by himself or by another, like the one ordered to repay a debt.
Source pages p. 14

Commentary
This matn complements the previous one: when the contract does not specify that the work must be done personally, the hirer may delegate to another. The reasoning is that the obligation is a work that is absolute (malaq) in his liability (dhimma), and can be discharged either by himself or by a substitute. An analogy is made with the case of a person ordered to repay a debt: he can pay it himself or appoint someone else to pay.

Key Terms
الواجب (al-wajib): The obligatory work; here it is a duty that can be delegated if not personal.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
When the contract is absolute (no personal work condition), may the hirer use a substitute?
A) Yes, because the obligation is in his liability and can be fulfilled by another.
B) No, because the work must be done by him.
C) Only if the employer agrees.
D) No, because it is a personal service.

Key Takeaway
In absolute ijara contracts, delegation is permissible because the obligation is an abstract liability, like a debt.

Prorated Wage for Partial Performance in Hire Contracts
Gives prorated wage if hired to bring family and some die en route

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on prorated wage when some hired family members die, and explain the condition that the family must be known for the prorated wage to apply.

Core Idea
Partial performance of a hire contract entitles the worker to a prorated wage — not a full forfeit.

In this passage from al-Kanz al-Daqaiq, the author rules on a specific hire (ijara) case: a man is hired to bring his family, but some die on the journey. Does he still get the wage? The Hanafi position is that he receives a proportional share. The commentary expands on the condition that the family members must be known for the wage to be allocated per person, and also draws analogies with grain carriage. Understanding this ruling clarifies the Hanafi principle that partial fulfillment yields partial compensation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Core Ruling
Find the principal hukm: when some family die, the worker gets 'al-ajr bi-hisabih' (wage proportionally). This is the starting point.
The ruling is explicit in the matn.
2
Understand the Reasoning (Ta'lil)
The reason given is 'because he fulfilled part of the contracted object'. This ta'lil justifies the prorated wage. Recognize that partial performance does not nullify the entire entitlement.
The argument is based on the principle of proportionality (qiyas on divisible contracts).
3
Note the Condition of Known Family
Al-Hindawani specifies that this ruling applies only if the family members are known (ma'lum). If they are unknown, the full wage is due or the contract is invalid. Understand why: the wage is allocated per person only when the individuals are specified.
This condition prevents ambiguity in the contract object.
4
Explore the Analogies
The commentary brings analogous cases: hiring to carry grain from a village, or from underground storage. In each, if the object is missing after partial effort, a half or prorated wage is given. See how the principle extends.
These examples reinforce the same ta'lil.
5
Recognize the Intra-Hanafi Ikhtilaf
Hisham narrates from Muhammad that in the ship case, no wage is due. This shows a difference of opinion within the school. The matn adopts the prorated view, which is the mufta bihi.
Knowing the ikhtilaf helps understand the scope of the ruling.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال رحمه الله : (وإن استأجره ليجيء بعياله فمات بعضهم فجاء بمن بقي فله الأجر بحسابه لأنه أوفى ببعض المعقود عليه فيستحق الأجر بحسابه. قال الفقيه أو جعفر الهندواني : هذا إذا كانوا معلومين حتى يكون الأجر مقابلاً لجملتهم، وإن كانوا غير معلومين يجب الأجر اهـ. وفي الخلاصة : وإذا كانوا غير معلومين فالإجارة فاسدة وفي النهاية نقلاً عن الفضلي : إذا استأجره في المصر ليحمل له الحنطة من القرية فذهب فلم يجد الحنطة فعاد؛ إن كان قال استأجرت منك من المصر حتى أحمل الحنطة . من القرية يجب نصف الأجر بالذهاب، وإن قال استأجرت منك حتى أحمل الحنطة . من القرية لا يجب شيء لأن الإجارة على الحمل لا غير وفي في الكتاب للجواب ولا لحامل الطعام إن رده للموت . يجد فلاناً . في الأول على الذهاب والحمل وعزاه إلى الذخيرة. وروى هشام عن محمد لا أجر ومثله في السفينة .اهـ. كلام الشارح وفي التتارخانية من باب ما يستحق الفارس : استأجره ليحمل له كذا كذا من المطمورة فذهب فلم يجد المطمورة استحق نصف الأجرة .اهـ. فظهر أنه لا فرق كما ذكره الشارح .
He said, may Allah have mercy on him: (And if he hired him to come with his family, and some of them died, and he came with those remaining, he gets the wage proportionally) because he fulfilled part of the contracted object, so he deserves wage proportionally. Al-Faqih Abu Ja'far al-Hindawani said: This is if they were known (specified) so that the wage corresponds to the whole; if they were unknown, the full wage is due. In al-Khulasa: if they are unknown, the hire is invalid. And in al-Nihaya quoting from al-Fadli: if he hired him in the city to carry grain from the village, and he went and did not find the grain and returned: if he said 'I hired you from the city to carry the grain from the village', half the wage is due for going; if he said 'I hired you to carry the grain from the village', nothing is due because the hire is for carrying only. And in the book: for the reply and not for the carrier of food if he returns it due to death. He finds so-and-so. In the first, it is for going and carrying, attributed to al-Dhakhira. And Hisham narrated from Muhammad: no wage, and similarly in the ship. The commentator's words. And in al-TatarKhaniyya from the section on what the rider deserves: he hired him to carry such-and-such from the underground storage, and he went and did not find the underground storage, he deserves half the wage. So it appears there is no difference as the commentator mentioned.
Source pages p. 14

Commentary
This matn addresses the situation where a person is hired to bring his family from one place to another, but some family members die en route. The ruling is that he receives wage proportional to the number actually brought. The commentary by al-Hindawani specifies that this applies if the family members were known (ma'lum) so the wage is allocated per person; if unknown, the full wage is due or the contract is invalid. Further illustrations are given about hiring to carry grain: if the contract is for carrying from a specific place and that place is not found, half wage may be due for the journey. Various narrations from Hisham, Muhammad, and others discuss similar cases. The upshot is that the wage is proportional to actual performance.

Key Terms
الأجر بحسابه (al-ajr bi-hisabih): Wage proportionally calculated based on the amount of work performed.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a man is hired to bring his family of 4 from city A to B, and one dies en route, how much wage does he receive?
A) Full wage because he tried.
B) Three-fourths of the wage.
C) Half the wage.
D) No wage because the contract is void.

Key Takeaway
Partial performance of a hire contract entitles the worker to a prorated wage, provided the subject matter is known and divisible.

Ijarah — Hire and Lease

Ruling on Carrier of Book or Food When Recipient Is Dead
Denies wage to carrier of message or food if recipient is dead and he returns

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on wage for a carrier when the recipient dies and evaluate the intra-Hanafi disagreement.

Core Idea
No wage for carrier if recipient dies because the contracted benefit was not realized.

This lesson examines a specific scenario in ijarah (hire) where a carrier is hired to transport goods or a message to a recipient. The focus is on what happens if the recipient dies before delivery. The passage presents the primary ruling and then discusses differing views within the Hanafi school, including the opinions of Zufar and Muhammad al-Shaybani.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What exactly is being ruled upon? The carrier who returns because the recipient died. The ruling is that he gets no wage (la ajr).
2
Locate the dalil
What proof does the author cite? Analogy with a tailor who undoes his work after finishing; similarly, the carrier nullifies the contracted benefit.
The analogy shows that undoing the completed work forfeits the wage.
3
Note the ikhtilaf
Within the Hanafi school, Zufar argues for wage in the food case (since transport was done) and Muhammad argues for wage for the journey in the book case (since part was fulfilled).
These are recorded but not the relied-upon view.
4
Analyze the Hanafi response
The majority Hanafi position responds that the wage is for the entire contracted object (including reply), and partial performance without result does not earn wage.
5
Apply the principle to analogous cases
The text extends the rule to tailors, sailors, and ship rentals to illustrate that wage is only due when the contracted benefit is fully realized or when the worker did his utmost beyond his control.
For example, if the carrier left the book to be delivered later, he gets wage for the journey.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال رحمه الله : (ولا أجر الحامل الكتاب للجواب ولا لحامل الطعام إن رده للموت) يعني إذا استأجره ليذهب بطعامه إلى فلان بمكة أو الذهب بكتابه إليه ويجيء بجوابه فذهب ووجد فلاناً ميتاً ورده فلا أجر له لأنه نقض المعقود عليه بالرد فصار كأنه لم يفعل فلا يستحق الأجر . وقال زفر له الأجر في الطعام لأن الأجرة بمقابلة حمل الطعام إلى مكة وقد وفي بالمشروط عليه فاستحقت الأجرة وقال محمد له الأجرة للذهاب في نقل الكتاب لأنه أوفى ببعض المعقود عليه . قلنا الأجرة مقابلة بالجواب والنقل ولم يوجد ولم يأت بالمعقود عليه فلا أجر له كما لو نقض الخياط الخياطة بعد الفراغ من العمل فلو وجده غائباً فهو كما لو وجده ميتاً لتعذر الوصول إليه، ولو ترك الكتاب هناك ليوصله إليه أو إلى ورثته فله الأجر في الذهاب لأنه أتى بأقصى ما في وسعه. قال في المحيط : ولو استأجر رسولاً ليبلغ رسالته إلى فلان ببغداد فلم وعاد فله الأجر لأن الأجر بقطع المسافة لأنه أتى بما في وسعه، وأما الاجتماع فليس في وسعه فلا يقابله الأجر . وفي الخلاصة : ولو استأجره ليبلغ الرسالة إلى فلان بالبصرة فذهب الرجل فلم يجد المرسل إليه أو وجده لكن لم يبلغ الرسالة ورجع فله الأجر اله. أقول : لعله لم يبلغ الرسالة لعدم تمكنه من التبليغ فعذره. قال في الخلاصة : والفرق بين الرسالة والكتاب أن الرسالة قد تكون سراً لا يرضى المرسل أن يطلع عليها غيره، أما الكتاب فمختوم. قال الشيخ الإمام شمس الأئمة الحلواني : لا نسلم الفرق بل هما سواء في الحكم اهـ. وفي المحيط : استأجر خياطاً ليخيط قميصاً فخاطه ففتقه رجل قبل أن يقبضه رب الثوب فلا أجر له لأنه تلف قبل التسليم، ولا يجبر الخياط على أن يعيده فإن كان الخياط فتقه يجبر على عوده، استأجر ملاحاً لحمل طعام إلى موضع كذا فرد السفينة إنسان فلا أجر للملاح وليس له أن يعيد السفينة، وإن ردها الملاح بنفسه لزمه الرد، ولو استأجر سفينة مدة معلومة فانقضت المدة في أثناء البحر تترك السفينة في يده إلى بلوغ ذلك المكان، ولو استأجر سفينة لحمل طعام إلى موضع كذا فلما بلغت السفينة الموضع أو بعضه ردها الريح إلى الموضع الذي اكتراها منه قال محمد: إن كان صاحب الطعام . معه فعليه الأجر كله أو بعضه بقدر ما بلغ وإن لم يكن صاحب الطعام . معه فلا أجر عليه لأنه انتقض الحمل بالرد فلم يستوف المعقود عليه، وكذا لو اكترى بغلاً إلى موضع كذا فلما سار بعض الطريق جمع فرده إلى الموضع الذي خرج منه فعليه من الكراء بقدر ما سار لأنه صار مستوفياً للمنفعة بنفسه فلا يسقط عنه البدل بعد التسليم . قيد بقوله للجواب» لأنه لو لم يشترط الرد للجواب. قال الحدادي : ولو تركه حتى يوصله إليه حيث كان غائباً أو إلى قريبه حيث كان .
He said, may Allah have mercy on him: (And no wage for the carrier of the book for the reply nor for the carrier of food if he returns it due to death) meaning if he hired him to go with his food to so-and-so in Makkah or with gold and his book to him and bring back his reply, and he went and found so-and-so dead and returned, then there is no wage for him because he nullified the contracted object by returning, so it is as if he did nothing, thus he does not deserve the wage. Zufar said: he gets the wage for the food because the wage is in exchange for carrying the food to Makkah, and he fulfilled what was stipulated, so the wage is owed. Muhammad said: he gets the wage for going in transporting the book because he fulfilled part of the contracted object. We say: the wage is in exchange for the reply and transport, and it was not found, and he did not bring the contracted object, so no wage, just as if the tailor unstitches the stitching after finishing the work. If he found him absent, it is as if he found him dead due to inability to reach him. If he left the book there to be delivered to him or his heirs, he gets the wage for going because he did his utmost. In al-Muhit: if he hired a messenger to deliver his message to so-and-so in Baghdad, and he went and returned, he gets the wage because the wage is for covering the distance, as he did what he could; but meeting is not within his capacity, so wage is not against it. In al-Khulasa: if he hired him to deliver a message to so-and-so in Basra, and the man went and did not find the addressee or found him but did not deliver the message and returned, he gets the wage. I say: perhaps he did not deliver because he was unable to deliver, so he is excused. In al-Khulasa: the difference between a verbal message and a written letter is that a message may be secret which the sender does not want others to know, whereas a letter is sealed. Shaykh Imam Shams al-A'imma al-Halwani said: we do not accept this difference; both are equal in ruling. In al-Muhit: he hired a tailor to sew a shirt, and he sewed it, then a man tore it before the owner took possession, so no wage for the tailor because it was destroyed before delivery; and the tailor is not forced to redo it. If the tailor tore it, he is forced to redo. He hired a sailor to carry food to a certain place, and someone turned the ship back, so no wage for the sailor, and he does not have the right to re-send the ship. If the sailor himself turned it back, he must redo. If he hired a ship for a fixed period and the period expired at sea, the ship is left with him until reaching that place. If he hired a ship to carry food to a certain place, and when the ship reached the place or part of it, the wind drove it back to the place of hire, Muhammad said: if the owner of the food is with him, then he owes the full wage or part proportionally to how far it went; if the owner is not with him, then no wage because the carriage was nullified by the return and he did not receive the contracted object. Similarly, if he hired a mule to go to a certain place, and after traveling part of the way, something forced it back to the starting point, then he owes rent proportional to the distance traveled because he himself enjoyed the benefit, so the compensation does not fall due after delivery. The restriction 'for the reply' is because if the return of the reply was not stipulated, then... Al-Haddadi said: and if he left it to be delivered to him while he was absent or to his relative where he was.
Source pages p. 15

Commentary
This final matn deals with the carrier of a book or food when the recipient is dead. The ruling is that no wage is due if he returns because the contracted benefit (delivery and reply) is not realized. The commentary presents a intra-Hanafi dispute: Zufar argues for wage in the food case because the carrier performed the transport; Muhammad argues for wage for the journey in the book case. The text rebuts both, stating that the wage is for the reply and transport, and since the reply was not obtained, no wage is due. An analogy is made to a tailor who undoes his work. If the recipient is absent, it is like being dead. If the carrier leaves the book to be delivered later, he gets wage for the journey. The commentary then compares a messenger (risala) vs a letter (kitab), with disagreement between al-Halwani and others. Various subsidiary rulings about tailors, sailors, and ships illustrate the principle that the wage is for the completed contracted benefit, and if the work is undone by external factors, no wage unless the worker did his utmost. The final part discusses restrictions and exceptions.

Key Terms
الرسالة (al-risala): A verbal message to be delivered orally.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon Hanafi position, what wage does a carrier receive if he returns because the recipient is dead?
A) Full wage for his trouble.
B) Half wage for the journey.
C) No wage at all.
D) The wage minus the cost of return.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, a carrier is not entitled to wage if the recipient dies and he returns, because the contracted benefit was not realized.

Ijarah — Hire and Lease
intermediate
10 min
Hiring a Carrier: No Wage if Recipient Dies Before Delivery
Commentary on matn with intra-Hanafi dispute and qiyas.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on a hired carrier's wage when the recipient is found dead, explain the intra-Hanafi dispute, and apply the qiyas to analogous cases.

Core Idea
If a hired carrier returns because the recipient is dead, no wage is due—the contract's entire service was not completed.

This lesson examines a specific ruling in ijarah: a person hires a carrier to deliver food or a letter and bring back a reply. What if the carrier reaches the destination but finds the recipient dead? The Hanafi school holds that the carrier deserves no wage, even though part of the journey was completed. This ruling is based on a precise understanding of what is contracted—the complete service including the reply—and is defended against alternative views from within the school.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is hiring a carrier to deliver food/letter and bring back a reply. The Hanafi ruling: no wage if the carrier returns due to the recipient's death.
The ruling is from Kanz al-Daqa'iq and its commentary.
2
Locate the dalil
The proof is a qiyas: a tailor who sews a shirt then undoes it gets no wage because the benefit is destroyed. Similarly, the carrier's return destroys the contracted benefit (delivery plus reply).
The qiyas is used to rebut the partial wage arguments.
3
Note the ikhtilaf
Zafar argued the carrier deserves full wage for food because carriage was completed. Muhammad argued for partial wage (outward journey) for the letter because part of the contract was fulfilled.
These are intra-Hanafi differences; the matn's position is the relied-upon.
4
Analyze the Hanafi response
The wage is in exchange for the entire service (transport plus reply). Since the reply was not obtained, the service is unfulfilled, so no wage is due.
The commentary emphasizes that returning cancels the contract.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
Practical consequence: in Hanafi practice, the carrier gets nothing; in Zafar's view, full wage for food; in Muhammad's view, wage for outward journey for the letter.
The mufta bihi is the Hanafi position (no wage).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الإجارة ١٥ الكتاب للجواب ولا لحامل الطعام إن رده للموت . يجد فلاناً . الأول على الذهاب والحمل وعزاه إلى الذخيرة. وروى هشام عن محمد لا أجر ومثله في السفينة .اهـ. كلام الشارح وفي التتارخانية من باب ما يستحق الفارس : استأجره ليحمل له كذا كذا من المطمورة فذهب فلم يجد المطمورة استحق نصف الأجرة .اهـ. فظهر أنه لا فرق كما ذكره الشارح . قال رحمه الله : (ولا أجر الحامل الكتاب للجواب ولا لحامل الطعام إن رده للموت) يعني إذا استأجره ليذهب بطعامه إلى فلان بمكة أو الذهب بكتابه إليه ويجيء بجوابه فذهب ووجد فلاناً ميتاً ورده فلا أجر له لأنه نقض المعقود عليه بالرد فصار كأنه لم يفعل فلا يستحق الأجر . وقال زفر له الأجر في الطعام لأن الأجرة بمقابلة حمل الطعام إلى مكة وقد وفي بالمشروط عليه فاستحقت الأجرة وقال محمد له الأجرة للذهاب في نقل الكتاب لأنه أوفى ببعض المعقود عليه . قلنا الأجرة مقابلة بالجواب والنقل ولم يوجد ولم يأت بالمعقود عليه فلا أجر له كما لو نقض الخياط الخياطة بعد الفراغ من العمل فلو وجده غائباً فهو كما لو وجده ميتاً لتعذر الوصول إليه، ولو ترك الكتاب هناك ليوصله إليه أو إلى ورثته فله الأجر في الذهاب لأنه أتى بأقصى ما في وسعه. قال في المحيط : ولو استأجر رسولاً ليبلغ رسالته إلى فلان ببغداد فلم وعاد فله الأجر لأن الأجر بقطع المسافة لأنه أتى بما في وسعه، وأما الاجتماع فليس في وسعه فلا يقابله الأجر . وفي الخلاصة : ولو استأجره ليبلغ الرسالة إلى فلان بالبصرة فذهب الرجل فلم يجد المرسل إليه أو وجده لكن لم يبلغ الرسالة ورجع فله الأجر اله. أقول : لعله لم يبلغ الرسالة لعدم تمكنه من التبليغ فعذره. قال في الخلاصة : والفرق بين الرسالة والكتاب أن الرسالة قد تكون سراً لا يرضى المرسل أن يطلع عليها غيره، أما الكتاب فمختوم. قال الشيخ الإمام شمس الأئمة الحلواني : لا نسلم الفرق بل هما سواء في الحكم اهـ. وفي المحيط : استأجر خياطاً ليخيط قميصاً فخاطه ففتقه رجل قبل أن يقبضه رب الثوب فلا أجر له لأنه تلف قبل التسليم، ولا يجبر الخياط على أن يعيده فإن كان الخياط فتقه يجبر على عوده، استأجر ملاحاً لحمل طعام إلى موضع كذا فرد السفينة إنسان فلا أجر للملاح وليس له أن يعيد السفينة، وإن ردها الملاح بنفسه لزمه الرد، ولو استأجر سفينة مدة معلومة فانقضت المدة في أثناء البحر تترك السفينة في يده إلى بلوغ ذلك المكان، ولو استأجر سفينة لحمل طعام إلى موضع كذا فلما بلغت السفينة الموضع أو بعضه ردها الريح إلى الموضع الذي اكتراها منه قال محمد: إن كان صاحب الطعام . معه فعليه الأجر كله أو بعضه بقدر ما بلغ وإن لم يكن صاحب الطعام . معه فلا أجر عليه لأنه انتقض الحمل بالرد فلم يستوف المعقود عليه، وكذا لو اكترى بغلاً إلى موضع كذا فلما سار بعض الطريق جمع فرده إلى الموضع الذي خرج منه فعليه من الكراء بقدر ما سار لأنه صار مستوفياً للمنفعة بنفسه فلا يسقط عنه البدل بعد التسليم . قيد بقوله للجواب» لأنه لو لم يشترط الرد للجواب. قال الحدادي : ولو تركه حتى يوصله إليه حيث كان غائباً أو إلى قريبه حيث كان ميتاً استحق الأجر كاملاً قال : فلو شرط عليه الجواب فدفعه إليه فلم يقرأه حتى عاد من غير جواب له الأجر كاملاً لأنه أتى بما في وسعه، ولو لم يجده أو وجده ولم يدفع له بل رد الكتاب فلا أجر له، ولو نسي الكتاب هناك لا يستحق أجرة الذهاب اهـ. والله تعالى أعلم.
The book of Ijarah. It is not permissible for the carrier of a letter for a reply nor for the carrier of food if he returns it due to [the recipient's] death. He finds so-and-so. The first [view is] for going and carrying, and [the commentator] attributed it to al-Dhakhira. Hisham narrated from Muhammad: no wage, and similarly for the boat. End of commentator's speech. In al-Tatarakhaniyyah from the chapter on what the horseman deserves: He hired him to carry for him such-and-such from the underground store, and he went and did not find the store, he deserves half the wage. End. So it appears there is no difference as the commentator mentioned. He said, may Allah have mercy on him: (And no wage for the carrier of the letter for a reply nor for the carrier of food if he returns it due to death). Meaning if he hired him to go with his food to so-and-so in Mecca or with his letter to him and bring back his reply, and he went and found so-and-so dead and returned, then he has no wage because he canceled the contracted [service] by returning, so it is as if he did nothing, so he does not deserve the wage. Zafar said he has the wage for the food because the wage is in exchange for carrying the food to Mecca, and he fulfilled what was stipulated, so the wage is deserved. Muhammad said he has the wage for going in transporting the letter because he fulfilled part of the contracted [service]. We said: the wage is in exchange for the reply and transport, and it did not occur, and he did not bring the contracted [service], so he has no wage, just as if a tailor undoes the stitching after finishing the work. If he found him absent, it is as if he found him dead due to the impossibility of reaching him. And if he left the letter there to have it delivered to him or to his heirs, he has the wage for going because he did his utmost. He said in al-Muhit: If he hired a messenger to deliver his message to so-and-so in Baghdad, and he went and returned, he has the wage because the wage is for covering the distance, as he did what was in his power; as for meeting, it is not in his power, so the wage does not correspond to it. In al-Khulasa: If he hired him to deliver the message to so-and-so in Basra, and the man went and did not find the addressee, or found him but did not deliver the message and returned, he has the wage. I say: perhaps he did not deliver the message due to inability to deliver, so he has an excuse. He said in al-Khulasa: The difference between a message and a letter is that a message might be a secret which the sender does not want anyone else to know, whereas a letter is sealed. Shaykh al-Imam Shams al-A'imma al-Halwani said: We do not accept the difference; rather both are equal in ruling. End. In al-Muhit: He hired a tailor to sew a shirt, and he sewed it, then a man tore it before the owner of the cloth took possession, so no wage for the tailor because it was destroyed before delivery, and the tailor is not compelled to redo it; but if the tailor tore it, he is compelled to redo it. He hired a boatman to carry food to a certain place, and a person returned the boat, so no wage for the boatman, and he does not have the right to return the boat; but if the boatman himself returned it, he is obliged to return. If he hired a boat for a known period and the period expired in mid-sea, the boat is left in his hand until reaching that place. If he hired a boat to carry food to a certain place, and when the boat reached the place or partway, the wind returned it to the place from which he hired it, Muhammad said: If the owner of the food is with him, he owes the full wage or part of it according to the distance; if the owner of the food is not with him, he owes no wage because the carriage was invalidated by the return, so he did not receive the contracted thing. Similarly, if he hired a mule to go to a certain place, and when he had gone partway, a crowd returned him to the place from which he set out, he owes from the hire proportionally to the distance he traveled, because he became a recipient of the benefit himself, so the compensation does not fall after delivery. [The author] restricted by saying "for the reply" because if he did not stipulate the return for the reply, [it would be otherwise]. Al-Hadadi said: If he left it to have it delivered to him whether he was absent or to his relative if he was dead, he deserves the full wage. He said: If he stipulated the reply and handed it to him and he did not read it until he returned without a reply, he has the full wage because he did his utmost. If he did not find him or found him but did not hand over to him but rather returned the letter, he has no wage. If he forgot the letter there, he does not deserve the wage for going. End. And Allah Almighty knows best.
Source pages p. 15

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the matn from Kanz al-Daqa'iq: 'And no wage for the carrier of a letter for a reply, nor for the carrier of food if he returns it due to death.' The commentator explains that if someone hires another to carry food or a letter to a specific person in a specific place and to bring back a reply, but upon arrival the recipient is found dead, the hired carrier has no wage because returning the item cancels the contract. This is the Hanafi position. Zafar argues that for food, the wage is earned for the act of carrying, which was completed. Muhammad argues that for the letter, the wage for the outward journey is due since part of the contract was fulfilled. The commentator rebuts both: the wage is for the entire service (carry plus reply), and since the reply was not obtained, no wage is due. The text then extends the ruling to analogous cases: if the recipient is absent, it is like death. If the carrier leaves the letter for delivery, he gets the wage for the journey. The distinction between a message (which may be confidential) and a letter (which is sealed) is rejected by al-Halwani, who says both are equal. Additional rulings from al-Muhit cover a tailor whose work is destroyed before delivery and a boatman whose cargo is returned—in both cases, no wage. The passage concludes with al-Hadadi's elaboration: if the carrier delivered to a relative of the deceased, he gets full wage; if he stipulated a reply but the recipient didn't read the letter, he still gets the wage for doing his utmost.

Key Terms
أجر (ajr): Wage or payment for hired service.
جواب (jawab): Reply; in this context, the return message from the recipient.
حامل الكتاب (hamil al-kitab): The carrier of a letter.
حامل الطعام (hamil al-ta'am): The carrier of food.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a person hires a carrier to deliver food to a specific person in Mecca and bring back a reply, but upon arrival the recipient is found dead, what is the Hanafi ruling on the carrier's wage?
A) The carrier deserves full wage because he carried the food to Mecca.
B) The carrier deserves half wage for the outward journey.
C) The carrier deserves no wage because he returned with the food without obtaining a reply.
D) The carrier deserves compensation for his effort.

Key Takeaway
A hired carrier who returns because the recipient is dead does not deserve any wage because the contracted service—delivery and reply—was not completed.

Renting Houses and Shops Without Specifying Use: Hanafi Istihsan
Explanation of permissibility of renting houses/shops without specification

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi school permits renting houses and shops without specifying the use and apply istihsan to override qiyas in similar rental contracts.

Core Idea
Custom (urf) makes specification unnecessary in renting houses and shops because use does not affect value.

In this passage from Al-Bahr al-Raiq, the author explains a key Hanafi ruling: renting a house or shop is valid even if the contract does not state how the property will be used. This seems to contradict qiyas, which would require specification. However, the Hanafi school applies istihsan (juristic preference) based on two factors: the customary use is residence, and the rental value does not vary significantly with different uses. The text also clarifies what the tenant may do and the effect of specifying a use.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Ruling
The matn states: 'صح إجارة الدور والحوانيت بلا بيان ما يعمل فيها' — renting houses and shops is valid without specifying the use. This is the mufta bihi position.
2
Understand the Qiyas Objection
Qiyas would require specification because houses and shops can be used for multiple purposes, just like hiring land for farming or clothes for wearing. The illa is that use affects the value.
The asl is hiring land/clothes; the hukm is that specification is required.
3
Analyze the Istihsan Reasoning
Two reasons: (1) The customary use of houses and shops is residence (or similar), and custom acts as an implied condition. (2) The rental value does not differ with the type of use, unlike land or clothes.
Istihsan overrides qiyas due to these practical considerations.
4
Examine the Disagreement on 'for Residence'
Taj al-Shari'ah interprets 'for residence' as describing the property, so if specified, the tenant cannot do otherwise. But the author of Ghayat al-Bayan argues it relates to the hiring, and the tenant may do anything not harming the building.
The commentator sides with the latter, because restriction in non-differential matters is not binding.
5
Apply the Ruling to Tenant's Actions
When the contract is absolute, the tenant may live alone or with others, store goods (even animals), and perform acts like ablution, bathing, washing clothes, as long as they do not weaken the building.
The key limit is not harming the structure.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب ما يجوز من الإجارة وما يكون خلافاً فيها قال في النهاية : لما ذكر مقدمات الإجارة ذكر في هذا الباب ما هو المقصود منها وهو بيان ما يجوز من عقود الإجارة وما لا يجوز وفي غاية البيان لما فرغ من ذكر الإجارة وشرطها ووقت استحقاق الأجرة ذكر ما يجوز من الإجارة بإطلاق اللفظ وتقيده، وذكر أيضاً من الأفعال ما يعد خلافاً من الأجير للمؤجر وما لا يعد خلافاً. قال رحمه الله : (صح إجارة الدور والحوانيت بلا بيان ما يعمل فيها والقياس أن لا تجوز هذه الإجارة حتى يبين ما يعمل فيها لأن الدار تصلح للسكنى ولغيرها، وكذا الحوانيت تصلح لأشياء مختلفة فينبغي أن لا تجوز حتى يبين ما يعمل فيها كاستئجار الأرض للزراعة والثياب للبس. وجه الاستحسان أن العمل المتعارف فيها السكنى والمتعارف كالمشروط ولأن إجارتها لا تختلف باختلاف العامل والعمل فجاز إجارتها مطلقاً بخلاف الأراضي والثياب لأنهما يختلفان، وعبارة المؤلف أحسن من عبارة صاحب الهداية حيث زاد للسكنى لسلامته عما أورد على هذا اللفظ. قال تاج الشريعة : قوله للسكنى صلة الدور والحوانيت لا صلة الاستئجار يعني ويجوز استئجار الدور والحوانيت المعدة للسكنى لا أن يقول زمان العقد استأجرت هذه الدار للسكنى لأنه لو نص على هذا وقت العقد لا يكون له أن يعمل فيها غير السكنى ..اهـ. كلامه. قال صاحب غاية البيان : ويجوز أن يتعلق قوله للسكنى بالاستئجار أي يجوز استئجار الدور والحوانيت للسكنى وله أن يعمل فيها كل شيء لا يوهن البناء ولا يفسده وهو الظاهر من كلام القدوري اهـ. وقول تاج الشريعة لو نص على السكنى ليس له أن يعمل غيرها كما سيأتي ليس بظاهر لأنه لو عمل غيرها بما هو . أنفع من السكنى بأن خزن فيها براً أو غيره يجوز لأن التقييد فيما لا يتفاوت لا يعتبر، ولو استحق المستأجر من يد المستأجر وقد هلك عنده وضمنه يرجع على الذي أجره ولا أجر عليه فيما استعمله لأن الأجرة والضمان لا يجتمعان . قال رحمه الله : (وله أن يعمل فيها كل شيء لما ذكرنا من أنها لا تختلف باختلاف العامل والعمل فجاز له أن يعمل فيها ما شاء عند الإطلاق، وله أن يسكن غيره معه أو ينفرد ولأن كثرة السكان لا يضر بها بل يزيد في عمارتها لأن خراب المسكن بترك السكان وله أن يضع فيها ما بدا له حتى الحيوان وله أن يعمل فيها ما بدا له من العمل كالوضوء والاغتسال وغسل الثياب وكسر
Chapter on what is permissible in ijarah and what constitutes a violation in it. He said in al-Nihayah: When he mentioned the preliminaries of ijarah, he mentioned in this chapter what is intended from it, which is an explanation of what is permissible from contracts of ijarah and what is not permissible. And in Ghayat al-Bayan: When he finished mentioning ijarah, its conditions, and the time of entitlement to the wage, he mentioned what is permissible from ijarah with absolute wording and its restriction, and he also mentioned actions that constitute a violation on the part of the hired person towards the employer and what does not constitute a violation. He (the author) said: (The renting of houses and shops is valid without specifying what is to be done in them. Analogy would necessitate that this ijarah should not be valid until what is to be done in them is specified, because the house is suitable for residence and for other purposes, and similarly shops are suitable for various things, so it should not be valid until what is to be done in them is specified, like hiring land for farming and clothes for wearing. The basis of istihsan is that the customary use in them is residence, and what is customary is like a stipulated condition; and because their ijarah does not differ with the difference of the worker and the work, so it is permissible to rent them absolutely, unlike lands and clothes because they differ. And the author's expression is better than that of the author of al-Hidayah because he added "for residence" to avoid what has been objected to this wording. Taj al-Shari'ah said: His statement "for residence" is a qualifier of houses and shops, not of the hiring; meaning that it is permissible to rent houses and shops prepared for residence, not that he says at the time of the contract "I rent this house for residence," because if he specifies this at the time of the contract, he does not have the right to do in it other than residence... end of his comment. The author of Ghayat al-Bayan said: It is possible that his statement "for residence" relates to the hiring, i.e., it is permissible to rent houses and shops for residence, and he has the right to do in them anything that does not weaken the building or corrupt it, and that is apparent from the statement of al-Quduri. And the statement of Taj al-Shari'ah that if he specifies residence, he cannot do other than it, as will come, is not apparent because if he does other than it that is better than residence, like storing wheat or other things, it is permissible, because restriction in what does not differ is not considered. And if the lessee [something] from the hand of the lessee and it perished with him and he guaranteed it, he gets recourse against the one who rented it to him, and there is no wage on him for what he used, because wage and guarantee do not combine. He said: (And he has the right to do in them everything) because we mentioned that they do not differ with the difference of the worker and the work, so it is permissible for him to do in them whatever he wishes when the contract is absolute. And he has the right to let others live with him or to live alone, because an abundance of residents does not harm them but rather increases their construction, because the ruin of a dwelling is caused by leaving it empty. And he has the right to place in them whatever he wants, even animals, and he has the right to do in them whatever work he wants, like ablution, bathing, washing clothes, and breaking [something?].
Source pages p. 16

Commentary
This passage opens a new chapter on what is permissible in ijarah and what constitutes a violation. The commentator first cites al-Nihayah explaining the purpose of the chapter. The matn states that renting houses and shops is valid without specifying the use. By qiyas, this would not be valid because the property can be used for multiple purposes, just like land for farming which requires specification. However, istihsan (juristic preference) permits it because the customary use of houses and shops is residence, and custom functions as an implicit condition. Additionally, the rental value does not vary significantly with different uses. The author's wording is considered superior to al-Hidayah's addition of 'for residence' because it avoids confusion. Taj al-Shari'ah interprets 'for residence' as describing the property, not the contract, but the author of Ghayat al-Bayan argues it can relate to the hiring, allowing the tenant to do anything that does not weaken the building. The text then discusses the consequence of specifying 'for residence': according to Taj al-Shari'ah, the tenant cannot do otherwise, but the commentator disagrees, saying that if the tenant does something more beneficial like storing wheat, it is permissible because the specification regarding non-differential uses is not binding. The passage concludes by listing the tenant's rights: he can live with others, store animals, and perform various acts like ablution, bathing, and washing clothes, as long as they do not weaken the building.

Key Terms
دور (dur): Houses or dwellings.
حوانيت (hawanit): Shops or commercial premises.
استحسان (istihsan): Juristic preference that overrides qiyas due to practical necessity or custom.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, why is renting a house without specifying the use considered valid?
A) Because the Prophet (s) explicitly permitted it in a hadith.
B) Because houses are only used for residence, so specification is unnecessary.
C) Because custom treats the house as for residence, and custom acts as an implied condition; also rental value does not vary.
D) Because any use is permissible under any circumstances, even if it damages the building.

Key Takeaway
Renting houses and shops without specifying use is valid due to istihsan, and the tenant has broad freedom limited only by avoiding structural harm.

Ijarah — Hire and Lease

Leasing Houses and Shops Without Specification: Istihsan Overrides Qiyas
Ruling on permissibility of absolute lease of houses/shops and conditions for land lease

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi school permits leasing houses and shops without specifying the use, using istihsan based on custom, and distinguish between permissible and prohibited uses based on structural harm.

Core Idea
Customary use in houses and shops is like a stipulation; lease is valid absolutely unless the use causes structural harm.

In the Hanafi school, leasing a house or shop without specifying the tenant's activity is valid, even though strict analogy would require specification. This ruling rests on istihsan (juristic preference) rooted in the customary use of such properties. The passage from Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq explains the reasoning and details exceptions for trades that damage the building. Understanding this principle clarifies how custom can shape contractual validity in Hanafi fiqh.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Ruling and the Qiyas Objection
State the rule: houses and shops can be leased without specifying use. Then note that qiyas would demand specification, analogizing to land and garments where use varies significantly.
Qiyas here is a strict analogy that the author uses as a baseline before introducing istihsan.
2
Analyze the Istihsan Basis
Two reasons: (1) Customary use (dwelling) is like a stipulated condition; (2) the lease value does not change with common uses.
Istihsan overrides qiyas because the effective cause (variation of use) is absent in houses and shops.
3
Apply the Exceptions for Harmful Trades
Identify which specific activities are prohibited: blacksmithing, fulling, and milling with water or ox mills. Hand mills are allowed unless built into walls. The guiding principle is structural harm.
The contract implicitly restricts the lessee from causing damage. Normal wood-breaking and cooking are permitted; excessive damage requires owner consent.
4
Extend to Land Lease Conditions
For agricultural land, lease is valid only if the crop is specified or if the contract gives a general permission ('whatever he wishes'). This difference from houses is due to significant variation in land use.
Land lease follows the general qiyas rule because custom does not create a uniform expectation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب ما يجوز من الإجارة وما يكون خلافاً فيها
صح إجارة الدور والحوانيت بلا بيان ما يعمل فيها والقياس أن لا تجوز هذه الإجارة حتى يبين ما يعمل فيها لأن الدار تصلح للسكنى ولغيرها، وكذا الحوانيت تصلح لأشياء مختلفة فينبغي أن لا تجوز حتى يبين ما يعمل فيها كاستئجار الأرض للزراعة والثياب للبس. وجه الاستحسان أن العمل المتعارف فيها السكنى والمتعارف كالمشروط ولأن إجارتها لا تختلف باختلاف العامل والعمل فجاز إجارتها مطلقاً بخلاف الأراضي والثياب لأنهما يختلفان. وله أن يعمل فيها كل شيء إلا أنه لا يسكن حداداً أو قصاراً أو طحاناً لأن في نصب الرحى واستعمالها في هذه الأشياء ضراراً ظاهراً لأنه يوهن البناء فيتقيد العقد بما وراءها دلالة. والمراد بالرحى رحى الماء والثور، وأما رحى اليد فلا يمنع منها لأنها لا تضر بالبناء. وفي الحدادي رحى اليد إذا بنيت في الحائط يمنع منها. وله أن يكسر فيها الحطب الكسر المعتاد، وله أن يطبخ فيها الطبخ المعتاد وإن زاد على العادة بحيث يوهن البناء فليس له ذلك إلا برضا صاحب الدار، وينبغي أن يكون الدق على هذا التفصيل. والأراضي للزراعة أن بين ما يزرع فيها أو قال على أن يزرع ما شاء) يعني يجوز استئجار الأرض للزراعة إن بين ما يزرع فيها أو قال على أن يزرع فيها ما يشاء
Chapter on what is permissible in ijarah and what constitutes a violation. It is valid to lease houses and shops without specifying what will be done in them. The analogy is that this lease is not valid until what will be done in them is specified, because a house is suitable for dwelling and other things, and likewise shops are suitable for various things, so it should not be valid until what will be done in them is specified, like leasing land for cultivation and garments for wearing. The basis of istihsan is that the customary use in them is dwelling, and the customary is like the stipulated, and because their lease does not vary with the variation of the worker and the work, so it is valid to lease them absolutely, unlike lands and garments because they vary. And he may do everything in them except that he may not accommodate a blacksmith, a fuller, or a miller, because installing the mill and using these things causes apparent harm, as it weakens the building, so the contract is implicitly restricted to beyond that. What is meant by mill is water mill and ox mill; as for hand mill, it is not prevented because it does not harm the building. And regarding blacksmithing, if a hand mill is built into the wall, it is prevented. And he may break firewood in it in the usual manner, and he may cook in it in the usual manner, but if it exceeds the custom such that it weakens the building, he does not have that except with the owner's consent, and pounding should be similarly detailed. And for lands for cultivation, that he specify what he will plant in it or say 'on condition that he plants whatever he wishes' – meaning it is valid to lease land for cultivation if he specifies what he will plant in it or says 'on condition that he plants whatever he wishes'.
Source pages p. 16

Commentary
This passage from Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq is an expansion of the matn from Kanz al-Daqa'iq regarding the permissibility of leasing houses and shops without specifying the use, and the conditions for leasing agricultural land. The author, Ibn Nujaym, first states the ruling from the matn: it is valid (sahih) to lease houses and shops without specifying what will be done in them. He then explains the legal reasoning: qiyas (analogy) would require specification, analogizing to the lease of land for cultivation or garments for wearing, where use significantly matters. However, istihsan (juristic preference) prevails because the customary use of houses and shops is dwelling/storage, which does not vary significantly, and custom is treated as a stipulated condition. Furthermore, the lease value does not differ based on the specific use. Therefore, the absolute lease is valid. The commentator clarifies that the lessee may use the property for any purpose that does not cause structural harm. Specifically prohibited are trades like blacksmithing, fulling, and milling that involve heavy equipment (water or ox mills) which weaken the building. Hand mills are generally allowed unless built into walls. The lessee may break firewood and cook in the usual manner, but excessive use that damages the building requires the owner's consent. Finally, the passage addresses leasing land for cultivation: it is valid only if the crop is specified or if the contract states 'whatever he wishes', because land use varies significantly.

Key Terms
الاستحسان (al-istihsan): Juristic preference overriding qiyas due to custom (muta'araf) or necessity; here used to validate absolute lease of houses/shops.
المتعارف (al-muta'araf): Customary practice; in this context, the typical use of houses (dwelling) is considered like a stipulated condition.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi ruling in this lesson, which of the following uses in a leased house is PROHIBITED without the owner's explicit consent?
A) Sleeping and storing furniture
B) Cooking ordinary meals
C) Operating a water mill for grinding grain
D) Breaking firewood for the fireplace

Key Takeaway
Houses and shops can be leased absolutely by Hanafi law due to istihsan based on custom, but uses causing structural harm are implicitly prohibited; agricultural land always requires crop specification or general permission.

Restrictions on Tenant's Use of a Rented House
Explains prohibited trades and liability in a rented house.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state which trades and activities are prohibited in a rented house and apply the Hanafi ruling on liability if the tenant violates the restriction.

Core Idea
The tenant cannot use the rented house for any activity that weakens the building; if he does, he is liable for compensation or additional rent by istihsan.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq expands on a ruling from Kanz al-Daqaiq regarding the tenant's use of a rented house. It clarifies that certain trades are implicitly excluded because they cause structural damage, and it details the consequences should the tenant engage in them. Understanding this helps you see how Hanafi jurists balance contractual terms with practical realities using istihsan.

Guided Path
1
Identify the prohibited trades
List the three trades explicitly mentioned: blacksmith (haddad), fuller (qassar), and miller (tahhan). The prohibition is because these involve heavy equipment that weakens the building.
2
Distinguish harmful from harmless activities
The text distinguishes between water/ox-mills (prohibited) and hand-mills (allowed unless built into wall); likewise, breaking firewood and cooking are allowed if usual, but excessive activities require permission.
3
Understand the consequence if the building collapses
If the tenant's prohibited work causes the building to collapse, he must pay compensation (daman) because he is a transgressor, and no rent is due for that period because compensation and rent cannot combine.
4
Understand the consequence if no collapse
If no collapse, rent is due by istihsan (juristic preference), overriding qiyas which would say no rent since the work was not in the contract.
5
Note the analogy and conflict resolution
The istihsan is analogized to hiring an animal and increasing its load; if safe, extra rent is due. Also, if lessor and tenant disagree, the lessor's word is taken, but if both have evidence, the tenant's evidence is preferred.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
لا يسكن حداداً أو قصاراً أو طحاناً والأراضي للزراعة أن بين ما يزرع فيها أو قال الحطب لأن ذلك كله من توابع السكنى. وذكر في النهاية أنه لا يدخل الحيوان في عرفنا لأن المنازل ضيقة.اهـ. ويربطها على الباب فإن أجره صحن الدار ربطها في الصحن. وليس للمؤجر أن يدخل دابته الدار بعدما أجرها، ولو كان فيها بئر أو بالوعة فسدت لا يجبر على إصلاحها، ولو بنى المستأجر التنور في الدار المستأجرة فاحترق شيء من الدار لم يضمن؛ كذا في الخلاصة. وفي المحيط : وله أن يربط الدابة إن كان في الدار سعة أما إن كانت ضيقة فلا، ولو استأجر داراً على أن يسكنها وحده فله أن يترك امرأته معه لأنه شرط لا فائدة فيه وفي الخلاصة : وإذا ربط الدابة فضربت إنساناً أو هدمت الحائط لم يضمن اهـ. اهـ . قال رحمه الله : (إلا أنه لا يسكن حداداً أو قصاراً أو طحاناً لأن في نصب الرحى واستعمالها في هذه الأشياء ضراراً ظاهراً لأنه يوهن البناء فيتقيد العقد بما وراءها دلالة. والمراد بالرحى رحى الماء والثور، وأما رحى اليد فلا يمنع منها لأنها لا تضر بالبناء. وفي الحدادي رحى اليد إذا بنيت في الحائط يمنع منها، وله أن يكسر فيها الحطب الكسر المعتاد، وله أن يطبخ فيها الطبخ المعتاد وإن زاد على العادة بحيث يوهن البناء فليس له ذلك إلا برضا صاحب الدار، وينبغي أن يكون الدق على هذا التفصيل، فظهر أن الحاصل كل ما يوهن البناء أوقيه ضرر ليس له أن يعمل فيها إلا بإذن وكل ما لا ضرر فيه جاز بمطلق العقد واستحقه به ولم يتعرض المؤلف لبيان ما يجب عليه إذا فعل ذلك ونحن نبينه، فلو أقعد حداداً فهدم البناء بعمله وجب الضمان لأنه متعدي ولا أجر لأن الضمان والأجر لا يجتمعان ولو لم ينهدم وجب عليه الأجر استحساناً، والقياس أن لا يجب لأن هذا العلم غير داخل تحت العقد. ووجه الإستحسان أن المعقود عليه هو السكنى وفي الحدادة وأخواتها السكنى وزيادة فيصير مستوفياً للمعقود عليه فيجب عليه الأجر بشرط السلامة فصار نظير ما لو استأجر دابة ليحمل عليها قدراً معلوماً فزاد عليها وسلمت الدابة فإنه يجب عليه الأجر. ولو اختلف المؤجر والمستأجر في اشتراط ذلك كان القول للمؤجر لأنه أنكر الإجارة، ولو أقاما البينة كانت بيئة المستأجر أولى. وفي الخلاصة: ولو استأجر ليقعد قصاراً فله أن يقعد حداداً إن كان ضررهما واحداً. وفي المحيط: أو كان ضرر الحداد أقل وإن كان أكثر فليس له ذلك وكذلك الرحى .اهـ. قيد بالدور لأن استئجار البناء وحده لا يجوز في ظاهر الرواية لأنه لا ينتفع به وحده وفي القنية ويفتي بجواز استئجار البناء وحده إذا كان ينتفع به كالجدار للسقف ولو أجره المستأجر من المؤجر لم يجز، والأصح أن العقد ينفسخ بالإجارة .
He does not let a blacksmith, a fuller, or a miller, and lands for agriculture specify what is sown therein or said firewood because all that is among the accessories of dwelling. And it is mentioned in al-Nihayah that animals are not included in our custom because houses are narrow. He ties it at the door; if he rented the courtyard of the house, he ties it in the courtyard. The lessor may not bring his animal into the house after he has rented it. If there is a well or a cesspool that becomes spoiled, he is not compelled to repair it. If the tenant built an oven in the rented house and something of the house burned, he does not guarantee; thus in al-Khulasa. In al-Muhit: He may tie the animal if the house has space; if it is narrow, then no. If he rented a house on condition that he dwell alone, it is permissible for him to leave his wife with him because it is a condition with no benefit. In al-Khulasa: If he tied the animal and it struck a person or demolished the wall, he does not guarantee. He said, may Allah have mercy on him: (Except that he does not let a blacksmith, fuller, or miller because setting up the mill and using these things is manifest harm, for it weakens the building, so the contract is restricted to what is beyond them by implication. What is meant by 'mill' is water-mill and ox-mill; as for hand-mill, it is not prevented because it does not harm the building. As for blacksmith's hand-mill, if built into the wall, it is prevented. He may break firewood in it in the usual manner, and he may cook in it in the usual manner. If he exceeds the usual to the extent that it weakens the building, he may not do that except with the consent of the house owner. Pounding should be similarly detailed. So it appears that the result is: whatever weakens the building or causes harm, he may not do it except with permission; whatever does no harm is permissible by the absolute contract and he deserves it. The author did not address what is obligatory upon him if he does that, and we explain it: If he installed a blacksmith and the building collapsed due to his work, compensation is obligatory because he is a transgressor, and no rent because compensation and rent do not combine. If it did not collapse, rent is obligatory by istihsan; by qiyas it would not be obligatory because that work is not included in the contract. The basis of istihsan is that the object of the contract is dwelling, and in blacksmithing and its likes there is dwelling plus an increase, so he becomes one who has received the object of the contract, thus rent is obligatory subject to safety. This is analogous to the case where someone hires an animal to carry a known load and increases the load and the animal is safe: rent is obligatory. If the lessor and tenant differ over stipulating that, the lessor's word is taken because he denies the lease; if both produce evidence, the tenant's evidence is preferred. In al-Khulasa: If he rented for a fuller, he may seat a blacksmith if the harm is equal. In al-Muhit: Or if the harm of the blacksmith is less; if it is greater, he may not do that, and similarly the mill. This is restricted to houses because renting the building alone is not permissible in zahir al-riwayah since it cannot be used alone; in al-Qunyah, a fatwa is given for the permissibility of renting the building alone if it can be used, like a wall for a roof. If the tenant sublets it to the lessor, it is not permissible, and the correct view is that the contract is invalidated by the lease.
Source pages p. 17

Commentary
This passage is an expansion of a ruling from the matn of Kanz al-Daqaiq regarding the tenant's use of a rented house. The author first states the basic rule: a tenant cannot bring in a blacksmith, fuller, or miller because these trades involve setting up heavy equipment (like mills) that visibly weaken the building structure. This restriction is implied in the contract even if not explicitly stated, because the default understanding is that dwelling (sukna) is the purpose, and any use that damages the building is excluded by implication. The commentary then distinguishes between types of mills: water-mills and ox-mills are prohibited because they cause structural harm, but hand-mills are generally allowed. However, if a hand-mill is built into the wall, it is prohibited. Similarly, the tenant may break firewood and cook in the usual manner, but if he exceeds the usual to the point of weakening the building, that requires the owner's permission. The same detailed distinction applies to pounding (daqq). The author then addresses the consequence if the tenant does a prohibited act: if the building collapses, the tenant must pay compensation for the damage (daman) because he is a transgressor, and no rent is due for that period because compensation and rent cannot combine. If the building does not collapse, the tenant must pay the rent by istihsan (juristic preference), even though qiyas (analogy) would suggest no rent since the prohibited use was not included in the contract. The istihsan reasoning is that the tenant still received the dwelling service (sukna) along with the extra benefit, so he owes rent subject to safety. This is analogized to hiring an animal for a specific load and then increasing the load: if the animal is safe, extra rent is due. The passage also discusses conflicts between lessor and tenant: if they disagree about stipulating such uses, the lessor's word is taken because he denies the lease (and the tenant claims an additional right). If both bring evidence, the tenant's evidence is given precedence because it affirms an extra condition beyond the contract's default. Finally, the ruling is restricted to houses: renting just the building (without the land) is not valid in zahir al-riwayah because it cannot be used alone, but a later fatwa allows it if it can be used (e.g., a wall as a roof prop). If the tenant sublets to the original lessor, that is invalid and the contract is terminated.

Key Terms
حداد (haddad): A blacksmith; a tenant cannot set up a blacksmith's workshop in a rented house due to the damage from hammering and heavy equipment.
قصار (qassar): A fuller (one who washes and presses cloth); prohibited for the same reason as blacksmith.
طحان (tahhan): A miller (grinding grain); prohibited if using a mill that weakens the building.
استحسان (istihsan): Juristic preference that allows a ruling contrary to qiyas due to custom, necessity, or fairness.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, if a tenant uses a rented house for blacksmithing and the building collapses due to his work, what is his liability?
A) He must pay compensation (daman) but no rent for the period.
B) He must pay both compensation and rent.
C) He owes nothing because the work was not in the contract.
D) He must pay rent but not compensation.

Key Takeaway
A tenant's use of a rented house is restricted by implied terms: activities that harm the building are prohibited, and if done, liability follows a nuanced rule of compensation or rent based on istihsan.
