Specifying the Crop in Agricultural Leases and Istihsan
Explains the requirement to specify the crop and the istihsan exception.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi rule that an agricultural lease requires crop specification or tenant discretion, and apply the istihsan exception that validates the lease upon actual sowing.

Core Idea
Uncertainty about the crop invalidates the lease; but once sown, istihsan cures the defect.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq expands the ruling of Kanz al-Daqaiq on renting land for agriculture. The benefit of land varies dramatically with the crop, so uncertainty (jahalah) about what will be planted leads to disputes. The Hanafi school balances contractual certainty with real-world flexibility through istihsan, allowing the contract to become valid once the crop is actually sown and known.

Guided Path
1
Identify the problem: jahalah
Recognise that the benefit of land differs according to crop; failure to specify creates dangerous uncertainty that invalidates the lease by default.
2
State the default qiyas ruling
If the crop is unspecified and no discretion is given, the lease is fasid (invalid) and remains invalid even after sowing according to strict analogy.
Qiyas demands certainty at contract formation.
3
Apply the istihsan exception
By juristic preference (istihsan), if the tenant actually sows, the lease becomes valid and the named rent is due because the subject matter becomes known through use.
Istihsan overrides qiyas to prevent hardship and dispute.
4
Examine the analogy to garment hire
The istihsan is analogised to hiring a garment without specifying the wearer: once worn, the hire becomes valid. The common illa is that the benefit becomes known by actual use.
This is a khafiyyah (hidden) analogy.
5
Distinguish subsidiary cases
Review rulings on free choice (two crops per year), partial irrigation, saline land, and non-agricultural uses (qayl, marah). Understand that land can be rented for any beneficial use, not just farming.
The passage clarifies common misconceptions.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال رحمه الله : ( والأراضي للزراعة أن بين ما يزرع فيها أو قال على أن يزرع فيها ما شاء) يعني يجوز استئجار الأرض للزراعة إن بين ما يزرع فيها أو قال على أن يزرع فيها ما يشاء لأن منفعة الأرض مختلفة باختلاف ما يزرع فيها لأنه منه ما ينفع كالبرسيم في ديارنا وما يضر كالقمح مثلاً فلا بد من بيانه أو يقول له ازرع فيها ما شئت كي لا يفضي إلى المنازعة. ولو لم يبين ولم يقل له ازرع فيها ما شئت فسدت الإجارة للجهالة ولو زرعها لا تعود صحيحة في القياس، وفي الاستحسان يجب المسمى وتنقلب صحيحة لأن المعقود صار صحيحاً معلوماً بالاستعمال، وصار كما لو استأجر ثوباً ولم يبين اللابس ثم ألبس إنساناً عادت صحيحة لما ذكرنا. وفي القنية: استأجر أرضاً سنة على أن يزرع فيها ما شاء فله أن يزرع فيها زرعين ربيعياً وخريفياً. وفي الجوهرة ولا بأس باستئجار الأرض للزراعة قبل ريها إن كانت معتادة للري في مثل هذه المدة التي عقد الإجارة عليها، وإن جاء من الماء ما يزرع به البعض فالمستأجر بالخيار إن شاء نقض الإجارة كلها، وإن شاء لم ينقض وكان عليه من الأجر بحساب ما روي منها .اهـ. وفي القنية : ولو استأجرها ولا يمكنه الزراعة في الحال لاحتياجها إلى السقي وكري الأنهار أو مجيء الماء، فإن كان بحال تمكنه الزراعة في مدة العقد جاز وإلا فلا كما لو استأجرها في الشتاء تسعة أشهر ويمكن زراعتها في الشتاء جاز لما أمكن من المدة، أما إذا لم يمكن الأنتفاع بها أصلاً بأن كانت سبخة فالإجارة فاسدة، وفي الاستئجار في الشتاء يكون الأجر مقابلاً بكل المدة لا بما ينتفع به فحسب، وقيل بما ينتفع به اهـ. واعلم أن الأرض لا ينحصر استئجارها للزراعة والبناء والغرس كما توهمه المتون فقد صرح في الهداية بأن الأرض تستأجر للزراعة وغيرها. وقال في غاية البيان: أراد بغير الزراعة البناء والغرس وطبخ والآجر والخزف ونحو ذلك من سائر الانتفاعات بالأرض اهـ . فإذا عرفت ذلك ظهر لك صحة الإجارات الواقعة في زماننا من أنه يستأجر الأرض مقيلاً ومراحاً قاصداً بذلك إلزام الأجرة بالتمكن منها مطلقاً، سواء شملها الماء وأمكن زراعتها أولاً، ولا شك في صحته لأنه لم يستأجرها للزراعة بخصوصها حتى يكون عدم ريها عيباً تنفسخ به. وفي الولوالجية : استأجر أرضاً ليلبن فيها فالإجارة فاسدة ثم هي على وجهين: إن كان للتراب قيمة ضمن قيمته وبكون اللبن له وإن لم يكن له قيمة فلا شيء عليه واللبن له وضمن نقصان الأرض إن نقصت وفي فتاوى قارئ الهداية : إن إجارة الأرض المشغولة بزرع الغير إن كان الزرع بحق بأن كان بأجرة لا يجوز أن يؤجر ما لم يستحصد الزرع إلا أن يؤجرها مضافة إلى المستقبل، وإن كان الزرع بغير مستند شرعي صحت الإجارة لأن الزرع في هذه الصورة واجب القلع فإن المؤجر في هذه الصورة قادر على تسليم ما أجره ويجب صاحب الزرع على قلعه سواء أدرك أم لا لأنه لا حق لصاحبه في إبقائه اهـ. والدار المشغولة بمتاع الساكن الذي ليس بمستأجر تصح إجارتها وابتداء المدة من حين تسليمها فارغة؛ كذا في القنية. وفي الخلاصة ولو أجر الأرض المزروعة ثم سلمه بعدما فرغ وحصد ينقلب جائزاً، ولو قال المستأجر أجرت منك الأرض وهي فارغة وقال المؤجر لا بل هي مشغولة
He, may Allah have mercy on him, said: (And lands for agriculture, that he specify what is sown therein or said on condition that he sows whatever he wishes) meaning it is permissible to rent land for agriculture if he specifies what is sown in it or if he says on condition that he sows therein whatever he wishes because the benefit of land differs according to what is sown in it, for among that is what benefits like alfalfa in our lands and what harms like wheat for example, so it must be specified or he says to him 'sow in it whatever you wish' to avoid dispute. And if he did not specify and did not say to him 'sow whatever you wish', the lease is invalid due to ignorance; if he sows it, it does not become valid by qiyas, but by istihsan the named [rent] is obligatory and it turns valid because the object of the contract becomes valid and known by use, and it becomes like the case where someone hires a garment without specifying the wearer, then he clothes a person, it becomes valid based on what we mentioned. In al-Qunyah: If he rents land for one year on condition that he sows whatever he wishes, he may sow two crops: spring and autumn. In al-Jawharah: There is no harm in renting land for agriculture before its irrigation if it is accustomed to irrigation within such period as the contract is made upon; and if water comes to irrigate only part, the tenant has the option: if he wishes he may rescind the entire lease, and if he wishes he may not rescind, and he must pay rent in proportion to what was irrigated. In al-Qunyah: If he rents it and cannot cultivate it immediately due to need for irrigation, digging canals, or the coming of water, then if he is able to cultivate within the term, it is permissible; otherwise not, as when he rents in winter for nine months and can cultivate in winter, it is permissible because it is possible within the term. But if he cannot benefit at all, e.g., saline land, the lease is invalid. In winter renting, the rent corresponds to the entire period, not just the benefited portion; it is also said to correspond to what is benefited. Know that land is not limited to being rented for agriculture, building, and planting as the texts might suggest; indeed it is stated in al-Hidayah that land may be rented for agriculture and other purposes. And in Ghayat al-Bayan: 'He intended by other than agriculture: building, planting, cooking, brick-making, pottery, and similar benefits from the land.' So if you know that, the validity of leases occurring in our time becomes clear: renting land for midday rest and shelter, intending thereby to obligate rent by mere ability to use absolutely, whether water covers it and cultivation is possible or not. There is no doubt about its validity because he did not rent it specifically for cultivation such that lack of irrigation would be a defect causing rescission. In al-Walwaljiyyah: If he rents land to make bricks, the lease is invalid; then it is of two types: if the soil has value, he guarantees its value and the bricks belong to him; if it has no value, nothing is upon him, the bricks are his, and he guarantees the land's decrease if it decreased. In Fatawa Qari' al-Hidayah: The leasing of land occupied by another's crop: if the crop is there by right (e.g., by a previous lease), it is not permissible to lease until the crop is harvested, unless leased for a future term. If the crop is without legal basis, the lease is valid because in this case the crop is obligated to be uprooted; the lessor is able to deliver what he leased, and the owner of the crop must uproot it whether ripe or not because he has no right to keep it. And a house occupied by the goods of a resident who is not a tenant: its lease is valid, and the term begins from the time it is delivered empty; thus in al-Qunyah. In al-Khulasa: If he leased the land while cultivated, then delivered it after it was cleared and harvested, it becomes valid. And if the tenant says 'I leased the land from you while it was empty' and the lessor says 'No, it was occupied.'
Source pages p. 17

Commentary
This passage is an expansion of the ruling from Kanz al-Daqaiq on renting land for agriculture. The matn states that for an agricultural lease to be valid, either the specific crop must be specified (e.g., wheat, barley) or the tenant must be given general permission to plant whatever he wishes (e.g., 'sow whatever you like'). This is because the benefit of land varies greatly with the crop: some crops enrich the soil (like alfalfa) while others deplete it (like wheat), so without specification there is dangerous uncertainty (jahalah) leading to disputes. If neither condition is met, the lease is invalid due to ignorance (jahalah) of the subject matter. However, by qiyas, if the tenant sows without specification, the lease does not become valid; but by istihsan, the lease becomes valid and the named rent is due because the object of the contract (the land's benefit) becomes known through actual use. This istihsan is analogized to hiring a garment without specifying the wearer: if someone then wears it, the contract becomes valid. The passage then presents various subsidiary rulings: if the lease gives the tenant free choice, he may plant two crops in a year (spring and autumn); it is permissible to rent land for agriculture before irrigation if irrigation is customary within the term; if water is insufficient, the tenant has an option to rescind the whole lease or pay proportional rent; if immediate cultivation is impossible due to preparation needs but possible within the term, the lease is valid; if the land is saline and useless, it is invalid. Importantly, the author clarifies that land is not limited to agriculture, building, or planting—it can be leased for any benefit, such as midday rest (qayl) or shelter (marah). This explains the common practice where land is rented with the intention of obligating rent merely by the ability to use it, regardless of whether irrigation is possible; that is valid because the lease is not specifically for agriculture. The passage also covers two special cases: leasing land to make bricks (which is invalid because it consumes the soil—the tenant must compensate for the soil's value if it has value, and pay for any decrease), and leasing land occupied by another's crop (if the crop is there by right, the lease must be for a future term after harvest; if the crop is unlawful, the lease is valid and the crop must be uprooted). Finally, a house occupied by non-tenant's goods can be leased, and the term starts when handed over empty. A cultivated field leased and later delivered after harvest becomes valid.

Key Terms
جهالة (jahalah): Ignorance or uncertainty about the essential terms of the contract (here, the crop type), making the lease invalid.
استحسان (istihsan): Juristic preference that validates a contract despite initial uncertainty once the subject matter becomes known through use.
مقيلاً ومراحاً (maqilan wa marahan): For midday rest and shelter; examples of using land for purposes other than agriculture, building, or planting.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If someone rents land without specifying a crop and without giving the tenant discretion, then the tenant sows wheat, what is the ruling by istihsan?
A) The lease is void and no rent is due.
B) The lease becomes valid and the named rent is due.
C) The lease is void but the tenant must pay rent for the crop.
D) The lease is valid only if the lessor agrees after sowing.

Key Takeaway
An agricultural lease without specification is invalid due to jahalah, but istihsan validates it once the crop is actually sown, preventing waste and dispute.

Land Lease Without Crop Specification: Qiyas vs Istihsan
Defines conditions for valid lease of land for cultivation and rectification via istihsan

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rule of istihsan to a land lease contract that initially lacks crop specification and determine the valid rental obligation.

Core Idea
Ignorance voids a lease initially, but actual use makes it valid through istihsan.

In Hanafi fiqh, a lease of land for cultivation requires the crop to be known or the lessee given freedom to plant. If neither is done, the contract is void due to uncertainty. However, the school employs istihsan to salvage the contract once the lessee actually uses the land, drawing an analogy to hiring a garment without specifying the wearer. This lesson unpacks the reasoning and conditions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the initial defect
The contract lacks specification of the crop, leading to jahalah (ignorance) about the benefit. In Hanafi law, this makes the contract fasid (invalid) from the start.
Jahalah here means the benefit is unknown at contract formation.
2
Apply strict analogy (qiyas)
Under qiyas, the contract remains invalid even after planting, because the defect existed at the time of contracting.
This follows the principle that a fasid contract cannot be corrected by later events.
3
Apply istihsan (juristic preference)
The Hanafi school departs from qiyas using istihsan, ruling that once the lessee plants, the benefit becomes known and the contract becomes valid (sahih). The lessee must pay the named rental.
The basis is preventing hardship and giving effect to transactions.
4
Understand the analogy
The case is analogized to hiring a garment without specifying the wearer. If the hirer then uses it to clothe someone, the contract becomes valid in istihsan because the benefit is realized.
The common illa (effective cause) is that the uncertain benefit becomes certain through actual use.
5
Recognize the final ruling
The mufta bihi (operative opinion) is the istihsan ruling: the lease becomes valid upon planting, and the agreed rent is due. This applies even if only part of the land is usable, with proportional rent adjustment.
This ruling is from the zahir al-riwayah and is the relied-upon position.

كتاب الإجارة باب ما يجوز من الإجارة وما يكون خلافاً فيها مسألة لأن منفعة الأرض مختلفة باختلاف ما يزرع فيها لأنه منه ما ينفع كالبرسيم في ديارنا وما يضر كالقمح مثلاً فلا بد من بيانه أو يقول له ازرع فيها ما شئت كي لا يفضي إلى المنازعة. ولو لم يبين ولم يقل له ازرع فيها ما شئت فسدت الإجارة للجهالة ولو زرعها لا تعود صحيحة في القياس، وفي الاستحسان يجب المسمى وتنقلب صحيحة لأن المعقود صار صحيحاً معلوماً بالاستعمال، وصار كما لو استأجر ثوباً ولم يبين اللابس ثم ألبس إنساناً عادت صحيحة لما ذكرنا. وفي القنية: استأجر أرضاً سنة على أن يزرع فيها ما شاء فله أن يزرع فيها زرعين ربيعياً وخريفياً. وفي الجوهرة ولا بأس باستئجار الأرض للزراعة قبل ريها إن كانت معتادة للري في مثل هذه المدة التي عقد الإجارة عليها، وإن جاء من الماء ما يزرع به البعض فالمستأجر بالخيار إن شاء نقض الإجارة كلها، وإن شاء لم ينقض وكان عليه من الأجر بحساب ما روي منها .اهـ. وفي القنية : ولو استأجرها ولا يمكنه الزراعة في الحال لاحتياجها إلى السقي وكري الأنهار أو مجيء الماء، فإن كان بحال تمكنه الزراعة في مدة العقد جاز وإلا فلا كما لو استأجرها في الشتاء تسعة أشهر ويمكن زراعتها في الشتاء جاز لما أمكن من المدة، أما إذا لم يمكن الانتفاع بها أصلاً بأن كانت سبخة فالإجارة فاسدة، وفي الاستئجار في الشتاء يكون الأجر مقابلاً بكل المدة لا بما ينتفع به فحسب، وقيل بما ينتفع به اهـ.
Book of Ijarah. Chapter on what is permissible in Ijarah and what is disputed in it. Issue: Because the benefit of land varies with what is planted in it, since some crops are beneficial like alfalfa in our regions and some are harmful like wheat for example, so it is necessary to specify it or say to him: 'Plant whatever you wish' to avoid dispute. If he did not specify and did not say to him 'Plant whatever you wish', the ijarah becomes void due to ignorance (jahalah). If he did plant it, it does not become valid in qiyas. But in istihsan, the named rental is due and it becomes valid because the contracted benefit became known through use, and it is like if someone hired a garment without specifying the wearer and then dressed a person, it becomes valid due to what we mentioned. In al-Qunyah: He hired land for a year on the condition that he plants whatever he wishes, he may plant two crops, spring and autumn. In al-Jawharah: There is no harm in hiring land for cultivation before its irrigation if it is accustomed to irrigation within the period of the ijarah. If water comes to irrigate only part, the lessee has the option to cancel the whole ijarah or not cancel, and then he must pay rent in proportion to what was irrigated. End quote. In al-Qunyah: If he hired it and cannot cultivate immediately due to need for watering, digging canals, or waiting for water, then if cultivation is possible within the contract period, it is permissible; otherwise not, like if he hired it in winter for nine months and cultivation in winter is possible, it is permissible due to possibility in the period. As for if no benefit is possible at all, like if it is saline land, the ijarah is void. In hiring in winter, the rent is for the entire period, not just what is benefited from, and it is said it is for what is benefited from. End quote.
Source pages p. 18

Commentary
This passage deals with the rules of leasing agricultural land. The author begins by noting that the benefit of land varies with the crop, so the crop must be specified or the lessee must be given general permission to plant anything. If neither is done, the contract is void due to ignorance (jahalah). However, if the lessee actually plants without specification, in strict analogy (qiyas) the contract does not become valid, but the Hanafi school applies istihsan (juristic preference) and rules that the contract becomes valid and the specified rent must be paid. This is because the benefit became known through actual use, analogized to hiring a garment for an unspecified person and then using it. The passage further discusses various scenarios: hiring by year with freedom to plant seasons, hiring before irrigation, inability to cultivate, and the distribution of rent. A key point is that the Hanafi school prioritizes actual benefit over initial specification.

Key Terms
إجارة (ijarah): A lease contract for benefit in exchange for rent
استحسان (istihsan): A juristic preference departing from strict analogy to achieve a more suitable result
جهالة (jahalah): Ignorance or uncertainty in the subject matter of a contract leading to invalidity

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the Hanafi ruling if someone leases land for cultivation without specifying the crop and without saying 'plant whatever you wish'?
A) The lease is void and cannot become valid even after planting.
B) The lease is valid from the start because the benefit is understood.
C) In qiyas the lease does not become valid, but in istihsan it becomes valid upon planting.
D) The lease is valid if the lessee plants a crop that is customary in the region.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi law, a land lease without crop specification is initially fasid, but becomes valid upon planting through istihsan, overriding strict analogy.
